- S3 — Variance-swap-style short via strip of options (replicate DVOL): Approximate a 30d variance swap by selling a CBOE-style strip and delta-hedging, capturing the +14-pt median premium directly. Most data-intensive; cost drag from many strikes' bid-ask — use only the liquid central strikes.
- S4 — Vol-targeted, regime-gated overlay (the version that actually nets positive): Apply EVaR/vol-target sizing to S1/S2 to a fixed ann. vol (e.g., 10-15%), only sell when DVOL term structure in contango AND DVOL>RV, cut size on funding/OI spikes. Liberty Road's only profitable live product (+9.90%/yr, SR 1.76 net of 2/20) was exactly this; passive selling lost ~10%/yr.
- S5 — Calendar/term-structure short-vol: Sell front-week, partially offset by longer-dated, to harvest the steep front-end contango while capping tail. Cuts the catastrophic short-gamma exposure that blew up naive sellers in Mar-2020/Jun-2022/Nov-2022 at the cost of premium.
- S6 — Tail hedge / event filter: Pair any short-vol book with cheap far-OTM puts or stand aside 7 days before known catalysts (FOMC/CPI/large expiries); Deribit's event-driven long-vol pre-CPI/FOMC was positive but small-N. Drag = hedge premium, but converts negative-skew payoff to survivable.
- S7 — Equity benchmark (free, our data): Run CBOE-PUT-style 25-delta short put/strangle on SPY/QQQ from our S&P 500 bars + free VIX data as a control to size how much of crypto VRP is genuine excess vs vol-beta.

### Pitfalls
- Sign-convention confusion: academics report VRP = RN_var - phys_var as a NEGATIVE number for the BUYER (Carr-Wu, Bakshi-Kapadia, Atanasova 'consistently negative') while practitioners quote IV-RV as POSITIVE (+14 pts). Both mean 'sellers earn the premium.' Mislabeling will invert a backtest's sign — define it explicitly.
- Negative-skew / peso problem: short-vol prints steady small gains then catastrophic losses (put-sellers historically -800% in tails; crypto blew up Mar-2020, May-2021, Jun-2022, Nov-2022). Sharpe massively overstates risk-adjusted value; report MaxDD, CVaR, skew, and Sortino, and use the Deflated/Probabilistic Sharpe (Bailey-Lopez de Prado) given many tested rolls/strikes.
- Cost underestimation: option bid-ask in crypto is WIDE (Almeida et al. note crypto IV-surface spreads are 'significantly wider' than equities) and the delta-hedge on perps incurs fees + funding + slippage every 2.5% move. Naive backtests using mid-prices and ignoring hedge costs will show 2-3x the achievable Sharpe. Deribit fee is 0.03% of UNDERLYING (not premium), which is brutal on cheap OTM options (capped at 12.5% of premium).
- Decay / institutionalization: this is the headline risk. Crypto carry Sharpe went 6.45->4.06->negative (2020->2024->2025); equity VRP alpha went to ~zero post-2010; ETF + IBIT-options convergence is compressing IV (to ~32%) and skew (gap 15.3->0.2 pts in 2025). Backtests on 2019-2022 data are the EASY regime; weight 2024-2026 heavily and assume continued compression.
- Regime-fitting / data-snooping: Deribit's own optimal allocations (90% straddle, 75-80% RR) are in-sample and chosen ex-post; the 'best' delta/tenor/hedge-band is overfit. Strict walk-forward (train 2021-2023, test 2024-2026), few parameters, and pre-registered rules are essential. ~23 strikes x tenors x hedge-bands = a multiple-testing minefield.
- Short sample & survivorship: usable Deribit option/DVOL history is only ~2019-2026 (DVOL from Apr-2021), spanning few independent vol cycles; Deribit dominates (~80-90%) so there is exchange concentration/counterparty risk, and historical L2/order-book is NOT available via the public API (only current book + trades), limiting realistic spread/impact modeling. Funding-history backbone (perps) starts 2024-02 in our data — shorter than the option surfaces.
- ETH/BTC and weekend microstructure: ETH VRP can be negative when BTC's is positive (early-2025); 24/7 trading + thin weekends create vol gaps not in equity VIX intuition. Don't pool BTC+ETH or assume weekday vol dynamics.
- Liquidation/feedback loops (BIS): a 10% rise in standardized carry predicts +22% of OI in short-futures liquidations next month — funding-driven cascades hit short-vol books precisely when hedging is hardest; model the joint funding-vol tail, not vol alone.

### Data needed
- HAVE: Deribit BTC/ETH IV surfaces + DVOL index 2021-2026 (core for H1-H7); 228 perps x ~23k hrs funding (H6, hedge-cost modeling); Coinalyze funding/OI/liquidations (H6, tail/feedback); top-50 OHLCV 1h/4h/1d 2024-02->2026-06 (realized-vol estimation: close-to-close + Garman-Klass/Parkinson on intraday).
- NEED (free, to make backtests realistic): Deribit public REST/WS for (a) historical option TRADES and per-instrument best-bid/ask to estimate true execution spreads — public API gives current order book + trade history but NOT historical L2 snapshots, so capture forward live and use Tardis.dev free tier / CryptoDataDownload free DVOL OHLC + per-contract trades as a proxy; (b) Deribit fee schedule (0.03% of underlying, 12.5%-of-premium cap, combo discount) hard-coded into cost model.
- NEED (free benchmark): VIX + VIX term structure (Cboe website / FRED 'VIXCLS'), CBOE PUT/PUTW/BXM index levels (Cboe) and SPX option chains (Cboe DataShop sample / free delayed) to run the equity-VRP control (H8) on our existing S&P 500 bars.
- NEED (free, cross-asset cousins requested): FX VRP — use FX option-implied vol from free sources (e.g., Fed H.10/H.15 for rate differentials; CME FX options settlements; investing.com / Yahoo for spot+forwards) to test whether crypto VRP is just a high-beta vol premium. Commodities — CME/Barchart free futures term structure + CME options settlements for a commodity VRP benchmark.
- NEED (validation): a clean BTC realized-variance series at multiple sampling frequencies (5m/1h) to construct an honest model-free variance-swap fixing matching DVOL's CBOE methodology; and an event calendar (FOMC/CPI/large-expiry dates) for the event-filter overlay (S6).
- NICE-TO-HAVE: IBIT/listed BTC-ETF option implied vols (free via Yahoo/CBOE delayed) to directly measure the TradFi-vs-Deribit VRP convergence (cross-check the decay finding) and to test cross-venue vol arbitrage.

### Adversarial verification — reliability: **medium**
_Net-of-cost reality:_ Blunt take: the crypto VRP is REAL and genuinely large gross (BVRP~14%, ~7x equities; 0.24%/day delta-hedged returns) — those headline numbers check out at the primary-source level. But almost nothing about the costs/tails is favorable, and the most recent data is actively hostile. (1) Costs are brutal and asymmetric to sellers: round-trip option bid-ask runs 20-40% of premium, Deribit's fee is 0.03% of UNDERLYING (capped 12.5% of premium — punishing on cheap OTM), and the perp delta-hedge bleeds fees+funding+slippage every move; the academic 0.24%/day is explicitly compensation for bearing illiquidity/hedging-cost risk (market makers are net-LONG), i.e. the upper bound, not the achievable net. (2) The premium is decaying fast and the decay is now empirical, not speculative: crypto carry Sharpe collapsed 6.45->4.06->NEGATIVE in 2025 (Borri 2026, verbatim), TradFi/crypto skew converged from 15.3 pts to <0.2 pts in Q3-2025, ATM IV tracks across venues, and the equity-VRP template went to ~zero alpha post-2010 (Dew-Becker-Giglio). (3) The tail risk is not hypothetical and the worst of it is NEWER than the cited research: a ~$19B Oct-10-12-2025 liquidation cascade, BTC -31% into November, a ~50% peak-to-trough drawdown bottoming Jan-Feb-2026 with put IV ~95% and the most put-skewed risk-reversal since 2022 — exactly the short-gamma regime that wipes naive sellers, and exactly the funding-driven liquidation cascade BIS quantified (10% carry rise -> 22% of OI liquidated next month). Net: this survives only as an actively risk-managed, vol-targeted, regime-gated, tail-hedged book on the LIQUID central strikes — and even that is shrinking. Passive short-vol/covered-call selling is a net money-loser. Backtests on the 2019-2022 (or even -2024) easy regime materially overstate what is harvestable in 2025-2026; weight the post-ETF, post-crash data heavily and assume continued compression.
- **[CONFIRMED]** BTC variance risk premium is large and same-signed as equities (IV>RV, short side earns it): annualized variance-swap VRP ~14% (risk-neutral var 0.72 vs physical 0.58), ~7x the S&P's ~2%; return premium ~66%/yr, BTC standalone Sharpe ~0.8 (~2x S&P's 0.5). — Primary-source confirmed from Almeida, Grith, Miftachov & Wang (arXiv:2410.15195v2, Aug-2025 revision), read directly: for a one-month horizon 'the BP averages 66% per annum, while the BVRP averages 14%, both of which are significantly higher than the premia of traditional assets'; S&P EP lower bound 5% (Martin 2017), Bollerslev-Tauchen-Zhou 2009 give 2% S&P VRP; BTC Sharpe 'approximately 0.8, which is nearly twice that of the S&P 500' (SR~0.5). The 14% BVRP and 7x-vs-equities framing are correct. TWO caveats lower confidence on the exact framing: (a) the specific '0.72 vs 0.58' risk-neutral-vs-physical variance decomposition does NOT appear in the paper's abstract/intro — the paper reports BVRP=14% directly, so that sub-number is an unverified reconstruction; (b) the sample is Jul-2017 to Dec-2022 only, so this paper does NOT establish persistence into the 2024-2026 ETF era (other papers do, but the level has since compressed — see decay verdict). The directional/magnitude claim is solid; treat the 0.72/0.58 split and any post-2022 persistence as not established by this citation.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Delta-hedged crypto option returns are strongly positive to sellers and very large: average DAILY delta-hedged BTC option return ~0.24%; +1 SD option illiquidity adds ~0.07%/day (calls) and 0.06%/day (puts); hedging/rebalancing cost proxies explain ~60% of cross-sectional spread variation. — Primary-source confirmed from Atanasova, Miao, Segarra, Sha & Willeboordse, 'Illiquidity Premium and Crypto Option Returns' (SFU/ACFR), read directly. Sample Jan-2020–Jul-2024 (Deribit BTC). Exact quotes: 'one standard deviation increase in option illiquidity corresponds to an approximate 0.07% increase in the daily delta-hedged return for calls and 0.06% for puts. This is economically very large when compared to the daily average delta-hedged return of 0.24%'; 'proxies for hedging and rebalancing costs explain almost 60% of the spread variation'; illiquidity-premium alpha 0.17%/contract. CRITICAL adversarial nuance the findings correctly flagged: the paper's mechanism is that market makers hold NET-LONG positions and demand the illiquidity premium as compensation for hedging costs/risk — so 0.24%/day is a risk-bearing return measured AT TRANSACTION PRICES, NOT a frictionless arbitrage. A short-vol harvester capturing it must cross the very spreads the literature pegs at 20-40% of premium round-trip. So the gross number is real and large but is the upper bound, not the achievable net.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Crypto carry/VRP is decaying fast with institutionalization: crypto carry annualized Sharpe 6.45 (2020-25) -> 4.06 (from 2024) -> NEGATIVE in 2025; ETF (Jan-2024) + IBIT options (Nov-2024) converged TradFi/crypto markets, skew gap 15.3 pts (Jul-1-2025: IBIT 33.4 vs Deribit 18.1) -> <0.2 pts by Sep-2025; IBIT OI ~$53B vs Deribit ~$50B. — Strongly confirmed and arguably understated. Borri, Liu, Tsyvinski & Wu (arXiv:2510.14435v4, prepared for Annual Review of Financial Economics 2026), fetched directly: 'the annualized Sharpe ratio of the cryptocurrency carry is 6.45 ... Beginning in 2024, the Sharpe ratio falls to 4.06, and it turns negative in 2025' (sample Aug-2020–May-2025); funding-rate mean ~8% with 0.8% vol. The 6.45/4.06/negative sequence is verbatim. Schmeling-Schrimpf-Todorov 'Crypto carry' (BIS WP 1087, now Management Science) confirms carry up to ~60% p.a. and that ETF introduction 'significantly decreased crypto carry across exchanges by about three percentage points and by an additional five on the CME'. Convergence confirmed near-verbatim by the ETF Express writeup of the cross-venue study: skew gap peaked Jul-1 'with IBIT at 33.4 percent versus Deribit at 18.1 percent, closing to within 0.2 points by late September'; IBIT reached 'USD53.3 billion in peak open interest ... Deribit ... approached USD50 billion ahead of December 2025'; ATM IV 'tracked closely across both venues throughout 2025.' One reconciliation note: other late-2025 trade press reported the IBIT/Deribit OI crossover at the lower ~$27B level (different snapshot/metric) — both the $53B peak and the ~$27B crossover figures circulate; the convergence direction is not in doubt.
- **[CONFIRMED]** The equity VRP — the template for crypto — has itself decayed to ~zero alpha over the last ~15 years (break ~2010), consistent with synthetic options; previously sharply negative. — Confirmed from Dew-Becker & Giglio, 'The Decline of the Variance Risk Premium: Evidence from Traded and Synthetic Options' (Chicago Fed WP 2025-17, Sep-2025; SSRN 5525882). Authoritative source summaries state: equity index options 'historically displayed sharply negative returns and CAPM alphas,' but 'Over the past 15 years, option alphas have become indistinguishable from zero.' Synthetic options (dynamic replication) 'never had negative alpha over the last 100 years,' implying the historical premium was an option-market/intermediation friction, not a deep risk price; decline attributed to 'declining asymmetry in dealer portfolios and the hedging costs they face.' This is a strong, credible prior that crypto VRP compresses as intermediation deepens — and the crypto data (carry Sharpe collapse, TradFi/crypto convergence) is already tracking that template. (I could not open the primary PDF directly — Chicago Fed/author servers returned 403/404 — but two independent authoritative retrievals of the abstract agree on all figures, so confidence is high.)
- **[WEAKENED]** PASSIVE crypto vol-selling has historically LOST money; only actively risk-managed/vol-targeted selling produced positive net Sharpe (Liberty Road: passive covered calls -9.79%/yr, SR -0.54; only the EVaR vol-targeted 'Treasury' product +9.90%/yr, SR +1.76 net of 2/20). — Directionally confirmed, but the specific live numbers could not be independently re-verified and the supporting evidence is weak/promotional. Liberty Road Capital's own 2023 writeup and factsheets confirm the qualitative thesis (active beats passive; they run an EVaR/Extreme-Value-at-Risk product targeting ~5-7% vol with a 'targeted Sharpe of 2'; passive lost money), but I could not surface independent confirmation of the precise -9.79%/-0.54 and +9.90%/+1.76 figures — they trace to a single small-N, self-reported, fee-conflicted live track record (manager marketing its winning product). The broader, independent evidence nonetheless supports the DIRECTION strongly: passive BTC covered-call/income ETFs (YBTC, BTCI, BITO-CC, BlackRock's new income fund) carry 0.65-0.96% fees, structurally cap upside, and the cost literature (20-40% of premium round-trip spreads) makes naive harvesting a net loser. So 'passive loses, active-vol-targeted can net positive' is credible; the exact Liberty Road point estimates are not adversarially verified and should be treated as illustrative, not evidentiary.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Naive short-vol blew up in Mar-2020/May-2021/Jun-2022/Nov-2022 and the premium is regime-dependent (sellable in contango/positive-skew, dangerous in backwardation/vol-shocks); ETH VRP went NEGATIVE (realized>implied) in early-2025. — Confirmed and reinforced by fresh tail episodes that POST-DATE the findings, strengthening the bearish case. The regime-dependence and historic blowups are well documented (Deribit research; Alexander & Imeraj 2021 'VRP spikes before large +/- returns'). The early-2025 ETH episode is corroborated: Block Scholes / Deribit reporting shows BTC realized vol broke its floor while ETH realized ran far higher, the ETH/BTC IV ratio hit a ~5-year high (>2x short-dated) yet ETH implied under-priced ETH realized — i.e., ETH short-vol sellers were squeezed; some venues show short-call PnL stayed positive in select windows, so 'ETH VRP negative' is episode/tenor-specific, not a clean monthly sign-flip — hence the conditional framing is right. CRUCIALLY, the worst evidence is the newest: a major Oct-10-12-2025 crash liquidated ~$19B+ (one of crypto's largest), BTC fell ~31% (Oct->Nov 2025, $126k->$86k), and the selloff extended to a ~50% drawdown into a Jan-29-Feb-6-2026 acute phase ($90k->$60k) where 25-delta put IV hit ~95% and the risk-reversal hit -19.34 (most put-skewed since 2022); short-gamma sellers' losses were explicitly amplified. The peso/negative-skew problem is alive and recent.

---

## Volatility term structure and vol-of-vol  `vol_term_structure`

The volatility risk premium (VRP) — implied vol systematically exceeding realized — is one of the best-documented harvestable premia, and the VIX-futures term structure is its tradable expression: contango ~80% of the time drives a roll-yield that is a structural short-vol carry. But the GROSS Sharpe ratios advertised (1.5-3.0) collapse once realistic costs, borrow, leverage caps and especially tail risk are imposed: AQR's delta+beta-hedged short-vol strategy earns only ~1.5%/yr at 2.2% vol (Sharpe 0.68) at unit leverage net of costs, and naive short-VIX-futures/short-VXX strategies blew up -96% in a single day (Feb 2018 "Volmageddon"). The premium is real but is compensation for crash/skew risk, not a free lunch; the durable edge is in TIMING (Cheng's VIX-premium signal: cut short exposure when the ex-ante premium turns negative beats short-only) rather than static carry. Crypto shows the SAME structure but larger: BTC variance risk premium ~14%/yr vs ~2% for S&P, IV>RV ~70% of the time, DVOL term structure in contango ~77% of the time — but with even fatter tails (LUNA/FTX), higher transaction costs (Deribit 0.03%/side), and a critical regime inversion (crypto VRP is HIGHER in calm markets, opposite the equity intuition). Vol-of-vol (VVIX) carries its own premium and its slope/level predict tail-hedge and straddle returns, but trading it requires VIX options and is largely paper-only at retail scale.

### Findings

**The equity variance/volatility risk premium is large, persistent and economically significant: risk-neutral implied variance exceeds subsequent realized variance on average, so shorting variance swaps on broad indices earns high risk-adjusted returns. The premium is strongly NEGATIVE for index variance buyers (i.e. positive for sellers) and cannot be explained by CAPM beta or Fama-French factors.**
- Effect size: Carr-Wu (2009): annualized Sharpe of shorting S&P 500 variance swaps ~0.98 (S&P 100 ~0.85, Dow ~0.87, ~1.02 in some specs); VRP strongly negative for S&P500/100 & DJIA, smaller-magnitude negative for Nasdaq-100 and single names. Bollerslev-Tauchen-Zhou (2009): ~2% VRP for S&P 500 (in variance terms, ~30-day). In vol points the equity VRP is typically ~2-4 vol pts on average, widening to 10-20+ in stress.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Foundational result (sample to ~2003) but repeatedly confirmed post-2018; AQR (2018) re-documents it 1996-2016 and notes it persists even in low-vol regimes (IV > RV even when vol is 'cheap'). Survives in crypto (see below). The premium itself has NOT disappeared, though the easy levered expression has.
- Cites: Carr & Wu 2009, 'Variance Risk Premiums', Review of Financial Studies 22(3) (NYU/Baruch working-paper version, May 2004); Bollerslev, Tauchen & Zhou 2009, 'Expected Stock Returns and Variance Risk Premia', RFS; AQR (Ang, Israelov, Sullivan, Tummala) 2018, 'Understanding the Volatility Risk Premium'

**Harvesting the VRP via a properly delta-hedged AND beta-hedged short-options strategy produces a positive but MODEST net-of-cost Sharpe with low equity correlation in normal times — but its worst losses cluster in sudden large market moves (up OR down), confirming it is crash/convexity-risk compensation, not free alpha. At unit leverage the raw return is tiny, which is precisely why practitioners lever it and thereby manufacture blow-up risk.**
- Effect size: AQR 2018 (S&P 500, sell 5% OTM monthly put, unit leverage, delta-hedged daily, NET of transaction costs, 1996-2016): annualized return 1.5%, vol 2.2%, Sharpe 0.68, max drawdown -10%, beta to S&P 0.04, full-period correlation to S&P 0.07. Worst months: Mar 2000 and Sep 2008 (S&P +/-~10%). Buying protection (the other side) is expensive: S&P+protective-put had Sharpe 0.14 vs 0.32 for S&P alone, return cut from 5.1% to 1.8%.
- Strength: strong · Recency: 1996-2016 net-of-cost. Post-2018 the unlevered premium persists, but Feb-2018 and Mar-2020 are out-of-sample tail events that confirm the convexity warning. The Sharpe is NOT robust to leverage: levering 0.68 Sharpe / 2.2% vol up to ~15% vol restores headline returns but reintroduces -50%+ tail drawdowns.
- Cites: AQR 2018, 'Understanding the Volatility Risk Premium' (Exhibits 3,4,5,6); Israelov & Nielsen 2015 (protective-put path-dependency); Israelov 2017 (put protection)

**VIX futures trade in contango the large majority of the time, so a static short-VIX-futures / short-VXX / long-SVXY 'roll-yield' position earns a structural carry. This is the engine behind both the high gross Sharpe figures and the catastrophic tail. Long-vol ETPs (VXX/VIXY) bleed structurally; short-vol products harvest that bleed but with unbounded crash exposure.**
- Effect size: VIX futures in contango ~80-84% of the time. VXX roll cost ~5%/month in normal contango (8-10% in steep contango, 1-2% in flat) → compounds to roughly -46% to -55%/yr; VXX is down >99% since 2009 inception. Pre-cost / pre-crash short-VIX strategies show eye-catching gross Sharpes: one cited VIX-futures strategy earned Sharpe ~3.0 over Mar-2004 to Dec-2018, and short-VIXY/long-VIXM term-structure trades show gross Sharpe 1.79-1.94 (2019-2025) — all GROSS, before borrow/slippage and ignoring tail.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Gross numbers are robust pre-cost but the realized net experience post-2018 is far worse. After Feb-2018, SVXY was permanently cut from -1.0x to -0.5x leverage, structurally halving the harvestable carry and the realized Sharpe; a 'move-to-cash-when-curve-inverts' short-vol rule delivered only ~0.36 Sharpe in some post-period samples vs the ~3.0 headline.
- Cites: sixfigureinvesting.com 'The Cost of Contango'; Quantpedia 'Exploiting Term Structure of VIX Futures'; Valuelytica 'Volatility Term Structure Arbitrage' (short VIXY/long VIXM, 2019-2025, gross); ProShares SVXY prospectus (leverage change to -0.5x)

**The single most catastrophic, well-documented tail event for static short-vol: the Feb 5 2018 'Volmageddon'. End-of-day rebalancing of the inverse/leveraged VIX-ETP complex created a mechanical feedback loop — these products MUST buy VIX futures into the close in proportion to the day's move — that amplified the VIX spike and destroyed the products. This is an endogenous, structural tail unique to leveraged vol-ETPs, not a generic market risk.**
- Effect size: Short/leveraged vol ETP complex ~$5bn AUM (Jan 2018). On Feb 5 the underlying short-term VIX-futures index was up ~20% by 3:25pm, requiring ~$800m of VIX futures to be bought at the 4:15pm close; ~$4bn of the two front VIX futures traded that day. VIX +116% (largest % move ever) on an S&P move of only ~-4.1%. XIV -96% to -97%, SVXY -91%, VMIN -87%; XIV was terminated (Credit Suisse acceleration event at <20% of prior NAV).
- Strength: strong · Recency: Feb 2018 — the defining post-2018 event for this area. A near-repeat risk persists because the leveraged-ETP rebalancing mechanic still exists (SVXY -0.5x, SVIX, UVXY, etc.); any single-day VIX-futures move large enough re-triggers it.
- Cites: sixfigureinvesting.com 'What Caused the February 5th 2018 Volatility Spike / XIV Termination'; Bloomberg 2019 'The Day the VIX Doubled'; Credit Suisse XIV acceleration disclosure

**Term-structure TIMING beats static carry. The ex-ante VIX premium (risk-neutral minus a physical forecast of future VIX) predicts ex-post VIX-futures returns with a coefficient near one, and — counterintuitively — FALLS or turns negative precisely when risk rises ('low premium-response puzzle'), because volatility-hedging demand collapses in stress. A short-VIX-futures investor who CUTS exposure when the estimated premium goes negative earns higher Sharpe and alpha than short-only.**
- Effect size: Cheng (2019): VIX premium predicts ex-post monthly VIX-futures excess returns with slope 0.92 (SE 0.29), sample 2004-2015; robust across forecast models, to excluding the GFC, and at daily/weekly/monthly frequencies. Simon-Campasano (2013) basis rule (short front VIX future when daily roll >0.10 pts, hedged with ES): ~19.67% indicative annual return 2007-2011 — but explicitly 'slightly negative' and deteriorating out-of-sample.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Cheng's sample ends 2015; the mechanism (hedging-demand-driven premium that vanishes in stress) is structural and consistent with the 2018/2020 episodes. Simon-Campasano-style mechanical basis rules degrade out of sample — a clear decay/snooping warning. The conditional 'turn off in backwardation' overlay is the part most likely to survive.
- Cites: Cheng 2019, 'The VIX Premium', Review of Financial Studies (Dartmouth working paper, May 2018; subsumes 'The Expected Returns to Fear'); Simon & Campasano 2013, 'The VIX Futures Basis: Evidence and Trading Strategies', Journal of Derivatives; Johnson 2017, 'Equity Risk Premia and the VIX Term Structure' (VIX slope as priced PC)

**VIX futures are persistently slightly CHEAP relative to a no-arbitrage model price built from the VIX options surface (a 'law of one price' violation), and cheapen further when the VIX rises — a genuine but very small relative-value harvest, dominated by transaction costs at retail scale.**
- Effect size: Van Tassel (NY Fed): VIX futures are ~0.50 vol points cheaper than option-implied model prices on average, widening when VIX rises. Term premia for realized variance vs implied volatility move in opposite directions with systematic risk (realized-variance term premium rises, implied-vol term premium declines) and each predicts variance-swap vs VIX-futures returns respectively.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: NY Fed Staff Reports SR867 (2018) and SR953 (2020/Law of One Price), recent. The ~0.5 vol-pt edge is too small to harvest net of VIX-options bid/ask for most; it is more a model-validation result than a standalone alpha.
- Cites: Van Tassel 2018, 'Equity Volatility Term Premia', FRBNY Staff Report 867 (SSRN 3259918); Van Tassel 2020, 'The Law of One Price in Equity Volatility Markets', FRBNY Staff Report 953

**Vol-of-vol (VVIX) carries its own risk premium, and both the LEVEL and the SLOPE of the VVIX term structure have predictive power for option/straddle and tail-hedge returns incremental to the VIX term structure and the VRP. High VVIX = tail hedges are richly priced = sell-them signal with subsequent low returns.**
- Effect size: Park (2013/2015, FRB): a 1-SD rise in VVIX predicts a 1.63%-2.19% LOWER next-day S&P 500 put return and 0.68%-0.87% lower next-day VIX-call return (predictability over ~3-4 weeks), robust to jump risk, skew, kurtosis, liquidity, VRP. Branger-Hulsbusch-Kraftschik (2017): a long/short strategy on the VVIX term-structure slope earned gross Sharpe 1.50 on 1-month S&P straddles (vs 1.20 short-only) and 1.09 on 12-month (vs 0.30), Sep-2007 to Aug-2014; the VVIX slope's predictive power is incremental to the VIX slope (Sharpe 0.98/0.51) and the VRP.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Samples end 2014; no post-2018 net-of-cost replication found. Authors explicitly concede daily long/short switching + monthly straddle reformation 'would reduce reported Sharpe ratios' and give NO net figures — treat as gross/paper-only until verified. Direction (high VVIX → sell vol/tail hedges) is economically sensible and likely persists in sign.
- Cites: Park 2015, 'Volatility-of-volatility and tail risk hedging returns', Journal of Financial Markets (FRB FEDS 2013-54, Aug 2013); Branger, Hulsbusch & Kraftschik 2017, 'The Volatility-of-Volatility Term Structure'; Chow et al., 'VIX Decomposition... Price of Fear and Stock Return Predictability'

**Crypto shows the SAME volatility-premium structure as equities but LARGER, and with a crucial regime twist: the Bitcoin variance risk premium is several times the equity VRP, IV exceeds RV the majority of the time, and the DVOL/options term structure is usually in contango — but the BTC VRP is HIGHER in calm/low-vol regimes (opposite to the equity intuition that VRP spikes in stress), reflecting demand for upside as well as downside protection.**
- Effect size: Almeida, Grith, Miftachov & Wang (2025, Deribit data): BTC variance risk premium (BVRP) averages ~14%/yr at 1-month horizon vs ~2% for S&P 500 (Bollerslev-Tauchen-Zhou); BTC return premium ~66%/yr; BTC unconditional Sharpe ~0.8 (~2x S&P). BVRP is HIGHER in the low-vol regime and LOWER in high-vol states; negative relationship between BTC price and BTC VRP. Deribit research: 30-day BTC IV > 30-day RV ~70% of the time since Apr-2019; mean VRP ~+15 vol points when term structure in contango; DVOL/term structure in contango ~77.5% of the time; backwardation episodes are short (~85h mean) but spike hard (backwardation ratio peaked ~1.45 in Mar-2020/May-2021/Jun-2022/Nov-2022).
- Strength: moderate · Recency: 2019-2025, directly on Deribit — the most relevant and current crypto evidence. Confirmed across Alexander & Imeraj (2021) 'Bitcoin VIX and its VRP' and Du (2025) on crypto vol-of-vol. The low-vol-regime-high-VRP finding is a distinctive, testable crypto feature.
- Cites: Almeida, Grith, Miftachov & Wang 2025, 'Risk Premia in the Bitcoin Market', arXiv:2410.15195; Alexander & Imeraj 2021, 'The Bitcoin VIX and Its Variance Risk Premium'; Deribit Insights 2023, 'Bitcoin Options: Finding edge in four years of volatility regimes'; Du 2025, 'Pricing Cryptocurrency Options With Volatility of Volatility', J. Futures Markets

**Systematic short-volatility in crypto (delta-hedged short straddles/strangles on Deribit) earns the VRP but with severe path dependency and crash exposure; weekly tenors are favored over monthly, and short risk-reversals exploit the persistently negative spot-vol correlation. Net returns are real but transaction costs and crash gaps are first-order.**
- Effect size: Deribit research (Apr-2019 to Dec-2022): weekly short straddle delivered strong risk-adjusted returns through multiple crashes; optimal mix ~90% weekly-straddle + 10% spot BTC (monthly straddle saturated at only ~30% allocation before Sharpe declined). Short risk-reversal systematically outperformed long (negative spot-vol correlation ~65% of the time). Deribit fees: 0.03% of underlying per side for BTC/ETH options, CAPPED at 12.5% of the option premium; futures bid/ask ~$1-2/BTC. Crash context: ~$450bn vanished in the May-2022 LUNA collapse, ~$200bn after Nov-2022 FTX; ETH 7-day IV jumped to ~98% annualized in the FTX week.
- Strength: weak · Recency: Practitioner backtest 2019-2022; gross-of-some-costs and survivorship/regime-dependent. No peer-reviewed net-of-cost crypto short-vol Sharpe found. The 12.5%-of-premium fee cap matters most for cheap OTM options where the % fee would otherwise be punitive.
- Cites: Deribit Insights 2023, 'Bitcoin Options: Finding edge in four years of volatility regimes'; Deribit fee schedule (0.03%/side, 12.5%-of-premium cap); Quant Buffet 2024, 'Delta Hedged Short Straddle BTC Strategy'; Carol Alexander et al. 2023, 'Delta hedging bitcoin options with a smile', Quantitative Finance 23(5)

### Testable hypotheses
- H1 (crypto VRP harvest): On Deribit BTC/ETH IV surfaces + DVOL (2021-2026), a daily-rebalanced delta-hedged short 1-week ATM straddle earns positive net returns after 0.03%/side fees (12.5%-premium cap) + realistic spread, with Sharpe materially above buy-and-hold BTC — but with max drawdowns concentrated in identifiable backwardation/jump windows. Falsified if net Sharpe <= 0 or if a single crash (e.g. the Aug-2024 yen-carry unwind) erases >1 year of carry.
- H2 (DVOL term-structure timing): The DVOL-vs-realized-vol gap and the front-vs-back implied-vol slope (or DVOL futures basis, 2023-2026) positively predict next-7-day short-straddle PnL; conditioning the short-vol position on 'contango only, flat to cash in backwardation' raises net Sharpe and cuts max drawdown vs always-short. This is the crypto analogue of Cheng's VIX-premium timing. Falsified if the conditional overlay does not improve drawdown-adjusted returns out-of-sample.
- H3 (crypto regime inversion): Replicate Almeida et al. — estimate the BTC VRP (DVOL^2 minus realized variance) and test whether it is HIGHER in low-realized-vol regimes than in high-vol regimes (opposite to equities). If true, a 'sell more vol when calm, less when stressed' rule (the reverse of equity intuition) should dominate in crypto. Directly testable on Deribit DVOL + OHLCV realized vol.
- H4 (perp funding as a vol/term-structure signal): Using 228 perps x ~23k hours of funding-rate history + Coinalyze OI/liquidations, test whether extreme funding and OI build-ups predict imminent backwardation/vol spikes in DVOL, giving an early-warning 'reduce short-vol' signal. Falsified if funding/OI extremes have no incremental predictive power for next-day DVOL changes beyond DVOL's own autocorrelation.
- H5 (equity term-structure timing on our data): On S&P 500 daily bars + sourced VIX/VIX-futures (free CBOE/FRED), reconstruct VIX-futures roll yield and a Cheng-style ex-ante premium; test that a 'short front VIX-future / short VXX only when curve in contango, flat in backwardation' rule beats always-short on net Sharpe AND on max drawdown 2010-2026. Falsified if the conditional rule's out-of-sample Sharpe is statistically indistinguishable from always-short after costs.
- H6 (VVIX as a sell-tail-hedge signal): With sourced VVIX (free CBOE), test Park's result out-of-sample 2018-2026 — does a high VVIX level predict LOW subsequent returns to S&P 500 OTM puts / VIX calls? Even if we cannot trade VIX options, a high-VVIX reading should predict richness of SPY puts in our SPY LOB/options data, usable as a 'don't buy / consider selling protection' filter.
- H7 (vol-of-vol in crypto): Construct a crypto 'VVIX' from the realized variance of DVOL (or from the cross-section of DVOL-implied vol) and test whether its level predicts subsequent BTC/ETH straddle and tail-option returns (crypto analogue of Park 2015). Falsified if DVOL-of-DVOL has no predictive power for next-month option returns.
- H8 (cross-asset VRP correlation / diversification): Test whether the equity short-vol PnL and the crypto short-vol PnL are correlated in tails (do they both blow up together, e.g. Mar-2020 COVID) or are genuinely diversifying. If tails are uncorrelated, a combined book has a much higher tail-adjusted Sharpe; if correlated, the 'diversification' is illusory exactly when it matters.

### Harvest strategies
- Crypto delta-hedged short straddle (PRIMARY, most testable on our data): systematically sell 1-week ATM BTC/ETH straddles on Deribit, delta-hedge daily with perps. Cost drag: 0.03% of underlying per option leg per side (capped at 12.5% of premium) entry+exit ≈ 0.06% notional round-trip per leg, plus perp-hedge funding (use our funding-rate data to net this), plus ~$1-2/BTC futures spread. Size weekly tenor ~70-90% of risk budget per Deribit research; keep dry powder for backwardation re-entry.
- Conditional (timed) crypto short-vol overlay: run the short-straddle ONLY when DVOL term structure is in contango and DVOL > trailing realized vol; flatten to spot/cash when the front-month inverts (backwardation) — the crypto analogue of Cheng's 'cut short exposure when premium turns negative'. This directly targets cutting the LUNA/FTX/Aug-2024-style tail rather than the carry.
- Crypto short risk-reversal: sell OTM call / buy OTM put financed structure (or vice-versa) to monetize the persistently negative spot-vol correlation and the skew premium; lower vega than straddle, captures skew richness. Cost: two legs of 0.03%/side; skew can gap violently in crashes so size small.
- Equity term-structure timed short-vol (needs sourced VIX-futures data): short front-month VIX future (or short VXX/long SVXY) ONLY in contango with a roll-yield threshold (Simon-Campasano-style), beta-hedge with ES/SPY, and FLATTEN in backwardation. Cost drag: VIX-futures commissions are small but slippage + ETP expense ratios (~0.85-1.3%/yr) + short-borrow on VXX (can be high/variable) + the structural -0.5x leverage cap on SVXY post-2018. Never run un-hedged or un-timed — that is the XIV trade.
- Long-vol tail hedge financed by VVIX timing (defensive, not pure harvest): only BUY S&P/SPY puts or VIX calls when VVIX is LOW (cheap tail insurance per Park); avoid buying when VVIX is high. Conversely treat high VVIX as a 'protection is rich' signal. Practical at our scale as a FILTER on protection cost rather than a standalone VVIX trade.
- Calendar/term-structure relative value (low tail): instead of outright short vol, trade the SLOPE — short front, long back (short VIXY / long VIXM in equities; near-vs-far DVOL futures in crypto) to isolate roll decay while muting the level/jump exposure. Reduces but does not eliminate tail (beta convexity in crashes); requires a DYNAMIC hedge ratio, not the constant 2.0 used in naive backtests.
- Cross-asset combination: run equity-VRP and crypto-VRP short-vol sleeves together ONLY if H8 shows their tails are uncorrelated; size each so the COMBINED 1-day stress loss (e.g. simultaneous +100% vol spike) is within risk budget. The diversification, if real, is the main way to push a ~0.7 standalone Sharpe toward a respectable tail-adjusted figure.

### Pitfalls
- Tail-risk masking / negative skew: short-vol PnL looks like a smooth ~0.7-2.0 Sharpe for years then loses 50-100% in days. Sharpe/vol are the WRONG metrics — they understate risk because the return distribution is severely left-skewed and fat-tailed. Always report max drawdown, worst single-day, CVaR, and stress-scenario PnL (e.g. instantaneous VIX +20 / DVOL +60). Feb-2018 (-96% XIV) and Mar-2020 are the reference disasters.
- Leverage illusion: the unlevered VRP Sharpe (~0.68, AQR) corresponds to a TINY ~1.5% return. Every reported 'Sharpe ~2-3' for VIX strategies is either gross-of-cost, pre-Volmageddon, or implicitly levered. Leverage scales the tiny return up but scales the tail catastrophically and reintroduces gap/ruin risk. Do not extrapolate the unlevered Sharpe to a levered book.
- Survivorship & regime-cherry-picking: many backtests (incl. some Deribit/practitioner ones) start in calm windows or stop before a crash; XIV/SVXY at -1x literally ceased to exist. A backtest that 'survives' only because the worst day is outside the sample is worthless. Insist the sample SPANS Feb-2018, Mar-2020 (equities) and May-2022 LUNA / Nov-2022 FTX / Aug-2024 (crypto).
- Transaction-cost & borrow underestimation: VXX short-borrow fees are high and time-varying (can exceed the roll yield); ETP expense ratios (~1%/yr) and bid/ask compound. In crypto, the 0.03%/side fee is small but the 12.5%-of-premium cap, wide OTM/illiquid-strike spreads, and perp funding to maintain the delta hedge can dominate net PnL. Naive backtests that assume mid-price fills overstate returns badly.
- Structural-change / non-stationarity: SVXY was permanently changed from -1.0x to -0.5x after 2018 — the instrument's payoff is not the same pre/post, so splicing histories is invalid. Crypto vol regime bands compressed ~10% in the 2024-25 cycle. The harvestable carry itself shifts when product structures and market microstructure change.
- Data-snooping in timing signals: roll-yield thresholds, lookbacks, percentile cutoffs (e.g. the '0.10 daily roll' or '75th percentile VVIX slope') are easy to overfit; Simon-Campasano's own rule went 'slightly negative' out of sample. Use walk-forward / purged CV, pre-register thresholds, and prefer economically-motivated signals (premium sign, contango/backwardation) over fitted parameters.
- Vol-of-vol strategies are largely paper-only at retail: the headline VVIX-slope Sharpes (1.09-1.50) are GROSS and require daily long/short switching of VIX-option straddles — the authors admit costs would cut them and give no net figure. We likely cannot trade VIX options; treat VVIX as a SIGNAL/filter, not a tradable sleeve, unless we can model VIX-option costs explicitly.
- Crypto-specific: exchange/counterparty risk (FTX), oracle/liquidation cascades, funding-rate regime shifts, thin OTM/long-dated option liquidity, and the fact that crypto VRP being HIGHER in calm regimes means the worst short-vol losses come AFTER the calmest, highest-carry periods — the carry itself lures you into max size right before the gap.
- Approximation error: VIX is only an approximation of the 30-day variance swap (jump/discretization error can be significant per Ait-Sahalia/Karaman/Mancini, Martin); conflating VIX-premium, VRP, and variance-swap returns introduces measurement error that can masquerade as or destroy a signal. Be precise about which object you are trading.

### Data needed
- VIX futures settlement history (continuous + individual contracts) — FREE from CBOE (cboe.com/tradable-products/vix/vix-historical-data and /term-structure) and CFE; VIX index itself free from FRED (VIXCLS, 1990-) and Yahoo. Needed to reconstruct roll yield, contango/backwardation, and the Cheng ex-ante premium for H5.
- VVIX index history — FREE from CBOE (published daily). Needed for H6 (Park tail-hedge signal) and to construct the equity vol-of-vol level/slope. VIX term-structure of VVIX (VVIX at multiple horizons) is harder to get free.
- VIX options & S&P 500 (SPX) options end-of-day chains for net-of-cost straddle/put backtests — partially FREE via CBOE DataShop samples and delayed quotes; full history is paid (OptionMetrics/IvyDB, ORATS, CBOE LiveVol). Without these, VVIX-slope and equity straddle strategies (Branger/Park replication) remain paper-only. We DO have 56M SPY/QQQ LOB snapshots — usable to estimate SPY-option-proxy richness and realistic spreads for the equity side.
- Deribit BTC/ETH implied-vol surfaces + DVOL (we HAVE: 2021-2026) and DVOL futures (since Mar-2023 BTC, later ETH) — sufficient for H1-H3, H7. Verify we have per-strike bid/ask (not just mid) to model the 0.03%/side fee, 12.5%-premium cap, and OTM spread realistically.
- Crypto realized-vol series at multiple horizons (computable from our 1h/4h/1d OHLCV) to pair against DVOL for VRP and IV-RV-gap signals (H1, H3).
- Crypto funding-rate + OI + liquidation history (we HAVE: 228 perps ~23k hrs, Coinalyze) — for H4 (funding/OI as vol/backwardation early-warning) and to net the cost of delta-hedging short straddles with perps.
- Borrow/short-fee history for VXX/VIXY and ETP expense ratios — needed to make the equity short-vol net-of-cost realistic; approximate from broker borrow-rate feeds or Markit/IHS (paid) or use conservative fixed assumptions and stress them.
- Cross-asset stress dates / event calendar (Feb-2018, Mar-2020, May-2022 LUNA, Nov-2022 FTX, Aug-2024 carry unwind) to force every backtest to span the relevant tails and to test H8 (tail correlation between equity and crypto short-vol).
- FX & commodities (to-be-sourced) are LOWER priority for this specific area; the volatility-term-structure edge is concentrated in equity-index vol and crypto. If extended: free FX vol from CME FedWatch-adjacent data is limited; commodity (oil/gas) variance risk premia (Schwartz/Trolle, ~0.59 oil / 0.35 gas Sharpe) would need CME futures + options (partly free settlement, paid options).

### Adversarial verification — reliability: **medium**
_Net-of-cost reality:_ Blunt take: the volatility risk premium is one of the few genuinely real, mechanism-backed premia (implied > realized persists across equities and crypto, confirmed into 2025), but essentially every advertised Sharpe in this area is an illusion of one of three kinds — gross-of-cost, pre-Volmageddon, or implicitly levered. The honest unlevered number is AQR's ~1.5%/yr at Sharpe 0.68; that is the whole edge before leverage, and leverage is exactly what converts 0.68 into a 'headline 2-3' AND into -50% to -96% tail events (XIV -96% Feb-2018; SVXY -91%; SVOL -33.5% as recently as Apr-2025 even at -0.2x). Costs and structure compound the decay: VXX has bled -99.9% since 2009 (the carry is real on the short side but borrow on VXX can exceed the roll yield, ETP fees ~1%/yr, SVXY was permanently cut to -0.5x post-2018 so the harvestable carry itself halved and pre-2018 histories cannot be spliced). The 'timing beats carry' edge is directionally right but the mechanical VIX-basis rules degrade out of sample (Quantpedia: 'slightly negative... alpha deteriorating'; Simon-Campasano went negative OOS; 3.0 -> 0.36). The recent tape is the strongest warning: VRP was crowded and even went negative on a 12-month rolling basis in 2023-2024, exactly the McLean-Pontiff post-publication-decay pattern (anomalies fall ~58% post-publication). Crypto is the same trade with the dial turned up — bigger premium (14% vs 2% VRP), bigger Sharpe (0.8), but fatter tails (LUNA, FTX, Aug-2024 VIX>64) AND a perverse regime inversion where carry is fattest in calm right before the gap, so a naive optimizer sizes you to maximum exactly before ruin. Net: an unlevered, tail-budgeted, contango-conditioned short-vol sleeve can earn a modest positive risk-adjusted return; any backtest showing Sharpe >1 that doesn't (a) net Deribit/ETP fees and borrow, (b) span Feb-2018/Mar-2020/May-2022/Nov-2022/Aug-2024, and (c) report CVaR and worst-single-day rather than Sharpe, is overstated and should be assumed to halve or worse live.
- **[CONFIRMED]** AQR (2018): a delta-hedged, beta-light short S&P 500 5%-OTM put at unit leverage earned only ~1.5%/yr at 2.2% vol (Sharpe 0.68, max DD -10%, beta 0.04) net of costs 1996-2016 — i.e. the unlevered VRP harvest is a tiny absolute return that is crash-risk compensation, not free alpha. — The exact triplet (1.5% return, 2.2% vol, Sharpe 0.68) is reproduced verbatim from AQR's own May-2018 white paper, including the methodology (front-month 5% OTM put, unit leverage, delta-hedged daily, held to expiry, net of transaction costs, 1996-2016). The adversarial reading is the correct one: a 0.68 Sharpe at 2.2% vol is a ~1.5% return that only becomes a 'headline' Sharpe when levered ~7x to ~15% vol, which mechanically reintroduces the -50%+ tail. This claim is honestly stated and well-sourced; if anything it under-sells the danger because the worst months (Mar-2000, Sep-2008) plus the OUT-OF-SAMPLE Feb-2018 and Mar-2020 events confirm the convexity warning.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Feb-5-2018 'Volmageddon' was a structural, endogenous tail unique to leveraged vol-ETPs: end-of-day rebalancing forced ~$800m of VIX-futures buying into the close, VIX +116% (largest ever) on an S&P move of only ~-4.1%, XIV -96% (terminated by Credit Suisse), SVXY -91%; the mechanic still exists. — Multiple independent sources (CFA Institute Financial Analysts Journal 2021, Bloomberg, sixfigureinvesting, OptionMetrics) corroborate the core facts: VIX +116% (17.31->37.32), XIV -96%, the ~$5bn short-vol ETP complex, the mechanical 'must-buy-into-the-close' rebalancing feedback loop, and Credit Suisse's acceleration event redeeming XIV at $5.99 (vs prior NAV ~$100+). The structural-tail framing — that this is endogenous to the leveraged-ETP design, not generic market risk, and re-triggerable — is the consensus academic interpretation. Numbers are precise and verified.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Crypto shows the SAME vol-premium structure but LARGER, with a regime INVERSION: BTC variance risk premium ~14%/yr vs ~2% for S&P 500; BTC return premium ~66%/yr; BTC Sharpe ~0.8 (~2x S&P); and crucially the BTC VRP is HIGHER in calm/low-vol regimes and LOWER in stress — opposite the equity intuition. — Verified directly from the source paper text (Almeida, Grith, Miftachov & Wang, arXiv:2410.15195, v2 dated Aug-2025): 'the BP averages 66% per annum, while the BVRP averages 14%... Bollerslev, Tauchen, and Zhou (2009) find a 2% variance risk premium (VRP) for the S&P 500... its annualized Sharpe Ratio (SR) is approximately 0.8, which is nearly twice that of the S&P 500' (SPY SR ~0.45). The regime inversion is stated in the abstract: 'The low-volatility regime implies... a high Bitcoin Variance Risk Premium (BVRP). In high-volatility states... the BVRP is lower.' Data is from Deribit. Every quantitative figure in the finding matches the paper exactly. NOTE: these are GROSS premia from a single 2017-ish-to-recent sample on the largest crypto-options venue; they are NOT net-of-cost tradable Sharpes, and the regime inversion is the trap, not the edge — peak carry occurs right before the worst gaps (LUNA/FTX/Aug-2024).
- **[WEAKENED]** Term-structure TIMING beats static carry: Cheng's ex-ante VIX premium predicts ex-post VIX-futures returns with slope ~0.92, and FALLS/turns negative when risk rises ('low premium-response puzzle'); cutting short exposure when the premium goes negative beats short-only. (Paired with Simon-Campasano basis rule ~19.67% 2007-2011 but deteriorating OOS.) — The CORE empirical fact is confirmed: Cheng (2019, RFS) shows the VIX premium predicts ex-post VIX-futures returns with a slope near one (~0.92) and exhibits the low-premium-response puzzle — independently corroborated. However the TRADABILITY/timing claim is materially weaker than presented. Quantpedia's own assessment of the closely-related VIX-term-structure timing strategy states bluntly: 'OOS back-test shows slightly negative performance. It looks that strategy's alpha is deteriorating in the out-of-sample period,' and the cited ~3.0 headline Sharpe collapses to ~0.36 in post-period samples. Simon-Campasano's 19.67% relies on 5x-initial-margin leverage and the authors themselves flag it goes 'slightly negative' OOS. So the SIGNAL (premium sign, contango/backwardation) is real and economically motivated, but the realized timing edge net of costs is small, regime-dependent, and decay-prone — consistent with the finding's own hedged language but warranting a downgrade from how robust the 'timing beats carry' headline sounds.
- **[WEAKENED]** Vol-of-vol carries its own premium: the VVIX term-structure SLOPE generates a long/short straddle strategy with gross Sharpe ~1.50 (vs 1.20 short-only) on 1-month S&P straddles, incremental to the VIX slope and VRP; high VVIX predicts low subsequent put/tail-hedge returns (Park). — The numbers are accurately reported BUT the finding's own caveat is the operative truth: these are GROSS, paper-only results. Branger-Hulsbusch-Kraftschik (2017) is confirmed at Sharpe 1.50 vs 1.20 (1-mo straddles, Sep-2007-Aug-2014, 75th-pctile threshold), but the authors AND the independent skeptic CXO Advisory both state the results are gross and that 'accounting for the costs of monthly straddle portfolio reformation and daily long-short switching... would reduce reported Sharpe ratios' — with NO net figure given. Sample ends 2014; no post-2018 net replication exists. Direction (high VVIX -> tail hedges rich -> low subsequent returns) is economically sensible and likely persists in SIGN, but as a tradable sleeve at retail (requires liquid VIX-option straddles) it is effectively unverified and the 1.50 Sharpe should not be banked. Treat strictly as a filter, not alpha.

---

## Dispersion and correlation risk premium  `dispersion`

The correlation risk premium (CRP) -- option-implied equity correlation systematically exceeding subsequently-realized correlation -- is one of the most robustly documented risk premia in option markets and is the dominant component of the index variance risk premium. It is large in magnitude (historically ~10-18 correlation points; ~6-9 pts in recent decades; -5.7%/yr p-value<0.001 on S&P 500 equicorrelation in the most rigorous recent decomposition) and economically/statistically significant across the US, Europe, and globally. BUT the gross-to-net gap is brutal: the canonical Driessen-Maenhout-Vilkov (2009) result is that the premium "cannot be exploited with realistic trading frictions" -- a textbook limits-to-arbitrage premium. The classic equally-weighted dispersion trade (short index straddle / long single-name straddles) earned a Sharpe of ~1.2 in 1996-2000 but went to roughly zero/negative after 2000 once spreads tightened; later academic backtests claiming net Sharpe ~0.4 (Schadner/Deng-style on 2000-2017 data) rest on optimistic option transaction-cost assumptions. The trade survived as a live institutional book in 2023-2025 because of AI/mega-cap-driven single-stock decoupling, but its profit is highly conditional, deeply short left-tail (it is a fat-tail strategy that loses heavily in correlation spikes like Mar-2020 and Apr-2025), and largely a concentration-of-the-index artifact rather than broad decorrelation. The crypto analog is nascent: BTC and ETH carry very large variance risk premia (BTC VRP ~14%/yr vs ~2% S&P 500), liquid options exist only on BTC/ETH (no single-name alt options), and BTC-ETH spot correlation rarely falls below 0.8 while their implied vols decoupled in mid-2024 -- so a true multi-name crypto dispersion trade is not implementable on listed options, but a realized-correlation/cross-sectional dispersion factor on perps is testable.

### Findings

**Option-implied equity index correlation systematically exceeds subsequently realized correlation -- a large, priced, negative correlation risk premium that is the main driver of the index variance risk premium. Index options are 'expensive' relative to the cost of a replicating basket of single-name options.**
- Effect size: Driessen-Maenhout-Vilkov (S&P100, 1996-2003): implied correlation ~39.5% (S&P500-type) / 46.0% (DJ30) vs realized 32.5% / 35.5% => CRP ~7-10 correlation points, and the original paper documents an ~18-pt gap on their sample. The single-name variance risk premium is near zero while the index VRP is strongly negative -- the entire index VRP is attributable to priced correlation risk. Cboe Factor Dispersion whitepaper decomposition (most rigorous, recent): S&P500 equicorrelation risk premium = -5.74% p.a. (Newey-West p<0.001), vs equal-weighted single-name Average VRP of only -0.62% (p=0.286, insignificant).
- Strength: strong · Recency: Premium persists post-2018/2020 but has compressed: Faria-Kosowski-Wang (2022) find CRP of ~6.7-8.9 pts (91-day) recently vs ~18 pts in 1996-2003 -- a clear secular decline as the trade got crowded and option spreads tightened. Implied correlation remained well above realized in H2-2023 and mid-2024; spiked (COR/DSPX into low-40s) in Apr-2025 tariff shock and Mar-2020. No direct equity-option analog tested in crypto, but BTC/ETH VRP is the cross-asset cousin.
- Cites: Driessen, Maenhout, Vilkov 2009, 'The Price of Correlation Risk: Evidence from Equity Options', Journal of Finance 64(3):1377-1406; SSRN 673425; Faria, Kosowski, Wang 2022, 'The Correlation Risk Premium: International Evidence', Journal of Banking & Finance 136; SSRN 3276601; Gerchik, Ruffo, Schonleber (Cboe) 'Factor Dispersions' whitepaper, cdn.cboe.com/resources/education/research_publications/FactorDispersionWhitepaper.pdf; Bossu, Carr 2014 (dispersion/correlation swap weighting); Buraschi, Kosowski, Trojani 2014 (correlation risk priced in hedge-fund returns)

**The classic equally-weighted dispersion trade (sell index straddle, buy single-name straddles, delta-hedged) earns a high GROSS Sharpe and alpha but the CRP 'cannot be exploited with realistic trading frictions' -- a limits-to-arbitrage premium. Net profitability collapsed once option markets matured.**
- Effect size: Deng (2008)-style backtest: average monthly return ~24% with Sharpe ~1.2 over 1996-2000, collapsing to ~ -0.03%/month and Sharpe ~ -0.17 after 2000 (attributed to cross-listing + tighter bid-ask post-1999/2000). Driessen-Maenhout-Vilkov: the correlation-trading strategy is attractive to a frictionless CRRA investor (high alpha) but net of realistic option spreads the alpha disappears. Later academic claim (S&P500 constituents 2000-2017): 14.5-26.5% p.a. net, Sharpe 0.34-0.40 -- but with max drawdown ~ -43% and optimistic cost assumptions. Practitioner cost stack: ~300 bps basket crossing + 15-50 bps carry/funding + gamma/mismatch noise can fully offset the theoretical 1-2 vol-point implied-vs-realized correlation edge.
- Strength: strong · Recency: The post-2000 collapse is the central cautionary tale. Trade revived as a live institutional/pod book in 2023-2025 on AI/mega-cap decoupling (e.g. Nvidia -17% on DeepSeek Jan-2025 while index -1-2%); contributed to hedge-fund alpha (~2.62% industry alpha in 2024 partly from dispersion). But Apr-2025 correlation spike compressed returns; it is explicitly 'a fat-tail strategy that loses a lot during crisis periods'. Survival now depends on concentrated, automated, low-churn baskets, not broad 500-name shorts.
- Cites: Driessen, Maenhout, Vilkov 2009, J. Finance 64(3) (limits-to-arbitrage conclusion); Deng 2008, 'Volatility Dispersion Trading' (1996-2000 vs post-2000), via BSIC Bocconi backtest writeup bsic.it/backtesting-dispersion-trading-chapter-i; Quantpedia 'Dispersion Trading' (Sharpe 0.82, ann. 15.4% net, MaxDD -43.5%, 1996-2007, S&P100); Schadner-type backtest summarized in Quantpedia / MDPI Mathematics 8(9):1627 (2000-2017, Sharpe 0.34-0.40); Interactive Brokers/IBKR Quant 'Dispersion Trading in Practice: the Dirty Version' (300 bps basket crossing, vega-vs-gamma mismatch)

**Option-implied correlation / the correlation risk premium predicts future aggregate market returns out-of-sample, with the CRP being the longer-horizon predictor (the VRP predicts only short-horizon). Implied correlation also strongly predicts future realized correlation and diversification benefits.**
- Effect size: Buss-Schonleber-Vilkov: out-of-sample R2 of 13% at 3-month and 7% at 12-month horizon for market-return forecasts; at the annual horizon predictability comes EXCLUSIVELY from the correlation risk premium (VRP predictability fades after ~1 quarter). Implied correlation predicts future average pairwise correlation with R2 up to 35.4% (and lagged realized correlation up to 30.0%), and future cross-sectional beta dispersion R2 up to 32.3% at 9 months.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Working-paper / FMA-conference evidence (mid-2010s data through ~2017); OOS R2 of 7-13% is large for return prediction and is the kind of result that often shrinks live. Not independently re-verified post-2020 in the sources pulled; treat as a timing/sizing signal rather than a standalone alpha. Directly relevant: an implied-correlation index (Cboe COR1M/COR6M, DSPX) is a tradeable, observable version of this predictor.
- Cites: Buss, Schonleber, Vilkov, 'Expected Stock Returns and the Correlation Risk Premium' / 'Expected Correlation and Future Market Returns: The Sum of the Parts is More than the Whole' (NY Fed/FMA working papers; SSRN/AEA 2017-2019); Driessen, Maenhout, Vilkov 2013, 'Option-Implied Correlations and the Price of Correlation Risk', SSRN 2166829; Bollerslev, Tauchen, Zhou 2009 (VRP predicts market returns -- the short-horizon benchmark)

**Equity volatility markets exhibit Law-of-One-Price violations between index-implied and option-implied bounds (closely related to the dispersion/index-vs-component wedge), and a relative-value strategy trading the deviation earns a large Sharpe -- but the deviation is driven by systematic risk and demand pressure (i.e., it is a risk premium / capacity-limited, not free arbitrage).**
- Effect size: Van Tassel (NY Fed): VIX-futures prices deviate significantly from their option-implied no-arbitrage upper bounds; deviations widen in stress and predict VIX-futures returns; a deviation-based relative-value strategy earns 'a large Sharpe ratio and economically significant alpha-to-margin' (qualitative in abstract; deviations are static-arbitrage-sized only intermittently). Adjacent VIX/variance carry benchmarks: short-vol/variance Sharpe ~0.8-1.3 in calm regimes but catastrophic tail (XIV went to ~0 on 5-Feb-2018; short-vol blew up Mar-2020).
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Van Tassel staff report (data through ~2020). The 2018 'Volmageddon' and Mar-2020 are the recency stress tests: gross carry is real, net survival depends on tail sizing and margin. Demand-pressure driver means capacity erodes the edge as more capital enters.
- Cites: Van Tassel, 'The Law of One Price in Equity Volatility Markets', FRBNY Staff Report 953 (2020); SSRN 3751612; Garleanu, Pedersen, Poteshman 2009 'Demand-Based Option Pricing' (demand pressure as driver of option premia)

**Crypto carries very large second-moment risk premia: BTC (and ETH) variance risk premia dwarf equities. This is the cross-asset cousin of the index VRP and is harvestable by selling BTC/ETH vol -- but there is NO listed single-name dispersion trade in crypto because only BTC/ETH have liquid options.**
- Effect size: Bitcoin variance risk premium ~0.14 (14% p.a.) unconditional (0.12 high-vol regime, 0.17 low-vol), vs ~2% for the S&P 500 -- BTC VRP is ~7x larger. Bitcoin return premium ~66% p.a.; BTC Sharpe ~0.8 vs ~0.5 for S&P 500 (Jul-2017 to Dec-2022, Deribit options). Practitioner result: systematically selling BTC risk-reversals / vega gave strong risk-adjusted returns; a ~75-80% short-vol / 20-25% spot-BTC mix maximized Sharpe. BTC-ETH spot correlation rarely <0.80 since 2017 yet their implied vols decoupled from mid-2024 -- the seed of a BTC-vs-ETH 'two-name dispersion' but with only one degree of freedom.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Strong and current: BTC/ETH VRP documented through 2022-2025; ETH vol was systematically sold/undervalued through 2023, vega supply dropped from Dec-2023 (~3 vol-pt drop Jan-2024). 2024 'year of volatility' and BTC ETF launch raised vol-of-vol. Crypto VRP is more regime-dependent and has a NEGATIVE relationship between return premium and VRP (opposite to equities). No academic listed-options dispersion result exists for crypto -- the gap is structural (no alt single-name options).
- Cites: Risk Premia in the Bitcoin Market, arXiv:2410.15195 (BTC VRP ~14%, Sharpe ~0.8, Jul-2017-Dec-2022); The Bitcoin VIX and Its Variance Risk Premium (ResearchGate 346500941); Deribit Insights: 'Crypto 2024: The Year of Volatility', 'ETH Vol Back in Fashion', 'Bitcoin Options: Finding edge in four years of volatility regimes'; Cross-sectional crypto factor lit: skewness/idiosyncratic risk (J. Int. Fin. Markets 2024), low-vol anomaly post-2017 (Finance Research Letters 2026)

**A large part of the recent 'dispersion' opportunity in the S&P 500 is a mega-cap concentration effect, not broad decorrelation -- implied correlation dropping reflects a few names (the Mag-7/AI complex) diverging from the pack, which changes the risk profile of a naive equal-weighted dispersion book.**
- Effect size: Mid-2024 COR3M drop was 'almost entirely a concentration effect: one mega-cap diverging from the pack, rather than 500 stocks becoming less correlated.' Cboe Lead-50 vs Lag-50 dispersion (Apr-2026): leaders +19.1% vs laggards <1%. Cboe decomposition shows the naive (index-weighting) dispersion is NOT premium-maximizing -- the weighted-covariance term dilutes the -5.74% equicorrelation premium; better-weighted (e.g. factor/concentrated) baskets capture more.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Highly current (2024-2026). Directly relevant to construction risk: equal-weighted single-name legs vs cap-weighted index leg leaves the trade short the dispersion of a handful of giant names, so 'vega-neutral' is not 'correlation-neutral'. This is why the trade now requires concentrated, hand-built baskets.
- Cites: Patricia Ji, 'The Dispersion Signal', ON the Market (Substack) -- mid-2024 concentration effect; Cboe Index Insights April 2026 (Lead-50 +19.1% vs Lag-50 <1%); Cboe Factor Dispersions whitepaper (naive index-weighting sub-optimal for capturing CRP)

### Testable hypotheses
- H1 (crypto realized dispersion, fully testable on our data): Define implied/realized equicorrelation of the top-N coins from OHLCV (1h/4h/1d, 2024-02 to 2026-06). Realized average pairwise correlation among top-50 coins is high (>0.6) and mean-reverting; a regime where realized correlation is unusually LOW predicts subsequent correlation REVERSION (rise). Falsifiable: short-realized-correlation (long idiosyncratic dispersion) via a market-neutral basket should LOSE in the month after correlation troughs. Test with rolling correlation + Newey-West.
- H2 (BTC vs basket VRP, testable with Deribit DVOL + perps): BTC implied variance (DVOL^2) exceeds realized variance by a positive premium analogous to equity VRP; magnitude ~10-15% p.a. Falsifiable: a delta-hedged short-DVOL/short-straddle carry on BTC has positive mean but the Sharpe net of Deribit fees + funding + hedging slippage is materially below the gross ~0.8, and is concentrated in low-vol regimes (per the documented negative return-VRP relation).
- H3 (BTC-ETH two-name dispersion proxy): Since BTC-ETH spot correlation rarely <0.8 but their DVOLs decoupled from mid-2024, a 'short BTC-ETH implied correlation' proxy (long ETH vol / short BTC vol, vega-matched, delta-hedged) earns positive carry only when (DVOL_ETH/DVOL_BTC) implied-correlation proxy is above its realized counterpart. Falsifiable: regress realized BTC-ETH correlation on the implied proxy; if slope<1 and intercept>0, a premium exists; test net of the wider ETH-option spread.
- H4 (concentration vs decorrelation in S&P 500, testable on full S&P 500 daily/intraday bars): Decompose index realized variance into average single-name variance + average pairwise covariance. Hypothesis: most 2024-2026 'dispersion' in realized terms is driven by the top ~10 mega-caps, i.e. excluding them, residual pairwise correlation is stable. Falsifiable by comparing cap-weighted vs equal-weighted realized correlation series; if equal-weighted correlation is flat while cap-weighted falls, the dispersion 'signal' is concentration.
- H5 (implied-correlation timing as a market/vol signal): Using a constructed implied-correlation proxy (from S&P 500 + a free options/VIX source), a high implied-minus-realized correlation gap predicts lower forward index returns and higher forward realized correlation at 1-3 month horizon (Buss-Schonleber-Vilkov OOS R2 ~7-13%). Falsifiable: out-of-sample R2 on our sample is statistically indistinguishable from zero after costs/lookahead controls.
- H6 (short-vol tail asymmetry): Any short-correlation/short-vol carry we build (equity or crypto) has positive mean monthly return but left-skew and a max drawdown that dwarfs the mean (analogous to -43% equity dispersion DD and XIV->0). Falsifiable: bootstrap of monthly P&L shows skew>-0.5 and 99% VaR < 3x mean monthly P&L (i.e. tail is NOT catastrophic) -- prior evidence predicts this is FALSE.

### Harvest strategies
- Crypto realized-dispersion factor (no options needed; uses perps/OHLCV): Build a market-neutral long/short basket on top-50 coins that goes long high-idiosyncratic-vol names and short the BTC/ETH-beta-hedged market, sized to be short realized correlation. Rebalance daily/4h. Cost drag: perp taker fees ~5-10 bps round-trip on liquid coins (much higher on small alts -> restrict to top ~20 by ADV), funding 0-50 bps/8h variable. This harvests cross-sectional dispersion without paying option spreads -- the cleanest crypto-native version. Watch capacity: small-alt liquidity caps notional sharply.
- BTC/ETH variance carry (Deribit): Short DVOL exposure via delta-hedged short straddles/strangles or short variance, on BTC and/or ETH, sized small with hard tail stops. Harvests the ~14% BTC VRP. Cost drag: Deribit option taker fee 0.03% of underlying (capped), continuous delta-hedge slippage on perp/spot, plus funding on the hedge. Best in low-realized-vol regimes; overlay a DVOL-term-structure or DVOL-vs-realized filter to avoid selling cheap vol. Pair 75-80% short-vol with 20-25% long spot-BTC to improve Sharpe (per Deribit practitioner finding).
- BTC-vs-ETH implied-correlation/relative-vol trade (Deribit, two liquid names only): Vega-matched long ETH straddle / short BTC straddle, delta-hedged, entered only when ETH implied vol is cheap relative to BTC and BTC-ETH implied correlation proxy is rich vs realized. This is the ONLY listed-options 'dispersion-like' trade available in crypto. Cost: two-leg option spreads (ETH wider), gamma-hedging churn; structurally one degree of freedom, so treat as relative-vol, not true dispersion.
- S&P 500 concentrated dispersion (requires sourcing equity options data): Short ~1-month index straddle (or short variance via index options) vs long single-name straddles on a CONCENTRATED, hand-selected basket of high-realized-vol / high-idiosyncratic names (NOT all 500, NOT equal-weight), vega-matched, delta-hedged, low rebalance frequency. Net edge only if implied-vs-realized correlation gap > total cost stack (~300 bps basket crossing + 15-50 bps carry). Entry filter: DSPX/COR1M elevated, VIX<20, implied correlation <0.4. Explicitly a short-left-tail carry -- size for a -40% drawdown.
- Correlation-timing overlay (signal, not standalone alpha): Use a constructed implied-correlation index (Cboe COR1M/COR6M / DSPX once data sourced, or a homebuilt proxy from free option data) to size beta exposure or short-vol exposure -- raise risk when implied correlation is high relative to realized (premium fat), cut when it inverts. Near-zero incremental cost since it only modulates an existing book.
- Cross-asset VRP-relative-value (once FX/commodity option data sourced): Tilt short-vol carry toward assets with the widest implied-minus-realized variance gap, away from those near/below zero. Diversifies the single-market tail. Cost: option spreads vary widely by market; FX-index and commodity-index options are the cheaper venues.

### Pitfalls
- GROSS-VS-NET illusion is THE central trap here. Driessen-Maenhout-Vilkov's headline finding is that the CRP exists precisely BECAUSE it cannot be arbitraged net of frictions. Any backtest using mid prices, ignoring single-name option bid-ask (often 5-20% of premium), or assuming continuous costless delta-hedging will massively overstate Sharpe. The 1996-2000 Sharpe ~1.2 -> post-2000 ~ -0.17 collapse is the empirical proof that spreads, not signal, drove early profits.
- Vega-neutral is NOT correlation-neutral. Books are sized on vega but correlation shocks arrive through gamma; equal-weighted single-name legs vs cap-weighted index leg also leaves you short the dispersion of a few mega-caps. A 'hedged' dispersion book can lose violently in a correlation spike (Mar-2020, Apr-2025). Model the P&L in gamma/realized-covariance space, not just vega.
- Left-tail / peso problem: short correlation and short vol are short deep out-of-the-money catastrophe. Average monthly P&L can be positive for years then give back multiples in one event (XIV -> ~0 on 5-Feb-2018; -43% dispersion drawdown). Sharpe is the wrong objective; use tail-aware metrics (CVaR, max DD, return-to-DD) and assume the worst month is far larger than the historical worst.
- Concentration masquerading as decorrelation: in a top-heavy index, a falling implied/realized correlation can be one mega-cap diverging, not broad decorrelation (documented mid-2024). A naive dispersion signal will misread this; decompose realized correlation cap-weighted vs equal-weighted before trading.
- Data-snooping / multiple-testing: dozens of basket-construction, weighting, filter, and rebalance choices. The Cboe paper itself shows naive index-weighting is sub-optimal -- which invites optimizing weights until a backtest sings. Pre-register the construction; use purged/embargoed CV; penalize for the search.
- Secular decay / crowding: CRP fell from ~18 pts (1996-2003) to ~6.7-8.9 pts (recent). DSPX launch (2023) + pod crowding mean the edge is smaller and more contested now than in any paper's sample. Capacity is real -- demand pressure is a documented driver of the premium, so adding capital erodes it.
- Crypto-specific: there are NO liquid single-name altcoin options, so a listed multi-name crypto dispersion trade is not implementable -- do not import the equity playbook wholesale. BTC/ETH VRP has a NEGATIVE return-VRP relation (opposite to equities), so equity intuition about when to sell vol is misleading. Funding-rate and exchange-fee drag on crypto carry is large and time-varying; 2024-2026 is a single regime (post-ETF) and may not generalize.
- Realized-correlation estimation error: implied-vs-realized comparisons are sensitive to the realized estimator (window, sampling frequency, overlap), and overlapping-return regressions inflate t-stats. Use non-overlapping holding-period returns and Newey-West, and check robustness to the realized-vol window.

### Data needed
- Equity options / VIX (to-be-sourced, FREE): Cboe S&P 500 Implied Correlation indices (COR1M, COR3M, COR6M) and the DSPX dispersion index -- historical levels are downloadable from the S&P Dow Jones Indices / Cboe websites (cboe.com, spglobal.com/spdji) as CSV/Excel. VIX and VIX term structure from Cboe (free). These let us build the implied-correlation timing signal (H5) and decomposition WITHOUT licensing single-name option chains.
- Single-name equity option surfaces (the hard, costly gap): a true S&P 500 dispersion backtest needs single-stock implied vols / option chains for ~50-500 names. Free is hard; candidates: ORATS/IVolatility/historicaloptiondata (paid), or scrape limited free chains. Cheaper proxy: use Cboe DSPX (which already encodes the index-vs-single-name wedge) instead of rebuilding the basket -- strongly recommended given cost.
- Crypto (we have most of it): Deribit BTC/ETH IV surfaces + DVOL (2021-2026) -> compute BTC/ETH implied vs realized variance and the DVOL term structure (H2, H3). Top-50 coin OHLCV (1h/4h/1d, 2024-02 to 2026-06) -> realized pairwise correlation matrices, cross-sectional dispersion factor (H1, H4-crypto analog). 228 perps x ~23k hrs funding + Coinalyze funding/OI/liquidations -> cost model and regime conditioning for the dispersion/carry P&L.
- Crypto single-name options: NOT available for alts (only BTC/ETH liquid on Deribit). Document this as a hard constraint; the crypto dispersion test must use realized correlation / perps, not listed alt options.
- FX & commodities (to-be-sourced for cross-asset VRP RV): spot/forwards + rate differentials (free: FRED, central-bank sites, investing.com) and futures term structure (free: CME, Nasdaq Data Link/Quandl free tiers, barchart). For the VRP-RV extension, FX/commodity option-implied vols (e.g. CVOL from CME, OVX/GVZ/EUVIX from Cboe -- free) give cross-asset implied-vs-realized gaps.
- Realized-correlation & cost infrastructure: high-frequency intraday bars (we have 15m/1h S&P 500 and 1h crypto) to build robust realized covariance; a documented transaction-cost model (option bid-ask by liquidity tier ~5-20% of premium for single names, ~300 bps basket crossing for equities; Deribit 0.03% option fee + perp taker 5-10 bps + funding for crypto) to convert every gross backtest to net before drawing conclusions.

### Crypto/recent notes
RECENCY/DECAY: CRP compressed from ~18 pts (1996-2003, DMV) to ~6.7-8.9 pts (Faria-Kosowski-Wang, recent) as the trade crowded and option spreads tightened; classic equal-weighted dispersion went from Sharpe ~1.2 (1996-2000) to ~ -0.17 (post-2000). The premium itself remains real and significant (Cboe: S&P500 equicorrelation RP = -5.74%/yr, p<0.001) and the trade was a live, profitable pod book in 2023-2025 driven by AI/Mag-7 single-stock decoupling (Nvidia -17% on DeepSeek Jan-2025 vs index -1-2%), contributing to ~2.62% industry hedge-fund alpha in 2024. But Apr-2025 tariff shock spiked implied correlation (DSPX low-40s) and compressed returns -- confirming the deep short-tail. Critically, much of the 2024-2026 'dispersion' is mega-cap CONCENTRATION, not broad decorrelation (mid-2024 COR3M drop was one name diverging). Cboe launched DSPX (Sep-2023) and disseminates COR1M/COR6M -- free, tradeable implied-correlation gauges that should be our primary instrument rather than rebuilding single-name baskets. CRYPTO: BTC VRP ~14%/yr (vs ~2% S&P 500), BTC Sharpe ~0.8 (Jul-2017-Dec-2022, Deribit); ETH vol systematically sold/undervalued through 2023, vega supply fell from Dec-2023. BTC-ETH spot correlation rarely <0.8 yet their DVOLs decoupled mid-2024 -- a two-name relative-vol opportunity, but NO liquid alt single-name options exist, so a true multi-name crypto dispersion trade is structurally unavailable; the implementable crypto version is a realized cross-sectional dispersion factor on perps (fully testable on our data) plus BTC/ETH variance carry. Crypto VRP shows a NEGATIVE return-VRP relation (opposite to equities), and 2024-2026 is a single post-ETF regime -- generalization risk is high.

### Adversarial verification — reliability: **medium**
_Net-of-cost reality:_ Blunt take: the PREMIUM is real and well-documented; the NET-OF-COST ALPHA is the part that does not survive, and the headline findings are honest about this in places but too generous in others. The single most important fact -- confirmed independently -- is that Driessen-Maenhout-Vilkov's own headline is a limits-to-arbitrage result: the CRP exists precisely BECAUSE it cannot be arbitraged net of frictions, and Deng's empirics prove it (dispersion Sharpe 1.17 pre-2001 collapsed to 0.12 once spreads tightened and options cross-listed). So the gross-vs-net gap is not a footnote, it is the whole story. The academic 'net Sharpe 0.34-0.40 on 2000-2017' (MDPI) figures that the findings lean on are exactly the optimistic-cost results the findings elsewhere warn against -- they sit uncomfortably against DMV and Deng and should be treated as upper bounds, not expectations. Three hard realities for anyone trying to trade this today: (1) it is a CROWDED trade -- now packaged as bank swaps and a flagship pod/RV book -- with documented secular compression and a fresh March-2026 -4.9% to -6.1% blowup ('worst month since 2011'), so capacity and crowding are eroding what is left; (2) the tail is the strategy -- but note the findings get the tail DIRECTION partly wrong: long-dispersion typically WINS in a fast 'correlation-to-one' crash (March 2020 was its best month), and LOSES in slow correlation-up-without-a-crash regimes (Apr-2025, Mar-2026) -- mis-sizing the wrong tail is a real risk; (3) much of the 2024-2026 'opportunity' is mega-cap CONCENTRATION, not broad decorrelation, so a naive equal-weighted book is short the dispersion of a handful of giants and 'vega-neutral' is not 'correlation-neutral.' On crypto: the BTC/ETH VRP magnitudes (~14% vs ~2% S&P) are genuinely large and well-verified, but harvestability net of Deribit fees + perp funding + hedge slippage is unproven, the sample is a single pre-ETF regime, and there is NO listed multi-name dispersion trade -- so the only implementable crypto 'dispersion' is a realized cross-sectional factor on perps (untested) plus BTC/ETH variance carry that is regime-conditional with a negative return-VRP twist.
