Practical recommendation embedded in the findings is sound: use the FREE Cboe DSPX/COR1M/COR6M as the instrument/signal rather than rebuilding licensed single-name baskets, size for a >-40% drawdown, model P&L in gamma/realized-covariance space, and assume the live net Sharpe is closer to DMV's 'zero after frictions' than to the academic 0.4.
- **[CONFIRMED]** The correlation risk premium exists (option-implied equity correlation systematically exceeds subsequently-realized correlation) and is the dominant driver of the index variance risk premium, but Driessen-Maenhout-Vilkov (2009) conclude it 'cannot be exploited with realistic trading frictions' -- a textbook limits-to-arbitrage premium. — Independently verified from primary sources. DMV (2009, JF 64(3):1377-1406) explicitly state the correlation-trading strategy has high alpha for a frictionless CRRA investor but 'cannot be exploited with realistic trading frictions,' giving a limits-to-arbitrage interpretation -- the SSRN/Wiley/Tilburg/INSEAD abstracts all confirm this verbatim. Faria-Kosowski-Wang (2021/2022 JBF, full text) independently confirm the CRP (implied > realized correlation) is 'economically and statistically significant for all equity markets' in the US, Europe, and globally, and that the entire index VRP is attributable to priced correlation risk while the single-name VRP is near zero. The Cboe Factor Dispersions whitepaper (full text extracted) confirms the equicorrelation decomposition framework and that 'a high level of diversification is typically associated with a high correlation risk premium, making basket options more expensive.' This is among the better-documented option-market premia; the adversarial prior (overstated alpha) does NOT apply to the EXISTENCE of the premium, only to its EXPLOITABILITY -- and DMV themselves anticipated that.
- **[CONFIRMED]** The classic equally-weighted dispersion trade (short index straddle / long single-name straddles) earned Sharpe ~1.2 in 1996-2000 but collapsed to roughly zero/negative after 2000 once option spreads tightened and options cross-listed; later academic backtests claiming net Sharpe ~0.34-0.40 on 2000-2017 data rest on optimistic option transaction-cost assumptions. — The central cautionary tale checks out, with one numerical nuance. Deng (2008, Univ. of Illinois) is confirmed: average monthly return ~24% and Sharpe ~1.2 in 1996-2000, with the historical-vs-implied-correlation version showing Sharpe 1.17 before 2001 collapsing to 0.12 after 2001 (the findings said '~ -0.17'; the actual post-2000 figure is a near-zero SMALL POSITIVE ~0.12, not negative -- so the 'collapse to roughly zero' thesis is correct but 'negative' overstates it slightly). The collapse is explicitly attributed to ISE launch, cross-listing, a DoJ settlement, and tighter bid-offer -- i.e., spreads (not signal) drove early profits. The MDPI Mathematics 8(9):1627 (Schadner-style, 2000-2017) net figures are confirmed exactly: 14.52% and 26.51% p.a., Sharpe 0.40 and 0.34. Quantpedia confirms Sharpe 0.82, 15.39% p.a., MaxDD -43.49% (1996-2007, S&P100). The adversarial skepticism that the 0.34-0.40 figures rest on optimistic costs is WARRANTED: they are net-of-cost claims that sit awkwardly against DMV's frictionless-only result and Deng's post-2000 collapse, and the MDPI cost model could not be independently re-derived as conservative.
- **[WEAKENED]** The dispersion trade is a fat-tail / short-left-tail strategy that loses heavily in correlation spikes, citing March 2020 and April 2025 as the loss episodes; it survived as a live institutional book in 2023-2025 on AI/mega-cap decoupling and contributed to ~2.62% industry hedge-fund alpha in 2024. — The QUALITATIVE thesis (dispersion is short-correlation, fat-tailed, loses in correlation spikes) is strongly confirmed and is even better supported by FRESHER data than the findings cite. But the findings contain a MATERIAL SIGN ERROR: they repeatedly list March 2020 as a LOSS episode for the (long-dispersion = short-index-vol / long-single-name-vol) trade. Independent sources show the OPPOSITE -- the canonical long-dispersion trade MADE money in March 2020 (it was the best-ever month for Assenagon Alpha Volatility, a long-dispersion strategy); the SHORT-dispersion strategy had its worst drawdown (~-12.18%) in March 2020. In a 'correlation-goes-to-one' crash, index vol spikes and single-name vol spikes too, and the long-single-name leg plus the long-vega/long-gamma profile of single names often dominates -- the trade frequently WINS in a fast crash. The genuine loss episodes are corr-UP-without-a-crash regimes: the findings correctly flag Apr-2025 (DSPX into low-40s), and the FRESHEST data (March 2026 Iran geopolitical shock) is a textbook example: COR1M rose from ~15 to ~40, the JPMorgan dispersion index fell -4.9%, DSPX fell -6.1% ('worst month since 2011 in back-tested data'), described as 'one of the most crowded relative-value trades of the past three years.' The 2024 institutional revival, Nvidia/DeepSeek Jan-2025 decoupling (NVDA -17% vs SPX -1.5%, 'best day since 2020'), Apr-2025 spike, and 2.62% hedge-fund alpha are all confirmed. Net: thesis right, March-2020 attribution wrong, and there is now a stronger, more recent tail event (Mar-2026) than the findings knew about.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Crypto carries very large second-moment risk premia: Bitcoin VRP ~14%/yr vs ~2% for the S&P 500 (~7x larger), BTC return premium ~66%/yr, BTC Sharpe ~0.8 vs ~0.5 for S&P 500, with a NEGATIVE return-VRP relationship (opposite to equities); no listed single-name altcoin options exist so a true multi-name crypto dispersion trade is structurally unavailable. — Verified almost verbatim from the primary source (Almeida, Grith, Miftachov, Wang, 'Risk Premia in the Bitcoin Market,' arXiv:2410.15195, full PDF extracted). Exact quotes: 'the BP averages 66% per annum, while the BVRP averages 14%'; S&P 500 one-month equity-premium lower bound is 5% (Martin 2017) and Bollerslev-Tauchen-Zhou (2009) find a 2% S&P 500 VRP; BTC 'annualized Sharpe Ratio is approximately 0.8, which is nearly twice that of the S&P 500' (S&P SR ~0.5 per Dew-Becker-Giglio-Kelly; SPY ~0.45). The regime conditioning is confirmed (higher BVRP in the low-vol regime). The negative BP-BVRP relationship is explicitly confirmed: 'a negative relationship on average between BP and BVRP, contrasting with the positive correlation between future returns and VRP reported in the equity market.' Sample is Jul-2017-Dec-2022 Deribit options. The structural constraint (only BTC/ETH have liquid options, no alt single-name options) is consistent with all crypto-options sources. CAVEAT (adversarial): these are gross/option-implied premia; the paper does NOT establish net-of-fee harvestable Sharpe, the sample is a single pre-ETF regime, and crypto VRP is highly regime-dependent -- so 'harvestable' is unproven net of Deribit fees + perp funding + delta-hedge slippage. The MAGNITUDE claims are confirmed; the IMPLEMENTABILITY/harvest claim remains untested.
- **[UNCERTAIN]** Option-implied correlation / the CRP predicts future aggregate market returns out-of-sample, with the CRP being the longer-horizon predictor (VRP predicts only short horizon): OOS R2 of ~13% at 3-month and ~7% at 12-month horizon for market-return forecasts. — Partially verified, with the optimistic end unconfirmed and the usual OOS-shrinkage caveat applying. Buss-Schonleber-Vilkov is real and the ANNUAL-horizon figure is confirmed from the source: OOS R2 maxes at 7.9% at 9 months and is 7.0% at the one-year horizon, and the CRP carries the long-horizon predictability while the VRP fades after ~1 quarter -- consistent with the findings. However, the more eye-catching '13% at 3-month' figure could NOT be independently confirmed in this round; a related BSV paper using sector-ETF implied correlation reports R2 >22% at the annual horizon (a different construct). These are working-paper / FMA-conference results on data largely through ~2017, not independently re-verified post-2020. OOS R2 of 7-13% is very large for return prediction and is exactly the kind of result that shrinks live (the findings themselves flag this). The adversarial read: treat as a timing/sizing signal with high shrinkage risk, not standalone alpha; the 7% annual figure is credible, the 13% 3-month figure is unverified and should be discounted.

---

## Skew and tail-risk premium  `skew_tail`

Equity index options embed a robust, decades-stable left-skew/variance risk premium: 1-month implied vol averages ~4.2 vol points above subsequent realized (VIX 19.3 vs RV 15.1, 1990-2018), and OTM puts are systematically over-priced. Harvesting it by selling puts/straddles delivers attractive gross Sharpe (~0.65 for the CBOE PUT index 1986-2018) but the premium IS compensation for a hidden, severely negative left tail (skewness -2.1, kurtosis 12.6, beta 0.56, occasional -65% to -90% monthly blowups: 2008, Feb-2018 Volmageddon, Mar-2020). The mirror image — buying crash insurance — has a deeply negative expected return: AQR's systematic 5%-OTM put-buy bled -6.4%/yr (Sharpe -0.61, -92% drawdown) over 1985-2020, and trend-following is a cheaper, more reliable tail hedge. As cross-sectional/timing SIGNALS, option skew measures (volatility smirk, risk-neutral skewness, RNS term-structure, VRP) carry real predictive content (smirk long-short ~10.9%/yr risk-adjusted; RNS term-spread up to ~14-19%/yr in deciles; VRP predicts index returns with monthly R² ~2-8%), but most cross-sectional option-skew anomalies collapse to roughly zero net of realistic option transaction costs and decayed ~50% post-publication. Crypto is the structurally different and least-arbitraged frontier: Bitcoin's variance risk premium is ~14%/yr (vs ~2% for S&P 500), but its skew is frequently POSITIVE (right-tailed: ~39% of the BTC return premium comes from large +20-60% moves vs <1/3 for equities), so the equity playbook of "sell puts / fade upside" does not transfer cleanly — Deribit-era evidence favors selling the risk-reversal and selling straddles (IV>RV ~70% of the time, contango VRP ~+15 vol points).

### Findings

**Equity index options embed a persistent variance/skew risk premium: implied vol systematically exceeds realized, and OTM puts are richer than OTM calls. This is the foundational, well-replicated stylized fact.**
- Effect size: VIX averaged 19.3% vs S&P500 1-month realized 15.1% over 1990-2018 = +4.2 vol-point premium, positive in 27 of 29 years (only 2008 negative at -2.5). Carr-Wu (2009): index variance risk premium strongly negative (synthetic variance swap earns large positive return to the seller); single-stock VRP much smaller/near zero. Bollerslev-Tauchen-Zhou: S&P500 VRP ~2% (variance units). Annual ATM-put premium income ~22.1%/yr (CBOE PUT), ~37.1%/yr (weekly WPUT).
- Strength: strong · Recency: Held post-2018 and post-2020 in direction; magnitude compressed in 2023-2024 as the short-vol trade re-crowded (12-month rolling VRP briefly turned negative). The premium is largest precisely after vol spikes (it is state-dependent, not constant).
- Cites: Carr & Wu 2009, 'Variance Risk Premiums', Review of Financial Studies 22(3):1311-1341; Bollerslev, Tauchen & Zhou 2009, 'Expected Stock Returns and Variance Risk Premia', RFS 22(11):4463-4492; Bondarenko 2019, 'Historical Performance of Put-Writing Strategies', CBOE/Univ. Illinois-Chicago (VIX 19.3 vs RV 15.1; annual figures); Bakshi, Kapadia & Madan 2003, 'Stock Return Characteristics, Skew Laws...', RFS 16(1):101-143

**Harvesting the premium by systematic put-writing earns attractive gross risk-adjusted returns but is fundamentally a short-left-tail strategy — the Sharpe is paid for with catastrophic, fat-tailed drawdowns.**
- Effect size: CBOE PUT index (sell 1-mo ATM SPX puts, 1986-2018): 9.54% CAGR, 9.95% vol, Sharpe 0.65, Sortino 0.85, vs S&P500 9.80% CAGR / Sharpe 0.49. BUT skewness -2.09, kurtosis 12.58, worst month -17.65%, max drawdown -32.7%, beta 0.56. Quantpedia short-straddle+OTM-put-wing variant: 26%/yr, 19% vol, Sharpe 1.16, MDD -24%. Tail realizations: Feb-2018 'Volmageddon' XIV -90% in one day (VIX 17.3->37.3); naked VRP blew to ~-65% in Mar-2020.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Survived 2008, 2018, 2020 as a strategy (PUT index recovered) but each event delivered exactly the left-tail loss theory predicts. Net Sharpe is materially below gross once spreads/slippage and downside margin capital are charged.
- Cites: Bondarenko 2019 (CBOE PUT/WPUT/PPUT statistics); Quantpedia, 'Volatility Risk Premium Effect' (short-straddle Sharpe 1.16); Bhansali & Harris 2021, 'Everybody's Doing It: Short Volatility and Volmageddon', Financial Analysts Journal 77(3)

**Buying crash insurance (OTM index puts) has a large, persistent NEGATIVE expected return — this is the direct price of the skew/tail premium paid by the hedger, and the most brutally honest fact in the area.**
- Effect size: AQR systematic 5%-OTM 1-mo SPX put-buy (1985-2020, scaled to 10% vol): -6.4%/yr geometric, Sharpe -0.61, max drawdown -92%, realized skew +3.5, equity correl -0.64 — i.e. it bleeds every decade despite 1987/1998/2001/2008/2020. CBOE PPUT (S&P + 5% OTM put): 6.64% CAGR / Sharpe 0.33 vs S&P 9.80%/0.49 (a ~3%/yr drag). CBOE Eurekahedge Tail Risk Index (live managers since 2008): ~-2%/yr full sample, ~-8%/yr through the 2010s. Deep-OTM puts CAN pay 5-10x (400-900%) in a crash but usually expire worthless. Trend-following is a cheaper hedge: +8.7%/yr, Sharpe 0.84, MDD -35%, equity correl -0.08, profitable in 9 of 10 worst equity months.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Israelov (2019) 'Pathetic Protection' and Israelov-Nielsen 'Still Not Cheap' confirm put protection remained ineffective/expensive through the late 2010s; AQR 2020 update reaffirms post-COVID. Robust across moneyness (5/10/20% OTM) and maturities.
- Cites: Ilmanen, Thapar, Tummala & Villalon 2020, 'Tail Risk Hedging: Contrasting Put and Trend Strategies', AQR (Put -6.4%/yr, Sharpe -0.61, MDD -92%; Trend +8.7%/Sharpe 0.84); Israelov 2019, 'Pathetic Protection: The Elusive Benefits of Protective Puts', Journal of Alternative Investments; Bondarenko 2019 (PPUT statistics)

**Cross-sectional equity option-skew signals (volatility smirk / skew, risk-neutral skewness, RNS term structure) genuinely predict future stock returns, but predictability is concentrated in hard-to-arbitrage names and short horizons.**
- Effect size: Xing-Zhang-Zhao (2010) volatility smirk (OTM-put IV minus ATM-call IV): steepest-smirk minus flattest stocks underperform by ~10.9%/yr risk-adjusted, persists ~6 months. Risk-neutral skewness long-short: FFC alpha ~55 bps/month (Stilger/Kostakis type, 1996-2012). RNS term-spread (short minus long RNS): low-spread minus high-spread decile ~14.6-19.3%/yr. Smirk steepness also forecasts negative earnings surprises and crash risk.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: In-sample mostly 1996-2012/2018. Predictive direction reconfirmed in 2020s working papers, but raw alphas have shrunk; signals load heavily on small, illiquid, expensive-to-short stocks where the option market leads price discovery.
- Cites: Xing, Zhang & Zhao 2010, 'What Does Individual Option Volatility Smirk Tell Us About Future Equity Returns?', JFQA 45(3):641-662; Stilger, Kostakis & Poon 2017, 'What Does Risk-Neutral Skewness Tell Us About Future Stock Returns?', Management Science 63(6) (~55 bps/mo); Bali, Hu & Murray / RNS term-structure literature, 'Information Content of the Term Structure of Risk-Neutral Skewness', J. Financial Economics (2020)

**Most cross-sectional option-skew/vol-spread anomalies do NOT survive realistic option transaction costs, and decayed ~50% after publication — the canonical data-snooping/cost trap of this area.**
- Effect size: McLean & Pontiff (2016): post-publication anomaly returns ~50% smaller. Multiple replications: volatility-spread and skew sorting strategies 'generate minimal profits net of fees and become unprofitable after institutional trading costs,' and remain unprofitable even in low-fee stock subsamples once option bid-ask/slippage are charged. Option effective spreads of 3-10%+ of premium dwarf the gross alpha for OTM names.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Cost/decay critiques intensified 2019-2024; option-implied signals are especially fragile because the tradable instrument (the option itself) has the widest spreads.
- Cites: McLean & Pontiff 2016, 'Does Academic Research Destroy Stock Return Predictability?', Journal of Finance 71(1):5-32; Chen & Zimmermann 2022, 'Publication Bias in Asset Pricing Research', arXiv:2209.13623; Muravyev/Goyenko-type option-cost replication studies (volatility-spread/skew net-of-cost)

**The variance/skew premium is overwhelmingly a DOWNSIDE-variance premium; the upside-variance premium is small and statistically insignificant — so the harvestable edge is specifically selling crash/left-tail insurance, not symmetric vol.**
- Effect size: Feunou, Jahan-Parvar & Okou (2018): downside VRP is the dominant, positively-and-significantly-priced component of the equity premium; upside VRP is negative and insignificant except in turmoil. Their difference is a clean skewness risk premium (SRP). SRP predicts market returns at 4-12 week horizons with adjusted R² comparable to VRP (~2.3% vs ~3.65% at k=6).
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Decomposition extended to global equity markets (Held et al. 2020) and reconfirmed post-2018; directionally stable.
- Cites: Feunou, Jahan-Parvar & Okou 2018, 'Downside Variance Risk Premium', Journal of Financial Econometrics 16(3):341-383; Held, Kapraun, Omachel & Thimme 2020, 'Up- and Downside Variance Risk Premia in Global Equity Markets', Journal of Banking & Finance

**Crypto has a much larger variance risk premium than equities but a structurally DIFFERENT (often right-tailed) skew, so the equity short-skew playbook must be inverted/adapted; harvesting via selling the risk-reversal or straddle is the favored approach in Deribit-era evidence.**
- Effect size: Almeida, Grith, Miftachov & Wang (2024, Deribit): Bitcoin variance risk premium (BVRP) ~14%/yr vs ~2% for S&P500; Bitcoin return premium ~66%/yr; Bitcoin Sharpe ~0.8 (≈2x S&P500). Crucially ~39% of the BTC premium comes from large POSITIVE returns (+20% to +60%) vs <1/3 from positive returns for S&P500; downside (-1 to -3 sigma) returns explain only ~1/3 of the BTC premium. Deribit research (2019-2022): IV > 30-day RV ~70% of the time; contango VRP ~+15 vol points; selling the risk-reversal gives the best risk-adjusted returns (optimal ~75-80% strategy + 20-25% spot); short ATM straddle (2.5% delta-hedge band) strong even ex-Black-Thursday. Crypto skew flips sign within days/hours (e.g., BTC 1-week 25d skew -2.6% -> +10.1% in a week).
- Strength: moderate · Recency: All evidence is post-2019 and specifically post-2021 (Deribit options + DVOL era). Crypto is the least-arbitraged, highest-premium frontier but has tiny effective sample sizes (few crash events) and severe regime instability.
- Cites: Almeida, Grith, Miftachov & Wang 2025, 'Risk Premia in the Bitcoin Market', arXiv:2410.15195v2 (BVRP ~14%, BP ~66%, SR ~0.8, 39% from +20-60% returns); Deribit Insights 2023, 'Bitcoin Options: Finding Edge in Four Years of Volatility Regimes' (IV>RV ~70%, contango VRP ~+15 vpts, short risk-reversal best); Alexander & Imeraj 2021 / Winkel & Härdle 2023, Bitcoin VIX & variance risk premium

**Crypto cross-sectional tail/skew signals exist but are noisy and partly opposite to equities: lottery/MAX-skew demand drives OVER-pricing of right-skewed coins, while downside-risk exposure earns a positive premium.**
- Effect size: Downside-risk (low minus high) sorts: significantly positive high-minus-low spread (downside beta priced). MAX/lottery: monthly horizon, high-MAX coins underperform (overpricing); but at 1-month skew the SIGN reverses vs the 12-month skew sort (most positively-skewed coins outperform short-horizon). Weekly MAX decile spread ~3.03% raw / ~1.99% risk-adjusted in early samples. Skewness risk priced in cross-section (Jia et al. 2024).
- Strength: weak · Recency: 2021-2025 working papers; results sensitive to lookback window (1m vs 12m flips sign), universe survivorship, and the violent 2022 drawdown. High decay risk.
- Cites: Dobrynskaya 2024, 'Downside Risk and the Cross-Section of Cryptocurrency Returns', J. Banking & Finance; Jia et al. 2024, 'Skewness Risk and the Cross-Section of Cryptocurrency Returns', J. International Financial Markets; Lottery/MAX-effect crypto literature, Financial Innovation 2021 (weekly MAX spread ~3.03%/1.99%)

### Testable hypotheses
- H1 (crypto VRP harvest, our core edge): On Deribit BTC/ETH IV surfaces + DVOL (2021-2026), DVOL (or 30d ATM IV) systematically exceeds subsequent 30d realized vol by a large margin (~10-15 vol points, positive >65% of windows). Test: build daily IV-RV spread series; regress forward realized on DVOL; a delta-hedged short-straddle / short-DVOL proxy earns positive gross return with Sharpe ~0.8-1.5 but a deeply negative skew/left tail concentrated in the largest down-moves.
- H2 (crypto skew is right-tailed, invert the equity prior): Using Deribit risk-reversals (25d call IV minus put IV), BTC RR is positive a meaningful fraction of the time and a positive/rising RR predicts continued positive drift (informed-trading channel), unlike equities where steep put-skew predicts negative returns. Test: sign and predictive sign of RR on forward 1d-7d returns; compare BTC vs ETH (ETH more call-skewed/right-tailed per Week-30-2025 data).
- H3 (short risk-reversal beats short straddle in crypto): A systematic short-risk-reversal (sell the rich wing) on BTC/ETH has higher risk-adjusted return and smaller tail than naked short straddle, per Deribit's regime study. Test net of Deribit taker fees + funding on the delta hedge using our perp funding history.
- H4 (funding rate as a crypto skew/tail proxy when no options): On 228 perps x 23k hrs funding + Coinalyze OI/liquidations, extreme positive funding (crowded longs) precedes negative skew/left-tail realizations (long liquidation cascades). Test: does the cross-sectional/time-series funding extreme predict subsequent realized downside semivariance and liquidation spikes? This gives a tail signal for the 47 coins without listed options.
- H5 (equity smirk cross-section, cost-honest): On S&P500 names we can proxy a crude put-skew/'fear' signal from intraday LOB-implied downside pressure or from FnSpID news-sentiment left-tail; sorting on the most negatively-skewed-expected names should NOT survive realistic costs at the single-name level. Falsify the claim that any equity skew cross-section is harvestable for us given we lack single-name option data.
- H6 (VRP timing on SPY): Using a free VIX feed + SPY realized vol, the VRP (VIX^2 - RV^2) positively predicts forward 1-month SPY returns with monthly R² in the 2-8% band; out-of-sample R² is positive but small and fragile (turns negative in crowded-vol regimes like 2023-24). Test as a market-timing overlay, not a standalone alpha.
- H7 (hidden-left-tail accounting): For any short-vol/short-skew strategy we build, the ratio of (gross Sharpe) to (Sharpe after charging downside margin capital + the single worst 1% of days) collapses by >50%; the 'edge' is largely a risk-transfer fee, not a market inefficiency. Quantify ES(1%) and max 1-day loss explicitly.
- H8 (skew as crash early-warning, not return alpha): Rapid steepening of BTC/ETH put skew (RR diving negative) or a DVOL spike has predictive power for near-term drawdown probability (crash timing) even if it has no unconditional return alpha — testable as a regime/de-risking filter on our crypto book.

### Harvest strategies
- Crypto short-volatility carry (PRIMARY, most testable on our data): systematically sell Deribit BTC/ETH ~1-week and ~1-month ATM straddles, delta-hedge with perps at a ~2.5% band. Expected gross Sharpe ~0.8-1.5 (IV>RV ~70%, contango VRP ~+15 vpts). Cost drag: Deribit option taker fee ~0.03% of underlying (capped) per leg + perp hedge funding + slippage on the LOB; tail risk is the binding constraint (size to survive a -40% gap). Hold ~70-90% notional in the straddle + 10-30% spot per Deribit's optimal-allocation finding.
- Crypto short-risk-reversal (sell the expensive wing): when |RR25| is large, sell the rich side (sell calls in positive-RR/greedy regimes, sell puts in negative-RR/fear regimes), delta-neutral. Deribit evidence: best risk-adjusted of the option strategies, smaller tail than naked straddle. Costs as above; works best in negative spot-vol-correlation regimes (~65% of time).
- Funding-rate carry as a skew/tail proxy on optionless coins: short the most extremely-positive-funding perps (crowded longs = embedded left-tail) / long extreme-negative-funding, sized for liquidation-cascade risk. Uses our 228-perp funding + Coinalyze liquidation data directly. This is a synthetic skew-premium harvest where no options exist.
- Equity VRP market-timing overlay (NOT single-name): scale SPY/QQQ net exposure up when VRP (VIX^2 - SPY RV^2) is high, down when low/negative. Cheap to run (monthly rebalance of an ETF/future), R² ~2-8%; treat as a modest beta-timing tilt, not standalone alpha. Free VIX data required.
- Tail-hedge replacement via trend, not puts (defensive sizing): if the program wants downside protection, AQR's evidence says a multi-asset trend overlay (+8.7%/yr, Sharpe 0.84, equity-correl -0.08, up in 9/10 worst equity months) dominates systematic put-buying (-6.4%/yr) on cost AND reliability. On crypto, a fast trend/momentum or vol-target de-risking rule is the analogue of the cheap tail hedge.
- AVOID as standalone alpha: systematic protective-put buying (negative carry by design), and single-name equity skew/vol-spread long-short (dies after option transaction costs and ~50% post-publication decay; we also lack single-name option data).

### Pitfalls
- Peso/hidden-left-tail problem: short-skew Sharpe is paid for by rare catastrophic losses (XIV -90% Feb-2018; VRP -65% Mar-2020; PUT skew -2.1, kurtosis 12.6). A backtest over 2024-02 to 2026-06 in crypto may simply not contain the defining crash — the strategy can look like Sharpe 1.5 free money until it draws down 40-90% in a day. ALWAYS report ES(1%), worst-day loss, and stress a synthetic gap.
- Gross-vs-net collapse on options: option effective spreads are huge (3-10%+ of premium for OTM strikes). The 0DTE evidence shows iron condors flip from +0.77 gross Sharpe to -0.20 net; an all-strategies basket goes 0.81 gross -> 0.25 net. Single-name skew long-shorts go to ~zero net. Never quote a gross option number without a spread/slippage charge.
- Data-snooping across skew measures: there are dozens of skew definitions (smirk, RNS, RR25, term-spread, up/down semivariance, SKEW index). Trying many and reporting the winner is the classic trap; McLean-Pontiff ~50% post-publication decay applies. Pre-register the signal and the cost model.
- Regime instability / sign-flips in crypto: crypto skew flips sign within hours/days, and the cross-sectional skew sort REVERSES between 1-month and 12-month lookbacks. A signal fit on one window/regime will not generalize; 2021 (positive RR) vs 2022 (negative RR) behaved oppositely.
- Tiny effective sample for tail events: 'tail premium' inference rests on a handful of crashes. Crypto has ~1-2 real crash episodes in our window; equity tail studies lean on 1987/2008/2020. t-stats are wildly overstated by serial correlation in big down-days; cluster/bootstrap by event.
- Crowding/capacity decay: the equity short-vol trade re-crowded into 2023-2024 (rolling VRP went negative); 0DTE selling is now heavily populated. Crypto VRP is fatter precisely because it is less arbitraged — but inflows (BTC ETFs, IBIT options, institutional vol funds) are compressing it in real time.
- CBOE SKEW index is a poor crash predictor: high SKEW does NOT reliably forecast crashes (it is a risk-neutral-moment level, mean-reverting and noisy). Do not treat a 'SKEW signal' as a tradable crash forecast.
- Margin/financing and path dependence: short-vol P&L depends on the delta-hedge path and on margin calls at the worst moment; ignoring funding on the perp hedge and exchange margin add-ons overstates returns and understates forced-liquidation risk.
- Survivorship/listing in crypto cross-section: top-50 universe changes; dead/delisted coins with the worst left tails drop out, biasing skew-sort backtests upward.

### Data needed
- HAVE: Deribit BTC/ETH IV surfaces + DVOL (2021-2026) — sufficient to build IV-RV spread, 25d risk-reversal, term-structure-of-skew, and to backtest short-straddle / short-risk-reversal (H1-H3, H8). This is the core testable asset.
- HAVE: 228 perps x ~23k hrs funding + Coinalyze OI/liquidations — for the funding-as-skew-proxy / liquidation-cascade tail signal on optionless coins (H4).
- HAVE: top-50 OHLCV 1h/4h/1d (2024-02 to 2026-06) — for realized-vol, realized-semivariance, realized-skewness, MAX/lottery cross-section (H2, crypto skew sorts).
- HAVE: S&P500 daily/15m/1h, SPY/QQQ LOB, FnSpID sentiment — for VRP timing overlay proxies and a cost-honest test that equity single-name skew is NOT harvestable for us (H5-H6).
- NEED (free): VIX, VVIX, SKEW, VIX term-structure (VIX9D/VIX3M) and VVIX from Cboe's free delayed data / website CSVs and FRED (VIXCLS); SPX/SPY realized vol we can compute. Enables the equity VRP/skew timing work without paid OptionMetrics.
- NEED (free, harder): single-name US equity option-implied vols / skew — OptionMetrics (IvyDB) is the standard but paid; free partial substitutes: ORATS/MarketChameleon free tiers, Nasdaq/Cboe end-of-day samples, or scrape Yahoo/Tradier option chains to build a smirk proxy. Required for any genuine equity smirk/RNS cross-section (otherwise H5 stays a falsification, not a strategy).
- NEED (to-be-sourced, free): FX spot/forward + rate differentials (for FX risk-reversal skew premium — the classic carry/skew link) from central-bank/Investing.com/Stooq; commodities futures term structure from CME free settlements / Nasdaq Data Link free sets / Stooq — to test whether the skew premium generalizes cross-asset.
- NEED: longer crypto options history pre-2021 if obtainable (it largely does not exist) — flag that crypto tail inference is fundamentally sample-starved; supplement with cross-coin pooling and event-bootstrap rather than more calendar time.

### Adversarial verification — reliability: **medium**
_Net-of-cost reality:_ Blunt take: the area is real as PHYSICS (insurance is priced, IV>RV on average, the left tail is genuinely fat) but mostly mirage as a NET-OF-COST, FORWARD alpha. Three hard truths. (1) Selling the premium: gross Sharpes (PUT 0.65, short-straddle baskets 0.8-1.5, crypto 0.8-1.5) are systematically overstated because they ignore (a) option effective spreads of 3-10%+ of premium, (b) downside margin capital, and (c) the defining crash that may be absent from any short backtest. The 0DTE evidence (iron condors +0.77 gross -> -0.20 net; baskets 0.81 -> 0.25 net) is the honest template: charge spreads + slippage + a synthetic gap and most of the edge evaporates, leaving a risk-transfer fee, not an inefficiency. The PUT index's 2020/2021/2023 upside misses (2.1 vs 18.4; 21.8 vs 28.7; 14.3 vs 26.3) show even the survivors deliver poor net deals in calm-up markets. (2) Buying the premium (crash insurance): the negative-carry direction is real for naive near-ATM rolled puts, but the analyst's flagship -6.4%/yr 'most honest fact' is OVERSTATED — AQR's own footnote shows Put is gross-of-cost while Trend is net, and the figure reverses for deep-OTM externally-funded convex hedges (Spitznagel). Trend as the cheaper hedge is the more defensible conclusion than 'puts always bleed.' (3) Cross-sectional skew signals: net-of-cost ~zero is the best-supported statement here — option spreads dwarf the alpha and much of the 'predictability' is a stock-borrow-fee artifact (drops >=2/3 excluding high-fee names) compounded by ~50% post-publication decay. (4) Crypto is the only place with a plausibly fat NET premium today precisely because it is least-arbitraged — but it is sample-starved (1-2 crashes), regime-unstable (skew flips sign), and visibly compressing in 2024-2026 (DVOL 70->45, equity-like 'put premium' regime, -53% Feb-2026 drawdown). Treat the crypto VRP harvest as a decaying, tail-exposed carry trade that must be sized to survive a -40% to -90% gap, with ES(1%) and worst-day loss reported explicitly — not as a Sharpe-1.5 free lunch.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Equity index options embed a persistent variance/skew premium: 1-month implied vol averages ~4.2 vol points above subsequent realized (VIX 19.3 vs RV 15.1, 1990-2018), positive in 27 of 29 years; OTM puts are systematically richer than OTM calls. — This is the best-supported claim in the area and survives adversarial scrutiny in DIRECTION, though the magnitude is state-dependent and has compressed recently. Independent sources confirm IV exceeded RV ~87% of the time over 1990-2011 (Cambridge Associates) and the VIX-minus-RV spread has been positive every year since 1990 except 2008, with a typical 2-4 vol-point average — consistent with the cited Bondarenko/Carr-Wu/BTZ figures. The key caveat the prior demands: the premium is NOT a constant free lunch. It is largest right after vol spikes and shrank materially in 2023-2024 as the short-vol trade re-crowded (multiple sources note rolling VRP went low/negative because realized vol rose alongside implied). So 'decades-stable' is true on average but the harvestable size is regime-dependent and currently compressed.
- **[WEAKENED]** Buying systematic OTM index puts ('crash insurance') has a large persistent NEGATIVE expected return: AQR's 5%-OTM 1-mo SPX put-buy bled -6.4%/yr (Sharpe -0.61, MDD -92%, skew +3.5, equity-corr -0.64) over 1985-2020, and trend-following (+8.7%/yr, Sharpe 0.84) is a cheaper, more reliable tail hedge. — I read AQR's primary 2020 paper directly and the headline numbers are reported EXACTLY as cited (Put -6.4% geom, Sharpe -0.61, MDD -92%, skew +3.5, EqCor -0.64; Trend +8.7%, Sharpe 0.84, EqCor -0.08, up in 9 of 10 worst months). BUT two adversarial findings cut hard against using this as 'the most brutally honest fact.' (1) AQR's OWN footnote 5 states Put returns are shown 'before (relatively high) trading costs as well as fees,' while Trend is shown 'after estimated trading costs' — the comparison is asymmetric and BIASED AGAINST puts; the Put series is also levered 1.67x to hit 10% vol, amplifying the negative geometric drag. (2) The Spitznagel/Universa critique (corroborated by an independent 2008-2025 replication) shows the result is framing-dependent: AQR tested ~5% OTM (near-the-money, delta ~-0.35) puts in an allocation-REDUCING frame; deep-OTM (40-45% OTM) convex puts funded EXTERNALLY (Universa-style, 100% equity retained) beat SPY in the same window (+16.7%/yr vs +10.7% at a 3.3% budget; -30% vs -52% drawdown). The negative-carry direction for near-ATM rolled puts is genuine and well-replicated (Israelov 'Pathetic Protection,' 'Still Not Cheap'), but the blanket 'crash insurance has deeply negative expected return' is sensitive to moneyness, leverage, and the cost convention — net of AQR's own footnote, the Put-vs-Trend gap is somewhat overstated.
- **[WEAKENED]** Harvesting the premium via systematic put-writing earns attractive GROSS risk-adjusted returns (CBOE PUT Sharpe ~0.65, 1986-2018) but is fundamentally a short-left-tail strategy paid for by catastrophic fat-tailed drawdowns (skew -2.1, kurtosis 12.6, XIV -90% Feb-2018, VRP ~-65% Mar-2020). — The TAIL-RISK half of this claim is fully confirmed and arguably understated. XIV lost ~96-97% (not just 90%) in a single session on 5-Feb-2018 (VIX 17.3->37.3) and was terminated; the CFA Institute's own retrospective frames it as 'the failure of short volatility products.' The fat-tailed-drawdown thesis is exactly right. What I am WEAKENING is the implicit 'attractive returns' framing: (a) the 0.65 Sharpe is a GROSS, pre-cost, pre-margin-capital number from a vendor (CBOE/Bondarenko) study; (b) more importantly, in the most recent decade the PUT index has been a poor deal even before tail events — it returned 2.1% vs SPX 18.4% (2020), 21.8% vs 28.7% (2021), and 14.3% vs 26.3% (2023), capturing little upside while retaining left-tail exposure; and (c) the short-vol space has crowded dramatically (0DTE now ~45% of SPX option volume, ~1.5M contracts/day), which compresses the premium and raises gap risk. So 'attractive Sharpe' is a gross-of-cost, full-sample artifact; the realized recent experience and the crowding both argue the net harvestable edge is materially smaller than 0.65.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Most cross-sectional option-skew / vol-spread anomalies (smirk, RNS, RNS term-structure) do NOT survive realistic option transaction costs and decayed ~50% post-publication — the canonical data-snooping/cost trap of this area. — This is the strongest adversarial claim and it holds up — arguably it is the single most reliable statement in the whole findings set. McLean-Pontiff (2016, JF) independently verified: portfolio returns 26% lower out-of-sample and 58% lower post-publication across 97 predictors, with larger decay for high-in-sample-return, illiquid, high-idio-risk predictors — precisely where option-skew signals live. On costs, independent option-microstructure work (the JFE 2025 'Why does options market information predict stock returns?' line, plus Goyenko/Muravyev/Christoffersen) finds volatility-spread and skew predictability falls by AT LEAST two-thirds when high-borrow-fee stocks are excluded, and the signals 'generate minimal profits net of fees and become unprofitable after institutional trading costs' — i.e., much of the apparent alpha is a stock-borrow/short-fee artifact and option bid-ask, not exploitable edge. The only nuance (Chen-Zimmermann 2022): pure publication bias is bounded (OOS decay implies pub-bias explains 0-46%, not necessarily a full 50%), and most anomalies do replicate in-sample — so '~50% decay' is a reasonable headline but blends genuine arbitrage/learning with cost effects rather than proving fraud. Net: directionally confirmed, and the net-of-cost-zero conclusion is well-supported.
- **[WEAKENED]** Crypto is a structurally different, least-arbitraged, high-premium frontier: Bitcoin VRP ~14%/yr (vs ~2% S&P), return premium ~66%/yr, Sharpe ~0.8, skew frequently POSITIVE (right-tailed; ~39% of BTC premium from +20-60% moves), so sell the risk-reversal / sell straddles (IV>RV ~70%, contango VRP ~+15 vpts). — The in-sample facts are sourced correctly (Almeida-Grith-Miftachov-Wang: BVRP ~14% vs ~2%, BP ~66%, and the right-tail decomposition where negative -1 to -3 sigma returns explain only ~1/3 of the BTC premium). But three adversarial findings weaken its use as a FORWARD edge. (1) Sample-starved & dated: the core paper's data ENDS December 2022 and the authors themselves caveat that 'Bitcoin has reached a broader user base and its volatility dynamics have evolved' since — there are essentially 1-2 crash episodes (2020 COVID, 2022 FTX) in the whole window, so t-stats/Sharpes are massively overstated by serial correlation in down-days. (2) The skew is NOT stably positive — it flips with regime: strong CALL skew in the 2021 bull, then NEGATIVE (equity-like put skew) through 2022's FTX collapse; it can flip sign within days. So 'invert the equity prior' is only half-right — in stress, crypto skew behaves like equities. (3) The premium is COMPRESSING in real time exactly as the adversarial prior predicts: by late-2025/2026, BVIV/DVOL fell from ~70% to ~45%, realized vol dropped, and a 'put premium'/covered-call (equity-like) regime emerged as ETFs/IBIT options and institutional vol funds arbitraged it. Crucially, the hidden left tail did show up: Bitcoin fell ~53% into a Feb-2026 bottom. So the 14%/66%/0.8 figures are real but regime-conditional, sample-fragile, and decaying — not a durable structural frontier.

---

## FX carry and currency factors  `fx_carry`

The currency carry trade (long high-yield, short low-yield) is the best-documented FX anomaly: gross Sharpe of roughly 0.6-0.8 on the academic 1976-2010 cross-section (LRV/Menkhoff), but it is a compensated-risk premium, not free alpha — returns are strongly negatively skewed and crash during funding-liquidity/risk-off events (2008, Aug-2024 yen unwind). Post-2008 the premium decayed materially: G10-only carry survives costs only at a modest ~0.3-0.5 net Sharpe with -30%+ drawdowns; the high gross Sharpes require illiquid EM currencies where bid-ask spreads (50-200+ bps round trip) and capacity (price impact kills it above a few hundred million AUM) erode most of the edge. Dollar factor (timing aggregate USD exposure off the average forward discount) is a distinct, lower-correlation source with conditional Sharpes up to ~1.0+ but heavy macro-data-snooping risk. Currency value (real-exchange-rate reversal) and momentum are real but weaker (~0.3-0.5 net) and momentum is largely eaten by costs. The crypto perpetual-funding "carry" is the same economic trade with a far larger, faster-decaying premium (full-sample Sharpe ~6.5, falling to ~4 in 2024, negative in 2025) — directly testable on our funding-rate data and the most actionable item here.

### Findings

**The cross-sectional FX carry trade (HML: long highest-yield, short lowest-yield currency portfolios, monthly rebal) earns a positive premium with gross Sharpe ~0.6-0.8 on the canonical academic cross-section, driven by the forward discount. It is the slope factor that prices the currency cross-section (LRV).**
- Effect size: LRV (2011 RFS): HML carry mean excess return ~6.0%/yr, vol ~9.5%, gross Sharpe ~0.63 (developed+EM, 1983-2009). Menkhoff et al. (2012 JF) similar. Long-history (Doskov/Chen, 1900-2012 / 1788+): much lower, gross Sharpe ~0.2-0.4. After transaction costs the high-minus-low return spread compresses ~1.2 pts (LRV note ~4.8% net spread vs ~6% gross).
- Strength: strong · Recency: Pre-2008 Sharpes 0.6-0.8; post-2008 decayed sharply — multiple studies show funding risk became the dominant driver only after 2008, lower-vol regime compressed the premium, and G10-only net Sharpe is ~0.3-0.5. No crypto analogue for cross-sectional FX carry, but the funding-premium logic carries over (see crypto finding).
- Cites: Lustig, Roussanov, Verdelhan 2011, 'Common Risk Factors in Currency Markets', Review of Financial Studies 24(11) (NBER w14082); Menkhoff, Sarno, Schmeling, Schrimpf 2012, 'Carry Trades and Global Foreign Exchange Volatility', Journal of Finance 67(2):681-718; Doskov & Swinkels / Accominotti et al. 2019 long-history; Chen 2024 SSRN 4692257 (carry equal-weighted Sharpe ~0.39, 1788+); Quantpedia 'FX Carry Trade' (DB Carry USD index 1989-2009): Sharpe 0.29, 7.27% ret, 9.6% vol, MaxDD -32.05%

**Carry returns are negatively skewed with severe crash risk ('going up by the stairs, down by the elevator'); crashes coincide with spikes in global FX volatility and contractions in funding liquidity. The premium is partly compensation for this tail risk, and global FX volatility is a priced risk factor that explains the carry cross-section.**
- Effect size: Brunnermeier-Nagel-Pedersen (2009): carry returns load negatively on innovations to funding liquidity and VIX; skewness strongly negative. Menkhoff et al. (2012): global FX vol carries a significant negative price of risk and explains most of the HML carry spread (R^2 high in cross-sectional pricing). Single-day crash example: 5 Aug 2024 BOJ +15bps hike, yen carry unwind -> Nikkei -12.4%, VIX intraday >65.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Mechanism re-confirmed in Aug-2024 yen carry unwind (estimated $0.5-2T of yen-funded carry, ~50% unwound per UBS). Same funding-spiral dynamic appears in crypto: long-funding regimes unwind violently in deleveraging cascades (liquidations), so our Coinalyze liquidation + funding data can directly test the crash mechanism.
- Cites: Brunnermeier, Nagel, Pedersen 2009, 'Carry Trades and Currency Crashes', NBER Macro Annual / NBER w14473; Menkhoff, Sarno, Schmeling, Schrimpf 2012, JF 67(2):681-718 (global FX volatility factor); Daniel, Hodrick, Lu 2017, 'The Carry Trade: Risks and Drawdowns', NBER w20433; Reuters/UBS Aug-2024 yen unwind coverage; AMRO yen carry reversal note

**The 'dollar carry trade' / dollar factor — timing aggregate long/short USD exposure against ALL foreign currencies using the average forward discount (and US industrial-production cycle) — is a distinct return source largely uncorrelated with cross-sectional carry, with strong conditional predictability.**
- Effect size: Lustig-Roussanov-Verdelhan (2014 JFE 'Countercyclical Currency Risk Premia'): average forward discount + US IP growth forecast up to ~25% of 1-yr dollar return variation; dollar-carry conditional Sharpe up to ~1.0-1.4 vs unconditional ~0.44; a naive sign-of-individual-forward-discount version only ~0.3. Koijen-Moskowitz-Pedersen-Vrugt (2018 JFE): global cross-asset carry avg Sharpe ~0.74; carry-timing global combo ~0.9.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: In-sample predictability strong through ~2010s; out-of-sample Sharpes are sensitive to the macro signal and prone to overfitting/regime shifts (ZIRP era compressed cross-country rate dispersion). Crypto analogue = aggregate market-wide funding level as a timing signal for net long/short basket exposure (testable on our 228-perp funding panel).
- Cites: Lustig, Roussanov, Verdelhan 2014, 'Countercyclical Currency Risk Premia', JFE 111(3) (NBER w16427); Koijen, Moskowitz, Pedersen, Vrugt 2018, 'Carry', Journal of Financial Economics 127(2):197-225; Quantpedia 'Dollar Carry Trade'

**Currency value (long currencies whose real exchange rate is undervalued, short overvalued — a multi-year mean-reversion) is a real, lower-correlation factor; adjusting the real exchange rate for fundamentals (productivity, net foreign assets, output gap, export quality) sharpens the signal.**
- Effect size: Menkhoff, Sarno, Schmeling, Schrimpf 2017 (RFS 'Currency Value'): raw real-exchange-rate value strategy Sharpe ~0.5/yr; fundamentals-adjusted value Sharpe ~0.8-0.9 (gains come mainly from lower volatility / less noisy signal). Low/negative correlation with carry and momentum -> diversification value in a multi-factor FX sleeve.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Value is slow-moving (low turnover -> cost-robust) but its premium is noisy and period-dependent; limited clean OOS post-2017 and modest in G10-only. No direct crypto analogue (no PPP), though long-horizon mean reversion of coin prices is a loose parallel — weak.
- Cites: Menkhoff, Sarno, Schmeling, Schrimpf 2017, 'Currency Value', Review of Financial Studies 30(2):416-441 (SSRN 2492082); Asness, Moskowitz, Pedersen 2013, 'Value and Momentum Everywhere', JF 68(3)

**Currency momentum (rank on past 1-12m returns) generates large GROSS returns but is heavily concentrated in illiquid, high-turnover currencies, so most of the profit is consumed by transaction costs; net profitability has deteriorated out-of-sample.**
- Effect size: Menkhoff, Sarno, Schmeling, Schrimpf 2012 (JFE 'Currency Momentum Strategies'): up to ~10%/yr gross for top spread portfolios, but profits concentrated where bid-ask is widest; net materially smaller. Quantpedia momentum factor proxy: 7.61% ret, 10.22% vol, gross Sharpe ~0.3, MaxDD -45.9%. EM momentum (Pojarliev/others, 1985-2009): ~1-3%/yr net, declining, money-losing after costs in last 5 yrs of sample.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Among the weakest survivors post-cost; several studies say standard FX momentum no longer profits in major rates on recent data (some life left in EM). Crypto cross-sectional momentum (top-50 coins) is a much stronger, directly testable analogue on our OHLCV data — distinct from FX.
- Cites: Menkhoff, Sarno, Schmeling, Schrimpf 2012, 'Currency Momentum Strategies', JFE 106(3):660-684 (BIS WP 366); Burnside, Eichenbaum, Rebelo work on FX momentum/carry costs; Quantpedia 'Currency Momentum Factor'

**Transaction costs and capacity, not signal decay alone, are the binding constraint. Realistic FX costs and price impact convert paper Sharpes into modest live ones, especially in EM where the gross premium lives.**
- Effect size: Round-trip spreads: G10 spot/forward ~1-5 bps (liquid), EM ~20-200+ bps and widen sharply in crises. Practitioner study (Lou et al. / SDX 2024 JFE): a carry strategy with gross Sharpe ~0.79 / net ~0.74 at small size sees Sharpe fall to ~0.5 at ~$80M AUM and goes UNPROFITABLE at >~$660M AUM once price impact dominates. G10-only augmented carry: Sharpe rises only ~0.45->0.53 (insignificant).
- Strength: strong · Recency: Capacity/cost drag is structural and if anything worse post-2008 (less dealer balance sheet, episodic EM liquidity). Mirrors crypto: funding 'carry' looks huge gross but exchange fees, slippage, borrow, and funding-flip risk compress net returns and capacity.
- Cites: Lou, Zhao et al. 2024, 'Importance of transaction costs for asset allocation in foreign exchange markets', JFE (S0304405X24001090); Quantpedia FX Carry/Momentum cost notes; Menkhoff et al. 2012 (bid-ask adjusted 1976-2010)

**The crypto perpetual-funding 'carry' (delta-neutral: long spot, short perpetual to harvest positive funding) is the same economics as FX carry with a vastly larger but rapidly decaying premium and the identical crash/unwind tail.**
- Effect size: Cryptocurrency-as-asset-class study (arXiv 2510.14435, 2025): crypto carry full-sample (Aug-2020 to May-2025) annualized Sharpe ~6.45, driven by funding (mean ~8%/yr, vol ~0.8%); Sharpe falls to ~4.06 in 2024 and turns NEGATIVE in 2025 as the premium competes away. Perps are >98% of BTC futures volume.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Strongest and most recent decay signal in this whole area, and exactly what our data covers (228 perps x ~23k hrs funding + Coinalyze + Deribit). Net-of-cost capacity-constrained; Ethena-style delta-neutral products ($14B) depend on it, so crowding/decay risk is live.
- Cites: 'Cryptocurrency as an Investable Asset Class: Coming of Age' 2025, arXiv:2510.14435; Koijen-Moskowitz-Pedersen-Vrugt 2018 JFE (carry as cross-asset concept)

### Testable hypotheses
- H1 (crypto carry, primary): On our 228-perp x ~23k-hour funding panel, a delta-neutral strategy that each rebalance shorts the top-decile-funding perps (long spot/short perp) and is flat the rest earns positive net return after taker fees + slippage; net Sharpe is high 2022-2023 but declines monotonically into 2024-2025 and turns near-zero/negative by 2025 — replicating the arXiv 2510.14435 decay (full ~6.5 -> 2024 ~4.0 -> 2025 negative).
- H2 (crypto carry crash mechanism = FX BNP): Sort hours by aggregate/cross-sectional funding level; the highest-funding (most crowded long) regimes exhibit significantly more negative forward skewness and cluster with Coinalyze liquidation spikes and DVOL jumps — i.e., the carry premium is paid for crash risk, mirroring Brunnermeier-Nagel-Pedersen.
- H3 (FX carry from FRED, signal only): Build monthly G10 carry signals from FRED policy/interbank rate differentials (CIP => forward discount ~ rate diff). Long top-3 / short bottom-3 yields, P&L = rate-diff carry + spot FX change. Test whether gross Sharpe is ~0.4-0.6 pre-2008 and drops toward ~0.2-0.3 post-2010, and whether it goes negative in risk-off months (proxy: VIX/DXY spikes).
- H4 (dollar factor): Using FRED spot DXY/USD pairs + average G10 forward discount, the average-forward-discount signal predicts next-month aggregate USD basket return with positive but unstable OOS Sharpe; predictability concentrates in high-US-rate-relative regimes and collapses in the 2012-2021 ZIRP window.
- H5 (value, slow/cost-robust): A real-exchange-rate value signal (vs long-run mean) on G10 produces a low-turnover ~0.3-0.5 gross Sharpe whose net Sharpe barely moves with costs (turnover-robust), and is roughly uncorrelated with the H3 carry sleeve.
- H6 (momentum is a cost artifact): A 1-12m FX momentum signal shows positive GROSS Sharpe that becomes statistically indistinguishable from zero (or negative) once realistic bid-ask is applied, and the gross profit concentrates in the widest-spread currencies — confirming the cost-artifact thesis.
- H7 (cross-asset carry crowding): Periods when FX carry and crypto carry are simultaneously richly priced (high yield dispersion AND high aggregate crypto funding) precede larger joint drawdowns, indicating a shared global-risk/funding-liquidity factor.

### Harvest strategies
- Crypto delta-neutral funding carry (most actionable on our data): long spot (or low/zero-funding venue) + short perpetual on coins with persistently positive funding; collect 8-hourly funding. Cost drag: taker ~5-10 bps/side per entry+exit, maker ~0-2 bps; spot-perp slippage; periodic rebal cost; borrow on spot leg. Net edge is real only when funding APR comfortably exceeds round-trip + carry-flip risk; size-limited by perp OI/liquidation depth. Use Coinalyze OI/liq + Deribit DVOL as a regime de-risking overlay (cut size when funding crowded and vol rising).
- G10 carry via deliverable forwards/futures (CME FX futures or rolling 1m forwards): long 2-3 highest-yield, short 2-3 lowest-yield G10. Cost drag: ~1-5 bps round trip in liquid G10 + roll cost; modest. Expect net Sharpe ~0.3-0.5 with -25% to -35% drawdowns; pair with a vol/risk-off filter (scale down when global FX vol or VIX spikes) to truncate the left tail.
- Dollar-factor timing: net long/short a G10 basket vs USD based on average forward discount + US macro (IP/PMI). Low turnover, low cost; treat conditional Sharpe claims (>1) skeptically and validate strictly OOS. Best as a diversifier to cross-sectional carry (low correlation).
- Currency value sleeve: long undervalued / short overvalued by real-exchange-rate deviation; very low turnover so cost-robust; modest ~0.3-0.5 gross Sharpe, useful mainly for diversification, not standalone alpha.
- Multi-factor FX combine (carry + value + dollar, vol-targeted ~8-10%): diversification lifts net Sharpe above any single sleeve and dampens carry crashes; this is the AQR 'style premia' template (live QSPIX ~0.37 net over 10y — sobering reality check on net delivery).
- Crash-neutral carry overlay: buy cheap OTM downside protection on the long-yield legs (or risk-reversal hedges) to cut negative skew; in crypto, hold tail puts on BTC/ETH via Deribit. Cost drag reduces mean return but materially improves drawdown/Sharpe-after-tail.

### Pitfalls
- Cost/capacity illusion: the headline 0.6-0.8 FX carry Sharpe lives in illiquid EM currencies; once realistic bid-ask (EM 20-200+ bps) and price impact are applied it collapses, and the strategy is empirically unprofitable above a few hundred million AUM (Lou et al. JFE 2024). Never quote a gross Sharpe without the net-after-cost-and-capacity number.
- Peso problem / survivorship in skew: realized-return backtests understate crash risk because the big unwind may sit outside the sample (pre-2008 backtests missed 2008; pre-2024 missed the yen unwind). Use option-implied skew (risk reversals) where possible; on crypto, account for delisted/blown-up coins and exchanges (FTX) to avoid survivorship bias.
- Regime dependence / structural break post-2008 and during ZIRP: the carry premium is conditional on rate dispersion and funding conditions; a single full-sample Sharpe masks that most of the edge is pre-2008. Always show rolling/sub-period Sharpe.
- Data-snooping the dollar-factor macro signal: average-forward-discount + IP predictability has few independent business cycles in-sample; in-sample R^2 ~25% and conditional Sharpes >1 are highly overfit-prone. Pre-register the signal and test strictly OOS with deflated Sharpe / multiple-testing correction.
- Momentum = transaction-cost artifact: large gross FX-momentum returns concentrate in the widest-spread currencies; net it largely vanishes. Do not report momentum gross Sharpe as harvestable.
- Crypto funding-carry crowding and decay: the ~6.5 Sharpe is a transient, rapidly-arbitraged premium already decaying (negative in 2025) as delta-neutral products (Ethena $14B) crowd in; funding can flip negative and unwinds cascade via liquidations. Model funding-flip + liquidation-gap risk, not just average funding.
- Free-data construction error: FRED has spot FX and policy/interbank rates but limited free FORWARDS, and removed USD LIBOR (Jan-2022). If you proxy carry by rate differentials you implicitly assume CIP — which broke down post-2008 (cross-currency basis), so a pure rate-diff signal misstates true forward-implied carry. Validate against any forward data you can source.
- Funding-rate look-ahead / settlement timing in crypto: funding is paid at fixed marks; using the realized funding to decide the position that earns it is look-ahead. Lag signals to the decision time and use only information available pre-settlement.

### Data needed
- FX spot: FRED (daily USD bilateral rates, category 15 / ~260 series) and Stooq (daily OHLC for majors) — FREE; sufficient for spot-return leg and value/momentum signals.
- FX forwards / forward points (the hard, partly-paid part): needed for true carry P&L and CIP-correct signals. FREE proxies: BIS Data Portal (nominal bilateral rates, ~190 economies) for spot; build forwards from interest-rate parity using FRED rates. Cleaner forwards typically require paid sources (Bloomberg/Refinitiv/Macrosynergy JPMaQS) — flag as a gap.
- Interest-rate differentials: FRED policy rates, T-bill/SOFR, and foreign central-bank/interbank series; BIS for broader coverage. Note USD LIBOR removed from FRED in 2022 — use SOFR/OIS equivalents. FREE.
- Effective exchange rates & long-run value anchor: BIS real/nominal effective exchange rate indices (also mirrored on FRED, e.g. RBUSBIS from 1994) for the currency-value real-exchange-rate signal. FREE.
- Intraday/tick FX (for realistic spread/slippage estimation and execution studies): Dukascopy historical tick export and DataFeed — FREE; use to measure actual bid-ask and impact rather than assuming.
- Transaction-cost reference: BIS Triennial FX Survey for liquidity/turnover by currency; academic bid-ask tables (Menkhoff et al. 2012) for EM spread magnitudes. FREE/published.
- Crypto carry (already in-house, primary test bed): our 228-perp x ~23k-hour funding-rate history, Coinalyze funding/OI/liquidations, top-50 OHLCV 1h/4h/1d (2024-02 to 2026-06), Deribit BTC/ETH IV surfaces + DVOL — sufficient to run H1/H2/H7 end-to-end with realistic fees.
- Risk-off/regime overlays: VIX (Cboe, free delayed), DXY (FRED/Stooq), and our DVOL for crypto — to build the crash filters and test the funding-liquidity crash mechanism.

### Adversarial verification — reliability: **medium**
_Net-of-cost reality:_ Blunt take: the SIGNALS are mostly real, but net-of-cost harvestable alpha here is thin and shrinking, and the analyst's note is solid on direction while occasionally overstating magnitudes and mis-citing. (1) The single best independent reality check is AQR's live QSPIX (the value/momentum/carry/defensive multi-asset 'style premia' template the analyst itself flags): realized since-inception (10/2013) Sharpe of ~0.41 with a -41% max drawdown — a professionally-implemented, cost-aware fund delivering far below paper Sharpes, which caps realistic expectations for any DIY FX-factor sleeve. (2) Cross-sectional FX carry decayed harder than the analyst's '0.3-0.5 net' floor admits — post-GFC realized Sharpes of 0.06-0.25 appear in the literature, the long-history number is 0.2-0.4, and the high gross Sharpes require illiquid EM where 20-200bps round-trip spreads and price impact dominate; treat G10-only net Sharpe as ~0.2-0.4 with -25% to -35% drawdowns, NOT 0.5+. (3) The capacity story is the most misrepresented item: the correct cite (Filippou-Maurer-Pezzo-Taylor 2024 JFE, not 'Lou et al.') actually shows that a properly cost-optimized carry can hold ~0.75 net at $1B AUM — so 'unprofitable above ~$660M' is true only for naive implementations; the binding constraint is implementation skill, not a hard capacity wall. (4) Momentum is the clearest cost artifact — assume ~0 net in majors. (5) The crypto funding 'carry' is the most actionable AND the most cautionary: the gross ~6.45 Sharpe is real in-sample but is a low-vol-denominator, pre-cost number that the source paper itself shows decaying to negative by 2025 as Ethena-style crowding arbitrages it away; net of taker fees/slippage/borrow/funding-flip and capacity-constrained by perp OI, expect a small fraction of the gross, front-loaded into 2022-2023, with violent liquidation-cascade tails — exactly the FX crash mechanism. Across the board, every headline Sharpe should be quoted only with its net, capacity-adjusted, sub-period (pre/post-2008, by-year for crypto) counterpart, and crash/peso risk modeled via option-implied skew rather than realized returns.
- **[CONFIRMED]** The crypto perpetual-funding 'carry' (delta-neutral: long spot, short perp) earns a full-sample annualized Sharpe ~6.45 (Aug-2020 to May-2025), driven by funding (mean ~8%/yr, vol ~0.8%), falling to ~4.06 in 2024 and turning NEGATIVE in 2025 as the premium competes away; perps are >98% of BTC futures volume and Ethena-style delta-neutral products (~$14B) depend on it. — Every number is reproduced verbatim from the cited source on independent fetch. arXiv 2510.14435 ('Cryptocurrency as an Investable Asset Class: Coming of Age', Borri/Liu/Tsyvinski/Wu, forthcoming Annual Review of Financial Economics Vol.18 2026) states full-sample Sharpe 6.45, 'Beginning in 2024, the Sharpe ratio falls to 4.06, and it turns negative in 2025,' funding mean ~8%/vol ~0.8%, perps >98% of BTC futures volume, Ethena ~$14B as of Sep-2025, and explicitly that 'funding-rate premia are neither guaranteed nor permanent.' The analyst's framing (transient, rapidly-arbitraged, crowding/decay risk live) is faithful to the source. CAVEAT for the user's own testing: 6.45 is a GROSS, low-vol-denominator Sharpe — it is fragile to taker fees, slippage, borrow, funding-flip risk, and the very low 0.8% vol denominator inflates the ratio; the headline number is not a net-of-cost capacity-adjusted figure, and the strategy is already negative in the most recent year, consistent with the strong prior that published alpha decays.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Cross-sectional FX carry (HML, long highest-yield/short lowest-yield) earns gross Sharpe ~0.6-0.8 on the canonical academic cross-section (LRV ~6.0% ret, ~9.5% vol, ~0.63), much lower (~0.2-0.4) in long-history samples, and decayed materially post-2008 to a net ~0.3-0.5 in G10. — The in-sample magnitude is corroborated independently: Burnside's NBER work reproduces LRV HML at 6.0% mean, 9.5% std, Sharpe 0.63. Long-history is confirmed exactly: Doskov & Swinkels (1900-2012, 20 currencies) report Sharpe 0.2-0.4, 'markedly lower than above 0.6 for recent samples.' Post-2008 decay is confirmed and, if anything, the analyst's '0.3-0.5 net' floor is OPTIMISTIC: one peer-reviewed study (Int. Rev. Fin. Analysis / S1042443121001670) finds the efficient carry Sharpe falls from 1.08 pre-GFC to 0.25 post-GFC, and a benchmark carry Sharpe of just 0.06 since the crisis; Quantpedia's DB Carry USD index (1989-2009) shows 7.27% ret / 9.6% vol / Sharpe 0.29 / MaxDD -32.05% (matches the analyst's cited figures exactly). Consistent with the adversarial prior: most of the edge is pre-2008 and full-sample Sharpes mask a structural break.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Carry returns are strongly negatively skewed with crash risk concentrated in funding-liquidity/risk-off events; global FX volatility is a priced risk factor that explains the carry cross-section; the Aug-2024 BOJ-driven yen unwind is a fresh confirmation. — Mechanism strongly corroborated and the pricing result is actually STRONGER than the analyst stated: Menkhoff et al. (2012 JF) report their global FX volatility proxy captures MORE THAN 90% of the cross-sectional excess returns across the five carry portfolios (analyst said only 'high R^2'). Negative skewness from sudden unwinds in low-risk-appetite/low-liquidity periods is confirmed across multiple sources (BNP 2009; Accominotti et al.). Aug-2024 yen unwind confirmed as a live re-test: Nikkei -12% in a single day (worst since 1987), ~-20% over Jul31-Aug5, VIX spiking to COVID-era levels; BIS Bulletin 90 characterizes it as procyclical deleveraging/margin-driven (i.e., funding/risk-off). One OVERSTATEMENT to flag: the analyst's '$0.5-2T yen carry, ~50% unwound (UBS)' is at the high end and not robust — BIS Bulletin 90 estimates total FX carry entering the event at only ~JPY 40tn (~$250bn, acknowledged biased down); 'carry trade' size estimates in the press range $250bn-$20tn depending on definition, so the specific figure is cherry-picked.
- **[WEAKENED]** Transaction costs and capacity (not signal decay alone) are the binding constraint: per Lou et al. 2024 JFE, a carry strategy with gross Sharpe ~0.79/net ~0.74 falls to ~0.5 at ~$80M AUM and goes UNPROFITABLE above ~$660M once price impact dominates; G10-only augmented carry rises only ~0.45->0.53 (insignificant). — Two material problems. (1) MISATTRIBUTION: the paper is Filippou, Maurer, Pezzo & Taylor, 'Importance of Transaction Costs for Asset Allocation in Foreign Exchange Markets,' JFE 159 (2024) (SSRN 3143970 / S0304405X24001090) — NOT 'Lou et al.' (2) The headline result is closer to the OPPOSITE of the analyst's spin: the paper's central contribution is that a mean-variance-transaction-cost-optimized (MVTC) implementation RETAINS a net Sharpe of ~0.75 even at $1 BILLION AUM, comparable to the 0.79 gross of simple carry — i.e., smart implementation largely defeats the capacity constraint. The '$80M -> ~0.5' and 'unprofitable above ~$660M' figures describe NAIVE/unoptimized strategies (the paper shows naive carry/momentum/MV portfolios are eroded to unprofitability by price impact). So the directional thesis ('naive EM-heavy carry is capacity-limited; proportional bid-ask is small but volume price-impact bites at size') is SUPPORTED, but the specific capacity numbers are presented misleadingly (as if they were the paper's verdict on carry generally) and the citation is wrong. Net: the binding-constraint claim is real for naive implementations but overstated as a blanket result, and the source attribution fails.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Currency momentum generates large GROSS returns concentrated in illiquid/high-turnover (widest bid-ask) currencies, so net profitability is largely consumed by costs and has deteriorated out-of-sample (a cost artifact, not harvestable). — Directly corroborated by the primary source and recent work. Menkhoff, Sarno, Schmeling & Schrimpf (2012 JFE, 'Currency Momentum Strategies'): momentum profits are skewed toward currencies with high transaction costs and adjusting for bid-ask 'significantly lowers' profitability. The 2024 Filippou et al. JFE paper explicitly lists currency momentum among strategies rendered unprofitable once trading-volume price impact is included. This is among the weakest post-cost survivors in the area; the analyst's 'do not report momentum gross Sharpe as harvestable' pitfall is well-founded. Consistent with the adversarial prior that gross momentum is a transaction-cost mirage.

---

## Commodity roll yield, carry and momentum  `commodity`

Commodity carry (long backwardated / short contangoed futures, i.e. harvesting positive roll yield) and momentum are among the most robust, decades-long, theory-backed cross-asset premia. Over 1877-2015 the interest-rate-adjusted carry/roll component (~2.8%/yr) actually exceeds the spot-return component as a driver of long-run futures returns (Levine-Ooi-Richardson). Classic gross Sharpes are ~0.5-0.6 for single-factor carry/momentum in commodities and >1.2 for diversified time-series momentum, and Boons-Prado's basis-momentum (slope+curvature of the curve) is the single strongest commodity predictor, surviving ~22bp/trade costs. BUT the most important 2018-2026 finding is severe decay: post-financialization (~2004) and post-GFC the net Sharpe of curve/slope strategies fell from ~1.74/1.47 to ~0.71/0.20 (Bianchi-Fan-Miffre), several factors had 29-58% drawdowns in the 2010s, and net-of-cost single-factor Sharpes are realistically ~0.3-0.7. The premia revived with 2021-22 inflation and survive when implemented with per-asset stop-losses (net Sharpe ~0.9 with fixed-stop; Fan 2024). The crypto perpetuals analogue (carry = funding rate) is directly testable on our data and showed a spectacular but now-decaying pattern: full-sample carry Sharpe ~6.45 (2020-2025) collapsing to 4.06 in 2024 and negative in 2025 as the BTC basis fell from ~25-40% to <5%.

### Findings

**Roll yield / interest-rate-adjusted carry is a LARGER long-run driver of commodity futures returns than spot price appreciation. Carry strategy = long backwardated (downward-sloping curve), short contangoed (upward-sloping) commodities.**
- Effect size: Over 1877-2015: equal-risk-weighted index avg adjusted carry yield = 2.8%/yr vs excess spot return 2.4% (1877-1945) and 1.6% (1946-2015). Futures returns conditional on backwardation vs contango = 14.1% vs -4.5% in high vs low inflation states. Shwayder/James-style backwardation-vs-contango carry across 28 commodities: avg return 7.7% in backwardation vs 1.8% in contango; carry yield 12.2% vs -3.6%.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Decomposition is structural/mechanical and holds across all 139yr subperiods. Carry premium thinned post-financialization (see decay finding) but the roll-yield mechanism itself is identity-true and revived 2021-22.
- Cites: Levine, Ooi, Richardson 2018, 'Commodities for the Long Run', NBER WP 22793 / Financial Analysts Journal; Erb & Harvey 2006, FAJ; Gorton & Rouwenhorst 2006, FAJ

**Cross-sectional commodity carry/term-structure (roll-yield) factor earns a positive, low-equity-correlation premium.**
- Effect size: Quantpedia term-structure long-short (top vs bottom 20% by roll-return, monthly, ~28 commodities): gross ann. return 11.73%, Sharpe 0.49, vol 23.8%, MaxDD -78% (1979-2004, unlevered, gross). Koijen-Moskowitz-Pedersen-Vrugt cross-asset carry: per-asset-class carry Sharpe avg ~0.6; commodity carry specifically positive; diversified global carry Sharpe 0.9.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Robust pre-2010; premium compressed 2010s then partially revived in 2021-22 inflation. Net-of-cost single-factor Sharpe realistically 0.3-0.6.
- Cites: Koijen, Moskowitz, Pedersen, Vrugt 2018, 'Carry', JFE 127(2):197-225; Quantpedia, 'Term Structure Effect in Commodities'; Bakshi, Gao, Rossi 2019, Management Science (carry one of 3 priced factors)

**Cross-sectional commodity momentum (rank on past 12m return, long winners/short losers) earns a positive premium; time-series (trend) momentum is even stronger and is the core CTA trade.**
- Effect size: Cross-sectional 12-1 momentum (Quantpedia, 1979-2004): gross ann. 14.6%, Sharpe 0.57, vol 25.6%, MaxDD -80%. Time-series momentum (Moskowitz-Ooi-Pedersen, 58 instruments incl. commodities, vol-scaled, gross): diversified Sharpe >1.2; commodity-only TSMOM also significant. Commodity momentum vol ~11%, MaxDD < -30% in factor form.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Momentum/TSMOM weakened materially in the 2010s (the famous post-2009 trend drought; 29-58% drawdowns across commodity factors pre-Covid) and reversed sharply at times; revived 2022. Net Sharpe sensitive to turnover.
- Cites: Moskowitz, Ooi, Pedersen 2012, 'Time Series Momentum', JFE 104(2):228-250; Miffre & Rallis 2007, JBF (momentum in commodities); Asness, Moskowitz, Pedersen 2013, 'Value and Momentum Everywhere', JF

**Basis-momentum (momentum in the slope/curvature of the futures curve, i.e. difference in momentum of first vs second nearby) is the single strongest commodity return predictor and is NOT spanned by carry or standard momentum.**
- Effect size: Boons-Prado 2019: basis-momentum high-minus-low strongly outperforms benchmark characteristics in both time-series and cross-section; significant alpha after controlling for momentum and basis/carry; survives ~22bp/trade transaction costs across 32 liquid commodities. Bakshi-Gao-Rossi-style and Fan multi-factor work confirm basis-momentum among ~4 priced latent factors. Best 5-factor combo (mom+basis+basis-mom+value+HP, ex-precious-metals, equal-weight): Sharpe 1.67, certainty-equiv 15.5%/yr.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Published 2019; replicated in 2023-2025 follow-ons. Among the more durable commodity signals because it is hard to arbitrage (needs curve trading). Still net-positive post-2015 in liquid commodities.
- Cites: Boons & Prado 2019, 'Basis-Momentum', JF 74(1):239-279; Sakkas & Tessaromatis 2020, 'Factor Based Commodity Investing', JBF; Bakshi, Gao, Rossi 2019, Management Science

**FINANCIALIZATION/CROWDING DECAY: commodity carry/curve/momentum premia fell sharply after the ~2004 index-investment wave and the GFC; equity-market beta of commodity factors rose.**
- Effect size: Bianchi-Fan-Miffre (curve slope 'S' strategy, 21 commodities, 1992-2019): pre- vs post-financialization NET Sharpe 1.74 -> 0.71; pre- vs post-GFC 1.47 -> 0.20 (differences significant at 1%). Net annualized alpha 2.16%/1.90% -> 0.87%/0.23%. Across commodity factors, 29-58% drawdowns in the decade before Covid. Pricing kernel shifted from macro to financial variables.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: This IS the post-2010/post-2018 story. Decay is well-documented; partial revival in 2021-22 inflation regime but lower plateau than pre-2004.
- Cites: Bianchi, Fan, Miffre, Zhang 2023, 'Exploiting the dynamics of commodity futures curves', arXiv 2308.00383 / JBF; Prokopczuk et al. 2021, J. Futures Markets (comovement/financialization); Qian 2025, 'Factor Momentum in Commodity Futures Markets', J. Futures Markets

**Curve/slope/curvature strategies (Nelson-Siegel decomposition of the whole curve) generate large gross Sharpes that DEGRADE substantially but remain economically meaningful net of realistic costs.**
- Effect size: Bianchi-Fan-Miffre out-of-sample: Slope strategy gross Sharpe 1.41 (t=7.23), Curvature 1.27 (t=5.34), 1992-2019, 21 commodities. After three transaction-cost scenarios net Sharpe range 0.44-1.04; net alphas of slope strategy significant at 1%. Roughly 30% of recent practitioner commodity-premia returns came from carry, ~70% from curve positioning (Bloomberg 2025).
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Recent (sample to mid-2019, published 2023). Demonstrates the cost wedge: gross ~1.3-1.4 -> net ~0.4-1.0. Carry contribution thinner in 2025 as precious metals rallied.
- Cites: Bianchi, Fan, Miffre, Zhang 2023, arXiv 2308.00383; Bloomberg Professional 2025, 'Capturing curve, carry and trend premia in commodity markets'

**RISK MANAGEMENT MATTERS: per-asset stop-losses materially raise net Sharpe and cut drawdowns of commodity factor premia, keeping them investable post-2018.**
- Effect size: Fan 2024 (commodity factors avg, 1983-2022, NET of costs): no-stop net Sharpe 0.92; with fixed-stop ~0.92, with trailing-stop 1.28; MaxDD cut to <20%; return skew turned positive. Confirms premia 'alive and well' when risk-managed.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Directly addresses post-2018/post-2020 viability; sample runs to 2022 and includes the inflation revival.
- Cites: Fan et al. 2024, 'Commodity premia and risk management', J. Futures Markets 44, doi:10.1002/fut.22507

**CRYPTO ANALOGUE (directly testable on our data): perpetual-futures carry = the funding rate; cash-and-carry (long spot/short perp) historically earned a very high but rapidly decaying premium. This is the commodity-carry mechanism reincarnated.**
- Effect size: arXiv 2510.14435: full-sample (Aug2020-May2025) crypto carry annualized Sharpe 6.45 (funding component mean ~8% with only 0.8% vol); 2024 Sharpe 4.06; 2025 negative. BIS WP 1087 (Apr2019-Jul2024): avg cross-exchange carry ~7% p.a. (BTC 1m basis 6.4% CME / 8% OKEx), spikes >40-55%, crashes < -50% during FTX; cross-exchange corr >90%; a +10% carry shock predicts +22% of OI in short-futures liquidations next month -> NOT risk-free. Practitioner delta-neutral realized APY ~4-30% (mostly 8-18%) 2024-25; BTC basis fell ~25%/Feb2024 -> 4.46%/Dec2025.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Most recent and most relevant to our holdings. Sharp 2024-2025 compression is the live decay story; negative-funding regimes (bearish unwinds, liquidation cascades) are the analogue of contango/crashes.
- Cites: arXiv 2510.14435v2 2025, 'Cryptocurrency as an Investable Asset Class: Coming of Age'; BIS Working Paper No 1087 2023, 'Crypto carry'; CF Benchmarks 2024-25, Bitcoin basis research

**SECTOR EFFECTS: carry/momentum efficacy varies sharply by sector; energy and agriculture/oilseeds carry strongest, metals (esp. precious) weakest; precious metals are near-permanent contango and dilute carry.**
- Effect size: Bianchi-Fan-Miffre sector Sharpes 0.36 (metals) to 1.24 (oilseeds). Best combination factor portfolios explicitly EXCLUDE precious metals (Sharpe 1.67 ex-precious vs lower with). Backwardation concentrated in storable energy/ags with convenience yield; gold/silver structurally contangoed (carry ~ -storage-rate).
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Stable structural feature; in 2025 precious-metals rally hurt carry sleeves that underweighted them.
- Cites: Bianchi, Fan, Miffre, Zhang 2023, arXiv 2308.00383; Sakkas & Tessaromatis 2020, JBF; Bloomberg Professional 2025

### Testable hypotheses
- CRYPTO CARRY (highest priority, fully testable on our 228-perpetual x ~23k-hour funding-rate + Coinalyze data): A cross-sectional carry portfolio that each hour/day goes long the bottom-decile (most-negative funding) and short the top-decile (most-positive funding) perpetuals, delta-hedged with spot, earns positive net funding-harvest. Falsifiable prediction from the literature: full-sample (2024-02 to 2026-06) Sharpe is high but monotonically declining; the 2025 cohort should be near-zero or negative net of fees+slippage.
- CRYPTO BASIS-MOMENTUM analogue: define each coin's 'curve slope' as (perp price - spot) or funding level, and 'slope momentum' as the change in funding over the trailing N days. Hypothesis: sorting on funding-momentum (rising funding = crowded longs about to unwind) predicts next-period returns better than funding level alone, and a short-the-rising-funding leg has positive return especially around liquidation cascades (test with Coinalyze liquidation data).
- CRYPTO TSMOM: vol-scaled time-series momentum (sign of trailing 1d-30d return) on top-50 coins delivers gross Sharpe >1 but net Sharpe collapses at 1h/4h rebalance due to taker fees+funding; the breakeven rebalance frequency where net Sharpe peaks is daily-to-weekly, not intraday.
- CARRY-MOMENTUM INTERACTION: in crypto, carry (funding) and momentum are positively correlated (high funding accompanies up-trends), so a naive long-high-carry book is a hidden momentum/crash bet; hypothesis: conditioning carry on momentum sign (only collect funding when trend agrees) reduces drawdown and raises net Sharpe vs unconditional carry.
- EQUITY-SECTOR ROLL-YIELD PROXY: using S&P 500 names, energy/materials equity-sector returns load on the same backwardation/inflation factor as commodity carry; hypothesis: a long energy-vs-defensives equity tilt has positive correlation (>0.3) with realized WTI roll yield (from EIA front-month series) and could proxy commodity carry without futures accounts.
