- FINANCIALIZATION/CROWDING DECAY (out-of-sample test): re-estimate any commodity carry/momentum signal on free continuous-futures data and confirm the net Sharpe in 2010-2026 is materially below the 1990-2004 net Sharpe (predicted drop of roughly half), validating crowding rather than rejecting the premium.
- STOP-LOSS OVERLAY: applying a per-asset trailing stop to a crypto carry or momentum book raises net Sharpe and cuts MaxDD below 20% (direct replication of Fan 2024 on our crypto data).

### Harvest strategies
- CRYPTO CASH-AND-CARRY (delta-neutral funding harvest) -- the cleanest harvestable version on OUR data: long spot + short perpetual of the same coin, collect funding when positive. Instruments: top-15 liquid perps (BTC, ETH, SOL, etc.). Cost drag: taker fees ~4-10bp/side to enter+exit, perp-spot basis slippage, plus the funding itself can flip negative (the real risk). Net realized APY in 2024-25 was ~8-18% (compressing); size to where funding > all-in cost. Best run as cross-sectional: short the highest-funding perps, long lowest, market-neutral.
- CRYPTO CROSS-SECTIONAL CARRY (no spot leg, pure long-short perps): long bottom-funding-decile perps / short top-funding-decile, dollar-neutral, daily rebalance. Cost drag: 2x taker fees per rebalance + funding paid/received; turnover is the killer at sub-daily frequency. Edge survives only if rebalanced daily-to-weekly, not hourly.
- COMMODITY CARRY (if futures sourced): long the 4-6 most-backwardated, short the 4-6 most-contangoed liquid commodities (rank by slope = (F_near - F_far)/F_far), monthly roll, vol-target ~10%. Exclude precious metals. Cost drag: ~10-22bp round-trip per liquid contract (energy/ags cheapest), plus roll-execution cost; net Sharpe realistically 0.4-0.7. Implement via continuous front+second contracts from Nasdaq Data Link CHRIS.
- BASIS-MOMENTUM SPREAD (highest research alpha-per-cost): for each commodity trade the calendar spread = long-near/short-deferred when near-contract momentum > deferred-contract momentum (and vice-versa), long-short across the 12-15 most liquid commodities, monthly. Survives ~22bp costs (Boons-Prado). Lower outright vol than directional carry because it is a curve trade. Cost drag dominated by trading two contracts per name.
- TIME-SERIES MOMENTUM / TREND OVERLAY: vol-scaled sign(trailing 3-12m return) on each commodity or coin, weekly rebalance, target ~10% vol; use as a diversifying overlay and as a crash-hedge for the carry book (TSMOM is long-vol-ish, carry is short-vol-ish -- combining them is the classic CTA improvement, Sharpe lift ~0.2-0.4). Cost drag modest at weekly frequency for liquid names.
- RISK-MANAGED WRAPPER (apply to all of the above): per-asset trailing stop-loss + monthly vol-targeting. Empirically (Fan 2024) lifts net Sharpe toward ~1.0-1.3 and caps MaxDD <20%, which is the difference between investable and not for the post-2018 regime.

### Pitfalls
- SURVIVORSHIP & ROLL-METHOD SNOOPING in continuous futures: free CHRIS/Stooq continuous series depend on roll date and adjustment method (ratio vs difference vs Panama). Roll yield IS the signal here, so a sloppy back-adjustment silently injects or destroys the very return you measure. Must construct roll yield from raw front+second contracts, not pre-stitched series, and match roll timing to a tradeable rule.
- CROWDING/FINANCIALIZATION DECAY is real and documented: net Sharpe of curve/carry strategies roughly halved post-2004 and post-GFC (1.74->0.71). Backtests anchored pre-2010 (most classic papers: 1979-2004) overstate live edge by ~2x. Always report a post-2010 and post-2018 subsample separately.
- COST UNDERSTATEMENT: classic gross Sharpes (0.5-1.4) shrink to net 0.3-1.0 at realistic ~10-22bp round-trip; high-turnover momentum/factor-momentum can be entirely eaten by costs. In crypto, taker fees + funding-on-funding + slippage on alts are far larger than headline funding; the 6.45 'Sharpe' is gross and pre-capacity.
- CRYPTO CARRY IS SHORT-VOLATILITY / NOT ARBITRAGE: funding can flip deeply negative in liquidation cascades (BIS: +10% carry shock -> 22% of OI liquidated next month; CME carry hit < -50% in FTX collapse). A long-funding book has fat negative tails masquerading as steady yield -- the same shape as commodity contango blow-ups. Sharpe is a poor metric for this skew.
- REGIME-CONDITIONALITY MISTAKEN FOR ALPHA: commodity carry/momentum return is highly state-dependent (14.1% high-inflation vs -4.5% low-inflation; great in 2021-22, dismal 2014-2020). Fitting on an inflationary window over-extrapolates. Crypto carry's 2020-23 boom was a one-time leverage-demand regime now compressing.
- MULTIPLE-TESTING ACROSS THE COMMODITY FACTOR ZOO: dozens of curve signals (basis, momentum, basis-momentum, curve-momentum, relative basis, hedging pressure, skewness, liquidity, value) are mutually correlated; many are the same backwardation bet re-expressed. Bonferroni/Harvey-Liu haircuts and out-of-sample (post-publication) tests are mandatory -- basis-momentum is one of few with post-2015 OOS support.
- CAPACITY / LIQUIDITY ILLUSION: precious-metals and energy front months are deep, but ags and alt-crypto perps are thin. Equal-weight backtests assume infinite liquidity in names that move on your own order. Volume-weight or cap the universe to genuinely liquid contracts (the literature's '21-32 liquid commodities', and top-15 crypto perps).
- LOOK-AHEAD IN FUNDING/SETTLEMENT TIMING: crypto funding is paid at discrete settlement times; collecting funding requires holding across the settlement timestamp. Backtests that mark funding continuously or assume you can predict the next funding print overstate returns.

### Data needed
- ALREADY HAVE (test crypto analogues immediately): 228 perpetuals x ~23k hours of funding-rate history + top-50 coins OHLCV (1h/4h/1d, 2024-02 to 2026-06) for cross-sectional carry, funding-momentum and TSMOM; Coinalyze funding/OI/liquidations to test the carry->liquidation-cascade mechanism and crash risk; Deribit DVOL/IV surfaces to relate carry to implied vol (carry is short-vol).
- FREE COMMODITY FUTURES TERM STRUCTURE: Nasdaq Data Link (formerly Quandl) free 'CHRIS' continuous-futures DB (e.g. CHRIS/CME_CL1, CL2 for front+second WTI) and 'Wiki Continuous Futures' -- gives multiple contract depths needed for roll yield / basis-momentum. NOTE these free DBs are stale/discontinued post-~2018 in places; verify current end-dates.
- FREE SPOT/FRONT-MONTH for roll-yield construction: EIA Open Data API (daily Cushing WTI, Brent, RBOB, Henry Hub natural gas back to 1986; weekly inventories for fundamentals); Stooq free daily history (US futures front-month + FX); Yahoo Finance continuous-front contracts (CL=F, GC=F, NG=F, ZC=F, etc.) for daily OHLC; FRED (DCOILWTICO, etc.) for clean spot series.
- FREE AGS DATA: USDA NASS QuickStats (monthly prices received for ~65 commodities; fundamentals); USDA WASDE reports for supply/demand surprises (event study for ag carry/momentum).
- FX (to-be-sourced, for cross-asset carry replication): free interest-rate differentials and spot from FRED + ECB/central-bank feeds; forwards harder to get free -- approximate carry via covered-interest-parity from deposit-rate differentials.
- TO BUY/UPGRADE IF SERIOUS ON COMMODITIES: a clean multi-contract futures term-structure feed (Barchart, CSI, or Nasdaq Data Link premium SCF/OWF) because the free CHRIS data's roll method and post-2018 coverage are inadequate for a publishable roll-yield/basis-momentum backtest -- the signal lives in the curve, so curve data quality is the binding constraint.
- BENCHMARKS for context: Bloomberg Commodity Index (BCOM) and S&P GSCI total-return vs spot-return series (roll-return = TR minus spot) to validate any internally-computed roll yield; available free in summary form.

### Adversarial verification — reliability: **medium**
_Net-of-cost reality:_ Net of realistic costs, this area is real but materially thinner and more fragile than the summary's confident framing. What survives independent scrutiny: (a) the carry/roll-yield MECHANISM is near-identity-true and the long-run level decomposition (carry > spot) checks out; (b) basis-momentum is the most defensible single signal -- peer-reviewed, replicated/extended through 2024-25, no failed replication, and hard to arbitrage because it needs curve trading; (c) time-series/trend momentum (CTA-style) genuinely revived in the 2022 inflation shock (SG Trend +27% in 2022) after a near-flat 2011-2019 'drought.' What does NOT survive cleanly: the headline gross Sharpes (single-factor 0.5-0.6, TSMOM >1.2, curve 1.3-1.4, crypto 6.45) are gross, pre-capacity, and in several cases sit on unlevered max-drawdowns of -78% to -80% (Quantpedia term-structure/momentum) -- a tell that these are high-vol backtests, not investable Sharpes. After ~10-22bp round-trip (energy/ags cheapest, ags/alts thinnest and most capacity-constrained), realistic single-factor net Sharpes are ~0.3-0.7, the curve-CURVATURE leg goes negative, and the curve-slope leg's post-GFC net Sharpe is ~0.20 (economically dead in the modern regime). The crypto cash-and-carry 'reincarnation' is the most overstated piece: the 6.45 Sharpe is an idealized funding-harvest number; BIS shows the same trade is explicitly NOT risk-free (>40% spikes, < -50% FTX crash, +10% carry shock -> 22% of OI liquidated next month), the 2024 spot-ETF causally cut the premium 36-97%, and real delta-neutral net APY in 2024-26 is ~6-11% (higher only via yield-stacking), now sub-5% basis on >90% of days -- a short-vol carry trade with fat left tails, exactly the contango-blowup analogue the summary's pitfalls correctly flag. Two adversarial cautions on the summary's OWN decay narrative cut the other way: the dramatic '1.74->0.71, halve-your-edge, backtests overstate by 2x' figure is ONE strategy on ONE break date; the broad meta-study consensus (Chen & Zimmermann 2023; McLean-Pontiff 2016; Bhardwaj-Gorton-Rouwenhorst 2015) is milder -- ~26% out-of-sample decay (74% persists), publication bias only ~10-15% of in-sample returns, and the core commodity risk premium was in-/out-of-sample STABLE. So the summary is simultaneously too optimistic on gross/crypto Sharpes and slightly too pessimistic in generalizing the worst single decay estimate to the whole area. Bottom line for deployment: trade these only risk-managed (vol-target ~10%, per-asset stops a la Fan 2024), capacity-capped to genuinely liquid contracts/top-15 perps, with carry and trend combined (trend hedges carry's left tail), reporting post-2010 and post-2018 subsamples and treating Sharpe as a poor metric for the short-vol carry sleeves. Expect net single-factor Sharpes in the 0.3-0.7 band, not the headline 1+.
- **[WEAKENED]** Crypto perpetual/cash-and-carry carry (funding-rate harvest) earned a full-sample Sharpe ~6.45 (Aug2020-May2025), funding component mean ~8% with only ~0.8% vol, falling to 4.06 in 2024 and negative in 2025 as BTC basis collapsed from ~25% to <5%. Framed as the commodity-carry mechanism reincarnated. — The headline numbers are real and I verified them in the primary source (arXiv 2510.14435v2 states Sharpe 6.45 over Aug2020-May2025, 4.06 in 2024, negative 2025; funding mean ~8% with vol ~0.8%). BUT three adversarial problems gut its usefulness as a live edge. (1) GROSS / PRE-CAPACITY: the paper does NOT state the Sharpe is net of taker fees, slippage on alts, or funding-on-funding; a 'mean 8% / vol 0.8%' funding component mechanically implies a ~10 information ratio on funding alone, which is a textbook idealized-backtest artifact, not an achievable Sharpe. Independent practitioner/2024-26 evidence puts realized delta-neutral APY at ~6-11% (5.98-11.4% fixed APY across BTC/ETH 2025 maturities); higher headline figures (~19-21%) come explicitly from 'yield stacking' (e.g. Securitize 10.78% basis + 4.25% BUIDL collateral = 20.71%), not the carry itself. (2) NOT RISK-FREE / SHORT-VOL: the independent BIS WP 1087 (Schmeling-Schrimpf-Todorov, rev. Oct 2025) explicitly REFUTES the 'risk-free' framing the high Sharpe implies. It documents avg cross-exchange carry ~7% p.a. (BTC 1m basis ~8% OKEx / 6.4% CME), spikes >40% p.a., and crashes below -50% during the FTX collapse, and shows a +10% (standardized) carry shock predicts liquidations of 22% of open interest in short-futures positions next month -- i.e. fat negative tails masquerading as steady yield, so Sharpe badly overstates risk-adjusted quality. (3) DECAY IS REAL AND CAUSAL: BIS shows the 2024 spot-ETF launch causally cut carry by ~3pp across exchanges and ~5pp on CME (DiD), economically -36% and -97% of mean carry. So the decay-to-negative-2025 part of the claim is CONFIRMED and is the honest takeaway; the 6.45 'robust premium' framing is misleading.
- **[CONFIRMED]** FINANCIALIZATION/CROWDING DECAY: the NET Sharpe of the commodity curve-slope ('S') strategy fell from 1.74 to 0.71 pre/post-financialization (CFMA 2000) and 1.47 to 0.20 pre/post-GFC, with net alphas 2.16%/1.90% falling to 0.87%/0.23% (all significant at 1%). — Verified verbatim against the primary source. Bianchi, Fan, Miffre & Zhang (arXiv 2308.00383, J. Banking & Finance 2023, 21 commodities, 1992-2019): 'The pre-event net Sharpe ratios (1.74 for financialization and 1.47 for GFC) are statistically different from the post-event net Sharpe ratios (0.71 and 0.20, respectively) at the 1% level... annualized pre-event net alphas (2.16% and 1.90%) ... post-event net alphas (0.87% and 0.23%).' Every number in the claim matches exactly. The authors attribute it to crowding, cheaper/easier post-2001 trading, algorithmic-trading efficiency gains and reduced limits to arbitrage -- a clean crowding-decay story. The only adversarial caveat is generalization: this is ONE strategy on ONE break date, and the post-GFC 0.20 effectively means the curve-slope edge is economically dead net of costs in the modern regime, which is arguably even MORE damning than the summary's framing.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Basis-momentum (momentum in slope/curvature of the futures curve) is the single strongest commodity return predictor, is NOT spanned by carry or standard momentum, and survives ~22bp/trade transaction costs; replicated/durable post-2015. — The original result is real and peer-reviewed (Boons & Prado 2019, J. Finance 74(1):239-279): basis-momentum strongly outperforms benchmark characteristics in both time-series and cross-section, is priced after controlling for momentum and basis/carry, and is interpreted as compensation for priced risk from impaired speculator/intermediary market-clearing. I found NO failed replication. Follow-on work through 2024-2025 keeps it as a priced commodity factor and extends it (currency basis-momentum decompositions; 'efficient' factor construction giving a further +0.13 Sharpe with t=2.76; factor-momentum-in-commodities papers). Two adversarial caveats keep this from being a slam-dunk rather than refuting it: (1) the specific '~22bp survival' and the headline best-combo Sharpe ~1.67 (ex-precious, equal-weight) are IN-SAMPLE/author results -- equal-weight ignores the capacity/liquidity illusion in thin ags, and the general literature shows ~26% out-of-sample and ~50% far-from-sample return decay (Chen-Zimmermann; McLean-Pontiff). (2) It sits in a crowded, mutually-correlated commodity factor zoo (basis, momentum, basis-mom, curve-mom, relative basis, hedging pressure), so multiple-testing haircuts are warranted. Net: the qualitative claim holds and is among the more durable commodity signals; the precise cost-survival figure should be treated as optimistic.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Roll yield / interest-rate-adjusted carry (net convenience yield) is a LARGER long-run driver of commodity futures returns than excess spot appreciation: 1877-2015 equal-risk-weighted adjusted carry ~2.8%/yr vs excess spot ~2.4% (1877-1945) and ~1.6% (1946-2015). — The decomposition and magnitudes are confirmed against Levine, Ooi, Richardson & Sasseville, 'Commodities for the Long Run' (NBER WP 22793 / FAJ 2018 / AQR datasets): average adjusted carry yield ~2.8% exceeds average excess spot returns (~1.6% for 1946-2015), so on a long-run AVERAGE-level basis carry is the larger contributor. This is also close to mechanically/identity true (futures excess return = excess spot return + net convenience yield), which is why the summary rightly calls the mechanism 'identity-true.' IMPORTANT NUANCE that the summary glosses: the same paper emphasizes that commodity returns ACROSS economic states (inflation up/down, expansion/recession) 'vary mostly as a result of moves in the underlying spot price' -- i.e. carry drives the average level but SPOT drives the variation/risk. So 'carry is the bigger driver' is correct for the unconditional mean but should not be read as 'spot doesn't matter' -- spot dominates the state-dependent swings (e.g. the cited 14.1% vs -4.5% backwardation-vs-contango gap in high/low inflation is largely a spot-state effect). Direction of the claim stands.
- **[WEAKENED]** Curve/slope/curvature (Nelson-Siegel) strategies post large gross Sharpes (slope 1.41 t=7.23, curvature 1.27 t=5.34) that degrade but 'remain economically meaningful' net of realistic costs (net Sharpe range 0.44-1.04). — The gross figures and the headline net range are verified (Bianchi et al. 2023: S gross Sharpe 1.41, t=7.23; C gross Sharpe ~1.23-1.27, t=5.34; net Sharpe range 0.44-1.04 across three cost scenarios). But the 'remain economically meaningful net of costs' framing is too generous on two counts the summary buries. (1) Only the SLOPE leg survives: the paper states the CURVATURE strategy's net mean excess return is -0.55% to +0.24%/yr and is 'statistically less than zero under both TC2 and TC3' -- i.e. curvature is a net LOSER under the two higher (more realistic) cost scenarios. (2) The authors themselves warn investors to 'proceed with caution' and that 'only institutions that can [bear the trading-intensive costs]' should implement -- these are high-turnover strategies. Combine with the same paper's post-GFC net Sharpe of 0.20 (above) and the modern-regime live edge is thin. So: slope survives net (weak-to-moderate), curvature does not; calling the bucket broadly 'economically meaningful net of costs' overstates it.

---

## Cross-sectional factor zoo and replication crisis  `anomaly_zoo`

The literature has split into three camps that, taken together, define a coherent answer. The "crisis" camp (Hou-Xue-Zhang 2020: 65% of 452 anomalies fail t>1.96, 82% fail the t>2.78 multiple-test hurdle once microcaps are tamed via NYSE breakpoints + value-weighting; Harvey-Liu-Zhu 2016: a new factor needs t>3.0; McLean-Pontiff 2016: returns fall 26% out-of-sample and 58% post-publication) shows that most published anomalies are fragile, microcap-driven, or decay sharply once known. The "no-crisis" camp (Jensen-Kelly-Pedersen 2023: 82.4% of 153 factors replicate under a proper Bayesian/multiple-testing model, cluster into 13 themes, and work out-of-sample across 93 countries; Chen-Zimmermann 2022 + Chen 2021: ~100% pure-replication, false-discovery rate <=22% and t-stats inflated <=28%, so t-hurdles need NOT be raised) shows that the crisis is largely an artifact of methodology choices (weighting scheme, breakpoints, treating noise as failure). Both camps actually agree on the practitioner-relevant conclusion: only a small number of robust THEMES survive -- value, momentum, profitability/quality, investment, and (contested) low-risk -- size alone is dead (~0.1%/mo, insignificant since 1980 unless quality-adjusted); and net of realistic costs the count shrinks further. The deepest current finding is that "non-standard errors"/forking paths (Menkveld 2024; Coqueret 2024) -- defensible researcher choices -- generate dispersion on par with statistical error and can push the honest significance bar to t>=8.2, making rigor (pre-registered protocol, OOS, cost-aware) the binding constraint on harvestable alpha, not model sophistication. In crypto the cross-section is real but thin: a 3-factor model (market/size/momentum, Liu-Tsyvinski-Wu 2022) prices it, trend survives costs, but anomalies concentrate in illiquid small coins and a 2-3 factor liquidity-dominated model absorbs the rest.

### Findings

**Hou-Xue-Zhang: most anomalies fail to replicate once microcaps are controlled. With NYSE breakpoints + value-weighted returns, 65% of 452 anomalies fail the single t>1.96 hurdle; 82% fail the t>2.78 multiple-test hurdle. The trading-frictions category is the biggest casualty (96%, 102/106, fail). Survivors are dominated by profitability/investment/momentum, not liquidity. Crucially, the failure rate drops to ~41% with equal-weighting -- so the methodology choice (VW vs EW, microcap treatment) drives much of the 'crisis'.**
- Effect size: 65% fail at |t|>=1.96 (VW/NYSE); 82% fail at |t|>=2.78; 41.4% fail at |t|>=1.96 with EW. 158 of 452 replicate at t>1.96. Microcaps = 3.2% of market cap but 60.7% of stock count. Even replicated anomalies have economic magnitudes 'much smaller than originally reported'.
- Strength: strong · Recency: RFS 2020; sample through ~2016. The result is methodology-dependent (VW vs EW), a point JKP 2023 exploit to overturn the headline.
- Cites: Hou, Xue, Zhang 2020, 'Replicating Anomalies', Review of Financial Studies 33(5):2019-2133 (NBER w23394); Hou, Mo, Xue, Zhang 2021, 'q5', Review of Finance (NBER w24709)

**Harvey-Liu-Zhu: rampant multiple testing means the conventional t>2.0 bar is far too low; a newly claimed factor should clear t>3.0. Harvey-Liu (2020, 'False and Missed Discoveries') refine this with a double-bootstrap that sets a t-hurdle for a target false-discovery rate and balances Type I vs Type II error -- implying the right hurdle depends on the relative cost of misses vs false positives (so t>3.0 is not universal).**
- Effect size: Recommended hurdle t>3.0 (HLZ 2016) for ~5% FDR given hundreds of tests; HL 2020 double-bootstrap yields data-dependent hurdles (often ~2.7-3.4) and explicitly trades off Type I/II costs. Harvey 2017 (Presidential Address): even t>3 yields many false positives when true effects are rare.
- Strength: strong · Recency: RFS 2016, JF 2020, JF 2017. Methodologically influential; the specific 3.0 number is contested by Chen (see below).
- Cites: Harvey, Liu, Zhu 2016, '...and the Cross-Section of Expected Returns', RFS 29(1):5-68; Harvey, Liu 2020, 'False (and Missed) Discoveries in Financial Economics', JF 75(5):2503-2553; Harvey 2017, 'Presidential Address: The Scientific Outlook in Financial Economics', JF 72(4):1399-1440; Harvey, Liu 2021, 'Lucky Factors', JFE 141(2):413-435

**McLean-Pontiff: out-of-sample and post-publication decay is large and real. Across 97 predictors from 80 studies, average long-short returns fall 26% out-of-sample (upper bound on data-mining bias) and 58% post-publication (the extra ~32% is investor learning / arbitrage). Decay is largest for high-in-sample-return predictors and is SMALLER for portfolios in illiquid, high-idiosyncratic-risk stocks (limits to arbitrage protect the premium) -- and post-publication correlations with arbitrageur portfolios rise.**
- Effect size: In-sample 0.582%/mo -> pre-publication OOS 0.402%/mo -> post-publication 0.264%/mo. Out-of-sample decline ~15.0 bps/mo (coef -0.26); post-publication decline 33.7 bps/mo (coef -0.337). 85 of 97 predictors had in-sample t>1.50.
- Strength: strong · Recency: JF 2016; sample ends 2013. Updated by crowding work (e.g. 2024 hyperbolic-decay model alpha(t)=K/(1+lambda*t)) showing crowding ACCELERATED post-2015, especially for 'mechanical' signals like momentum.
- Cites: McLean, Pontiff 2016, 'Does Academic Research Destroy Stock Return Predictability?', JF 71(1):5-32; 'Not All Factors Crowd Equally', 2024, arXiv:2512.11913 (momentum hyperbolic-decay R2=0.65; predicted 0.30 vs actual 0.15 alpha for 2016-2024)

**Jensen-Kelly-Pedersen (the strongest 'no-crisis' rebuttal): with a Bayesian hierarchical model that shrinks noisy estimates and handles multiple testing correctly, 82.4% of 153 factors replicate (vs HXZ's 35%). The replication ladder: HXZ 35% -> 55.6% baseline -> 61.3% (noise/measurement adj) -> 82.4% (CAPM-alpha tests) -> 75.6% naive multiple-testing but back to 82.4% under Bayesian MT. Factors cluster into 13 themes, >50% replicate in 11 of 13 themes, the themes are significant parts of the tangency portfolio, and they work OOS in 93 countries. Key insight: MORE factors STRENGTHEN (not weaken) the evidence because they share economic structure.**
- Effect size: 82.4% global replication rate (US 81.5%; 79.8% with extra-conservative prior); 13 themes; OOS in 93 countries; >50% replicate in 11/13 themes. Posterior FDR for the 82.4% rate is tight.
- Strength: strong · Recency: JF 2023 (NBER w28432, 2021). The current authoritative synthesis; data+code public (bkelly-lab/ReplicationCrisis). Directly rebuts HXZ on methodology.
- Cites: Jensen, Kelly, Pedersen 2023, 'Is There a Replication Crisis in Finance?', JF 78(5):2465-2518 (NBER w28432)

**Chen & Zimmermann: publication bias is modest, not dominant. Pure-replication reproduces ~100% of predictors (for 161 clearly-significant originals, 98% of reproductions clear t>1.96; reproduced-vs-original t-stat regression slope 0.88, R2=82%). Four stylized facts argue against a crisis: (1) almost all findings replicate, (2) predictability persists OOS, (3) empirical t-stats are MUCH larger than 2, (4) predictors are weakly correlated. Empirical-Bayes corrections put publication bias at only 10-15% of in-sample returns and FDR <10%. Chen (2021) separately shows t-hurdles need NOT be raised: published t-stats inflated by at most 28%, FDR at most 22% (95% CI).**
- Effect size: Publication bias = 10-15% of in-sample returns; FDR <10% (CZ) to <=22% worst-case (Chen 2021); t-stat inflation <=28%; pure-replication ~100%; reproduced/original t-stat slope 0.88.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Critical Finance Review 2022 (OSAP, 319 characteristics); arXiv 2209.13623 (2022); 'Do t-Statistic Hurdles Need to be Raised?' arXiv:2204.10275 (2022). The leading counter to HLZ/HXZ.
- Cites: Chen, Zimmermann 2022, 'Open Source Cross-Sectional Asset Pricing', Critical Finance Review 11:207-264; Chen, Zimmermann 2022, 'Publication Bias in Asset Pricing Research', arXiv:2209.13623; Chen 2021, 'Do t-Statistic Hurdles Need to be Raised?', arXiv:2204.10275 (also 'Most claimed findings... likely true', arXiv:2206.15365)

**Value premium: not dead but lived through its worst-ever drawdown. Standard HML lost ~2.6%/yr over 2010-2019 and drew down ~55% from 2007 to mid-2020 (value losses 2018 -12.3%, 2019 -8.1%, 2020 -21.9%). AQR (Israel-Laursen-Richardson) argued death was premature; Blitz-Hanauer 'resurrected' it with better metrics. Value-spread reached ~100th percentile in 2020 then mean-reverted violently: AQR value strategies returned +20-31% in 2021-2022. Measurement matters enormously -- monthly-updated value (Asness-Frazzini 'Devil in HML') earns 305-378 bps/yr alpha vs annually-lagged HML.**
- Effect size: HML -2.6%/yr 2010-2019, -55% peak-to-trough drawdown; value spread ~94th-100th pct end-2020/2022; AQR Equity Market-Neutral Global Value +20.6% (2023), Absolute Return +43.5% (2022); monthly-updated value +305 to +378 bps/yr alpha over 5-factor model. Long-run value Sharpe ~0.3-0.4.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Lost decade 2010-2020 then sharp 2021-2023 recovery. Survives but is regime-dependent and metric-sensitive; a clean forking-paths example.
- Cites: Israel, Laursen, Richardson 2021, 'Is (Systematic) Value Investing Dead?', J. Portfolio Management 47(2):38-62 (AQR); Blitz, Hanauer 2021, 'Resurrecting the Value Premium', JPM 47(2):63-81; Asness, Frazzini 2013, 'The Devil in HML's Details', JPM 39(4):49-68; Fama, French 2021 / Blitz 'Factor Performance 2010-2019: A Lost Decade?', SSRN 3562242

**Momentum: large gross premium, robust across studies, but the most cost- and crowding-fragile of the major factors. Strong returns historically (~10%/yr 1990s) but decayed (practitioner estimates ~2%/yr recently) and capacity-limited. The cost debate is sharp: Korajczyk-Sadka cap momentum at ~$5bn before alpha vanishes; Patton-Weller find typical mutual-fund momentum implementation costs of 2.2-8.5%/yr that ELIMINATE the premium; AQR (Frazzini-Israel-Moskowitz) counter that real costs are <1/10 of academic estimates and momentum is scalable. Crash risk is severe (left-tail), motivating volatility-scaling/risk-managed momentum.**
- Effect size: Gross long-short ~0.5-1.0%/mo (post-2000 alpha 0.77-0.91%/mo in some studies); capacity ~$5bn (Korajczyk-Sadka); implementation cost 2.2-8.5%/yr (Patton-Weller, kills net premium for typical funds) vs <1/10 academic cost (FIM, scalable). Long-run gross Sharpe ~0.5.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Persists post-2000 but decayed and crowded (mechanical signal crowds fastest, 2024 work). Net-of-cost survival is the central dispute and is portfolio-design dependent.
- Cites: Jegadeesh, Titman 1993, JF; Korajczyk, Sadka 2004, 'Are Momentum Profits Robust to Trading Costs?', JF 59(3):1039-1082; Frazzini, Israel, Moskowitz 2018, 'Trading Costs of Asset Pricing Anomalies', SSRN 2294498 (AQR, ~$1trn live data); Patton, Weller 2020, 'What You See Is Not What You Get', Mgmt Science

**Low-risk / BAB: high reported Sharpe but the alpha is substantially a construction artifact and partly microcap/cost-driven. Frazzini-Pedersen report BAB Sharpe 0.78 (1926-2012). Novy-Marx-Velikov show BAB's headline alpha comes from non-standard rank-weighting that effectively equal-weights and loads ~$1.05 per $1 on bottom-1%-cap stocks; once value-weighted it earns a much smaller ~56 bps/yr excess return, transaction costs cut profitability ~60%, and the residual is explained by profitability/investment exposure. So a real low-risk effect exists but the famous BAB number overstates harvestable alpha.**
- Effect size: BAB gross Sharpe 0.78; 5-factor alpha ~51-55 bps/MONTH (FP replication); value-weighted BAB only ~56 bps/yr excess; costs reduce BAB profitability ~60%; ~$1.05 per $1 in bottom-1% cap stocks.
- Strength: contested · Recency: FP 2014 (JFE); Novy-Marx-Velikov 2022 (JFE) critique; 'Betting Against (Bad) Beta' 2025 revives a cleaner version (BABB Sharpe ~1.09, alpha 75 bps/mo). Net-of-cost survival depends entirely on construction.
- Cites: Frazzini, Pedersen 2014, 'Betting Against Beta', JFE 111(1):1-25; Novy-Marx, Velikov 2022, 'Betting Against Betting Against Beta', JFE 143(1):80-106; 'Betting Against (Bad) Beta', Quantitative Finance 2025

**Quality/profitability and investment are the most robust survivors. Profitability (Novy-Marx) and QMJ (Asness-Frazzini-Pedersen) earn information ratios >1 in the US and across 24 countries with a negative market beta (defensive, good in crises). Feng-Giglio-Xiu's LASSO 'taming the factor zoo' finds most NEW factors redundant but profitability has significant marginal explanatory power beyond hundreds of factors. The HXZ q/q5 model (market, size, investment, profitability, + expected growth) is built precisely on these and prices the largest share of the 150 surviving anomalies (Profitability 40, Momentum 39, Intangibles 27, Investment 26, Value 15, Trading frictions only 3).**
- Effect size: QMJ information ratio >1 US + 24 countries; profitability survives FGX LASSO selection; q5 factors price ~150 NYSE/VW-significant anomalies. Of 150 survivors: Profitability 40, Momentum 39, Intangibles 27, Investment 26, Value 15, Trading frictions 3.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Robust post-2000 and internationally; quality also 'resurrects' the dead size effect post-1980 (Alquist-Israel-Moskowitz). These themes are the backbone of both q5 and JKP's 13 themes.
- Cites: Asness, Frazzini, Pedersen 2019, 'Quality Minus Junk', Review of Accounting Studies 24(1):34-112; Novy-Marx 2013, 'The Other Side of Value: Gross Profitability', JFE; Feng, Giglio, Xiu 2020, 'Taming the Factor Zoo', JF 75(3):1327-1370; Hou, Xue, Zhang 2015, 'Digesting Anomalies', RFS; Hou et al 2021 'q5', Rev. Finance

**Size alone is dead; only survives conditionally. The standalone SMB premium is ~0.11-0.18%/mo and statistically indistinguishable from zero since the early 1980s (Schwert; van Dijk). It revives only after controlling for quality/junk (Alquist-Israel-Moskowitz: quality-adjusted size is significant and larger internationally). Implication for harvesting: do not trade size as a standalone factor; use it as an interaction/conditioning variable.**
- Effect size: SMB ~0.11%/mo (1981-2006), insignificant; ~0.18%/mo (1951-2006). Was 4.8%/yr small-minus-large 1960-1979. Quality-controlled size significant in ~24 markets.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Dead standalone since 1980; conditional version (size x quality) holds. Microcap/illiquidity confounds make naive size a cost trap.
- Cites: van Dijk 2011, 'Is Size Dead?', J. Banking & Finance; Schwert 2003, Handbook of Economics of Finance; Alquist, Israel, Moskowitz 2018, 'Fact, Fiction, and the Size Effect', J. Portfolio Management (AQR)

**Forking paths / non-standard errors are the deepest robustness threat: defensible researcher choices generate dispersion comparable to statistical error. Menkveld's 164-team crowdsourcing experiment found non-standard errors 'on par with standard errors' for the same hypotheses on the same data. Coqueret et al show each extra degree of researcher freedom widens the t-stat range by >=30%, and that requiring robustness across ALL reasonable forking paths raises the honest significance bar to t>=8.2 -- far above the literature's t=3. This is the strongest argument that the binding constraint on real alpha is rigor (pre-registration, OOS, fixed protocol), not signal discovery.**
- Effect size: Non-standard errors ~= standard errors (Menkveld, 164 teams, 6 hypotheses); +30% t-range per extra researcher choice; full forking-path significance bar t>=8.2 (vs t=3 HLZ).
- Strength: strong · Recency: Menkveld JF 2024; Coqueret 'Forking Paths in Financial Economics' arXiv:2401.08606 (2024). Most current methodological frontier; directly cautions against in-sample factor mining.
- Cites: Menkveld et al 2024, 'Nonstandard Errors', JF 79(3):2339-2390; Coqueret et al 2024, 'Forking Paths in Financial Economics', arXiv:2401.08606

**Crypto cross-section is real but thin and liquidity-confounded. Liu-Tsyvinski-Wu (2022) show 10 characteristics form significant long-short strategies, ALL captured by a 3-factor model (crypto market + size + momentum, C-3). Size (small coins) and momentum (1-4 week) are the workhorses; value/fundamentals largely do NOT work. A trend factor (CTREND, aggregating 28 technical signals) prices the cross-section and survives transaction costs, rendering momentum insignificant. BUT recent crypto factor-zoo work finds 2-3 factors -- with liquidity (turnover-vol, bid-ask spread) and blockchain-native ratios dominating -- absorb all alphas, and anomalies concentrate in small/illiquid coins, exactly where costs bite (Cryptocurrency anomalies & economic constraints, 2024).**
- Effect size: C-3 prices 10 LS strategies (Liu-Tsyvinski-Wu); CTREND survives costs and beats C-3/CMOM (423 weekly obs); crypto LS Sharpe >1 in some studies but concentrated in illiquid coins; 2-3 liquidity-dominated factors eliminate alphas (2026 crypto factor zoo).
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Liu-Tsyvinski-Wu JF 2022; CTREND JFQA 2024; crypto factor zoo / anomalies-and-constraints 2024-2026. Short samples, severe survivorship/delisting bias, and high costs make crypto factor claims fragile.
- Cites: Liu, Tsyvinski, Wu 2022, 'Common Risk Factors in Cryptocurrency', JF 77(2):1133-1177 (SSRN 3379131); 'A Trend Factor for the Cross Section of Cryptocurrency Returns', JFQA 2024, doi:10.1017/S0022109024000747; 'Cryptocurrency anomalies and economic constraints', Int. Rev. Financial Analysis 94 (2024), S1057521924001509; 'Crypto factor zoo (.Zip)', Int. Rev. Financial Analysis 113 (2026), S1057521926000645

**Real-world net-of-cost evidence is genuinely contradictory and is the single most important thing to resolve for harvesting. Frazzini-Israel-Moskowitz (AQR, ~$1trn live trades, 19 markets, 1998-2011) find actual costs <1/10 of academic estimates and value+momentum scalable >$1bn-$100bn. Patton-Weller (7,320 mutual funds) find the opposite: real funds capture ~zero net momentum (costs 2.2-8.5%/yr) and lose 2.6-5.0%/yr on value. Novy-Marx-Velikov: low-turnover anomalies (<50%/mo) survive costs, high-turnover ones rarely do; mid-turnover trade costs 20-57 bps. Bottom line: cost survival is driven by turnover and execution skill, not the signal per se.**
- Effect size: Costs <1/10 academic + scalable (FIM) vs momentum net ~0, value -2.6 to -5.0%/yr (Patton-Weller); survival threshold ~50% monthly turnover (Novy-Marx-Velikov); mid-turnover trade cost 20-57 bps.
- Strength: contested · Recency: FIM 2018, Patton-Weller 2020, Novy-Marx-Velikov 2016. The contradiction (proprietary execution vs typical fund) is unresolved and is exactly what to test on own LOB/funding data.
- Cites: Frazzini, Israel, Moskowitz 2018, 'Trading Costs of Asset Pricing Anomalies', SSRN 2294498; Patton, Weller 2020, 'What You See Is Not What You Get', Management Science; Novy-Marx, Velikov 2016, 'A Taxonomy of Anomalies and Their Trading Costs', RFS 29(1):104-147

**Cross-asset replication is even WORSE than equities where data is noisier, confirming that 'survival' is data-quality-dependent. The corporate bond factor literature faces a severe replication crisis: before correction 119 of 432 specifications are nominally significant (t>1.96) but only ~22 survive an FDR correction, and only 26 (6.0%) retain significant CAPM alpha after bias-correcting illiquid-bond pricing errors. Short-term reversal's premium collapses from -0.99%/mo to -0.09%/mo (t -4.46 to -0.51) after correcting stale-price bias (>90% of the effect was bias). Non-standard error (NSE) of the premium (0.35%/mo) exceeds the average premium itself (0.33%/mo).**
- Effect size: Bonds: 26/432 (6.0%) survive; only ~22 survive FDR; ST-reversal -0.99% -> -0.09%/mo; NSE 0.35%/mo > mean premium 0.33%/mo. In a typical year 70% of bonds trade <=10 days.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Dickerson, Robotti, Rossetti 2025-2026 (arXiv:2604.07880); part of a 2023-2026 wave (also Duarte et al, Bessembinder et al) on bond-factor fragility. Cautionary analogue for crypto/illiquid markets.
- Cites: Dickerson, Robotti, Rossetti 2026, 'The Corporate Bond Factor Replication Crisis', arXiv:2604.07880; Dickerson, Robotti, Nozawa 2025 (bond liquidity); Bessembinder et al 2023 (data errors)

### Testable hypotheses
- H1 (crypto momentum survives costs?): On top-50 coins (2024-02 to 2026-06), a weekly-rebalanced cross-sectional momentum LS (1-4 week lookback, value-weighted by market cap a la Liu-Tsyvinski-Wu C-3) earns gross weekly Sharpe >0 but net Sharpe <=0 after realistic taker fees (~5-10 bps) + bid-ask + funding. Falsifiable: if net annualized Sharpe stays >0.5 after costs, momentum is harvestable in crypto.
- H2 (liquidity dominates the crypto factor zoo): Following the 2026 crypto factor-zoo result, a 2-3 factor model with a turnover-volatility / bid-ask-spread / Amihud-illiquidity factor will drive the alpha of crypto size and momentum LS portfolios to insignificance (|t|<1.96). Falsifiable: if size/momentum alphas remain significant after controlling for an illiquidity factor built from our LOB data, the cross-section is NOT just liquidity.
- H3 (anomalies concentrate in illiquid coins): Crypto LS factor returns are monotonically larger in the bottom-liquidity tercile (lowest dollar volume / widest spread) and shrink toward zero in the top-liquidity tercile (BTC/ETH/majors). Falsifiable: if returns are flat or larger in liquid coins, the McLean-Pontiff limits-to-arbitrage story does not hold in crypto.
- H4 (low-vol regime dependence): A crypto low-volatility / low-beta LS (sort top-50 on trailing 30d realized vol or beta-to-BTC) earns positive returns in the post-2017-style regime but flips sign in high-momentum bull phases. Falsifiable: stable significant low-vol premium across our 2024-2026 sub-periods would contradict the 'regime-dependent / no premium pre-2019' literature.
- H5 (forking-paths fragility on our own signals): For any single equity or crypto anomaly we build, enumerate >=100 defensible specification paths (lookback, weighting, breakpoint, winsorization, rebalance freq, universe filter). Hypothesis: the in-sample t-stat distribution spans both <1.96 and >3, and the median path has t materially below the best path. Falsifiable: if a signal clears t>=3 across >90% of paths AND out-of-sample, it is a genuine robust effect (rare).
- H6 (US equity decay): Re-running classic anomalies (12-1 momentum, gross profitability, asset growth/investment, book-to-market) on our 1-yr S&P 500 sample, post-2020 realized long-short returns are materially below their published in-sample magnitudes (consistent with McLean-Pontiff 58% post-pub decay), and the gap is larger for 'mechanical' signals (momentum) than 'judgment' signals (value), per the 2024 hyperbolic-crowding model.
- H7 (quality is the robust survivor): A profitability/quality LS (gross profits-to-assets, or QMJ-style composite) on S&P 500 has the highest net-of-cost information ratio and lowest turnover among momentum/value/size/quality, and survives costs where momentum does not. Falsifiable: if quality's net IR is below momentum's or insignificant in our sample, the 'quality is most robust' claim fails on our data.
- H8 (cost survival = turnover, not signal): Across all anomalies we test, net Sharpe is a steep negative function of monthly turnover, with the ~50%/month threshold of Novy-Marx-Velikov separating survivors from non-survivors, independent of which factor it is. Falsifiable: if low-turnover factors also fail to survive costs, costs are not the binding constraint.
- H9 (size is dead standalone, alive conditional): A standalone crypto or equity size LS is insignificant net of costs, but a size x quality (or size x low-illiquidity) interaction is significant -- replicating Alquist-Israel-Moskowitz in our universe.
- H10 (multiple-testing honesty): Apply Harvey-Liu-Zhu / Benjamini-Hochberg FDR control to the full set of signals we mine; hypothesis is that the number surviving a 5% FDR hurdle (roughly t>=2.7-3.0) is <=20% of nominally significant signals, matching Chen's worst-case FDR<=22% only if we are disciplined.

### Harvest strategies
- Crypto cross-sectional momentum (the most documented crypto factor): weekly-rebalanced LS on top-50 coins, long top-quintile / short bottom-quintile by trailing 1-4 week return, value-weighted by market cap (Liu-Tsyvinski-Wu C-3). Cost drag: ~2x weekly turnover x (taker fee ~5-10 bps + half-spread ~5-30 bps for small coins) ~= 20-80 bps/week round-trip; this is the make-or-break. Use limit/maker orders and a no-trade band to cut turnover. Express the short via perpetual futures (use our 228-perp funding history) -- funding can ADD to or subtract from carry.
- Crypto trend factor (CTREND-style): aggregate ~20-28 technical signals (moving-average crossovers, momentum oscillators) into one composite trend score per coin, value-weighted weekly LS. JFQA evidence says it survives costs and subsumes plain momentum -- test whether the signal-aggregation reduces turnover/noise vs single-signal momentum. Cost drag similar to H1 but potentially lower turnover.
- Crypto carry/funding factor (native, not in equity zoo): LS on perpetual funding rates -- short coins with extreme positive funding (longs pay), long coins with negative funding -- harvesting the funding premium. Cost drag: funding is received/paid every 1-8h with no spread cost on the carry leg itself, but entry/exit spread + the risk that funding mean-reverts. Use Coinalyze funding/OI and our 23k-hour funding history; cross-check with liquidations as a crowding signal.
- Equity quality/profitability LS (lowest-turnover survivor): on S&P 500, long high gross-profits-to-assets / QMJ-composite, short low, monthly or quarterly rebalance. Turnover <50%/mo -> per Novy-Marx-Velikov this is the category most likely to clear costs. Cost drag: ~10-35 bps round-trip on liquid large caps x low turnover -> small net drag. Use FnSpID fundamentals to build the quality score.
- Equity value with timely prices (Devil-in-HML): build book-to-price using current (monthly) prices, not 6-18 month lagged, to capture the +305-378 bps/yr alpha edge over standard HML. Combine with quality (avoid value traps). Cost drag low (annual fundamentals, low turnover). Test net IR vs standard annually-lagged HML.
- Multi-factor composite / tangency (JKP lesson): rather than trade single factors, combine value+momentum+quality+investment into one cross-sectionally-ranked composite and trade the composite -- diversification across weakly-correlated themes raises Sharpe and the JKP result says the ensemble is more robust than any single factor. Net the trades across factors before execution to slash turnover (a value buy can offset a momentum sell), directly attacking the Patton-Weller cost problem.
- Avoid (paper-only / cost traps): standalone size, short-term reversal (highest turnover, dies on costs and stale-price bias per the bond analogue), naive equal-weighted small/microcap LS (HXZ: this is where 'crisis' anomalies live), and uncorrected BAB rank-weighting (Novy-Marx-Velikov artifact). In crypto, avoid LS that goes deep into bottom-decile illiquid coins -- that is where spreads/slippage destroy the paper alpha.

### Pitfalls
- Methodology-as-result (the #1 trap): HXZ's 65% failure becomes 41% just by switching VW->EW; JKP's 35% becomes 82% with proper Bayesian MT; value's strength swings 305-378 bps on lagged-vs-timely prices. Any single specification of a backtest is one forking path; report the DISTRIBUTION across reasonable choices, not the best path.
- Forking paths / non-standard errors (Menkveld 2024, Coqueret 2024): defensible choices generate dispersion on par with statistical error; full forking-path honesty pushes the bar to t>=8.2. Pre-register the protocol (lookback, weighting, breakpoints, winsorization, rebalance, universe) BEFORE seeing results, or the in-sample t-stat is meaningless.
- Multiple testing / data snooping: with hundreds of candidate signals, t>1.96 guarantees false discoveries. Use FDR control (Benjamini-Hochberg) or the HLZ t>3.0 hurdle; but note Chen's caveat that 3.0 may be too conservative when true effects are common -- so report FDR explicitly rather than a single hurdle.
- Post-publication / crowding decay (McLean-Pontiff 58%; 2024 hyperbolic model): every well-known factor's live alpha is a fraction of its paper value; crowding ACCELERATED post-2015, hitting 'mechanical' signals (momentum) hardest. Crypto factors copied straight from equity papers are already arbitraged in liquid coins. Assume realized alpha << backtest alpha.
- Transaction-cost denial: the FIM-vs-Patton-Weller contradiction means you CANNOT assume AQR-style <1/10 costs without proprietary execution. For retail/small AUM, use conservative costs (taker fees, full half-spread, slippage, funding) and turnover-aware design; momentum's 2.2-8.5%/yr implementation cost can erase the entire premium.
- Microcap / illiquid-coin contamination: in equities, microcaps (3.2% of cap, 60.7% of names) drive most 'anomalies' and are uninvestable; in crypto, small coins with wide spreads and delisting risk are the analogue. Value-weight and screen by liquidity, or the paper alpha is an illiquidity-premium mirage you cannot capture net.
- Survivorship / delisting bias in crypto: top-50 today != top-50 in 2024; dead coins (LUNA-style) and delistings create severe look-ahead/survivorship bias that inflates momentum and size factors. Reconstruct the historical universe point-in-time; a 2.4-yr crypto sample is far too short for stable factor inference (vs decades in equities).
- Stale-price / bias inflation (bond analogue): in illiquid assets, infrequent trading makes returns appear predictable (the bond ST-reversal premium was 90% bias). Crypto small-coin reversal/illiquidity signals are vulnerable to the same artifact -- the 'edge' may be a pricing-error mirage.
- Short-sample over-fitting on our data: 1 yr of S&P 500, 2.4 yr of crypto, 2 months of LOB snapshots are tiny relative to the parameter space of factor strategies; in-sample Sharpe will be wildly optimistic. Reserve strict OOS holdouts and prefer cross-sectional breadth (many names) over time-series length where possible.
- Crowding/regime fragility: low-vol had NO crypto premium pre-2019; value had a -55% decade. Factors are regime-dependent; a strategy fit on 2024-2026 crypto (a specific regime) may invert. Stress-test across sub-periods and assume regime change.

### Data needed
- Point-in-time crypto universe / delisting history: the single biggest gap. Need historical top-N membership and delisted-coin returns to kill survivorship bias. FREE sources: CoinGecko / CoinMarketCap historical snapshots, Kaiko/Amberdata trials, or reconstruct from our own OHLCV by tracking entries/exits. Without this, crypto factor backtests are biased upward.
- Realistic crypto execution costs: per-coin historical bid-ask spreads and depth (we have 56M SPY/QQQ LOB but need crypto LOB / quote data) + exchange taker/maker fee schedules. Use our Coinalyze + perp funding + Databento-style crypto L2 if obtainable; otherwise Binance/Bybit public trade+book archives (FREE).
- Longer equity factor history with point-in-time fundamentals: 1 yr of S&P 500 is too short. FREE: Ken French Data Library (factor returns + portfolios, decades, monthly/daily), Open Source Asset Pricing (openassetpricing.com -- Chen-Zimmermann, 200+ signals with code), AQR datasets (QMJ, BAB, Devil-in-HML factors, monthly/daily). These give validated benchmarks to calibrate decay.
- FX (to be sourced) for carry/value/momentum cross-asset tests: FREE: FRED (spot, forward points via interest-rate differentials), BIS, investing.com. Needed to test whether factor themes (carry, value, momentum) generalize cross-asset (JKP's external-validity argument).
- Commodities futures term structure (to be sourced): FREE: Nasdaq Data Link/Quandl free tiers, CME public settlement data, Stevens Continuous Futures. Needed for carry/momentum/basis factors as an OOS cross-asset robustness check.
- Equity options / VIX (to be sourced): FREE: Cboe (VIX/VVIX/SKEW history, delayed option chains), OptionMetrics (academic), Deribit (we already have BTC/ETH IV surfaces + DVOL 2021-2026 for crypto-vol factors). Needed for vol-risk-premium and low-vol cross-checks.
- Multiple-testing / replication toolkit: the JKP code (github.com/bkelly-lab/ReplicationCrisis) and Chen-Zimmermann code (github.com/chenandrewy) -- both FREE/open-source -- to implement Bayesian shrinkage, FDR control, and the exact replication protocol on our own signals.
- Funding/borrow costs for short legs: crypto perp funding (have it), but for equity shorts need stock-loan/borrow fees (hard-to-borrow names destroy short-leg alpha). FREE proxies: IBKR borrow-rate snapshots; otherwise assume conservative borrow on small/illiquid shorts.

### Adversarial verification — reliability: **medium**
_Net-of-cost reality:_ Blunt take: the factor literature largely survives as STATISTICS and largely dies as HARVESTABLE NET-OF-COST ALPHA -- and the report's own synthesis gets this right even though one key number (BAB) is wrong by 12x. What independent research supports: (1) Effects are real in-sample and mostly persist gross OOS (Chen-Zimmermann ~74% persist; JKP 82.4% replicate) -- there is no 'it was all data-mining' crisis. (2) But decay is real and accelerating: ~26% OOS and ~50-58% post-publication on average (McLean-Pontiff), and WORSE/faster for mechanical, crowded signals post-2015 (momentum hyperbolic decay, ETF-driven, predicted 0.30 vs realized 0.15 alpha for 2016-2024). (3) Net of realistic costs the survivor set is small and turnover-determined: low-turnover quality/value-with-timely-prices plausibly clear costs; high-turnover momentum and short-term reversal plausibly do not for non-elite execution. The FIM-vs-Patton-Weller contradiction is genuine and unresolved, but the adversarial reading favors Patton-Weller for anyone without proprietary, sub-decimal execution -- FIM is explicitly a best-case LOWER BOUND from a single elite manager. (4) The honest significance bar is far above t=2-3: forking paths push it toward t>=8.2 (Coqueret) and non-standard errors rival statistical errors (Menkveld). Practical implication for this user's harvesting program: assume realized alpha << backtest alpha; treat any single specification as one forking path and report the distribution; budget conservative costs (full half-spread + taker fees + funding + borrow); prefer low-turnover, multi-theme composites that net trades across factors; and be especially skeptical of (a) the BAB/low-vol premium net of its ~60% cost haircut and (b) momentum net of 2.2-8.5%/yr implementation costs. The 'crisis vs no-crisis' debate is largely resolved into: real effects, small robust theme set (value, momentum, profitability/quality, investment, contested low-risk), size dead standalone -- but the net-of-cost survivor count is materially smaller than even the optimistic statistical replication rates suggest.
- **[WEAKENED]** Low-risk/BAB: value-weighted BAB earns 'only ~56 bps/yr excess return' so the famous BAB Sharpe (0.78-1.08) is largely a construction artifact; costs cut profitability ~60%; ~$1.05/$1 goes to bottom-1%-cap stocks. — The report contains a hard 12x unit error that materially distorts the conclusion in BOTH directions. Novy-Marx & Velikov's actual figure is 56 bps PER MONTH (t=3.5, Sharpe 0.49), not 56 bps/yr. So value-weighting does NOT collapse the low-risk premium to a trivial ~0.56%/yr; it earns ~6.7%/yr gross with t=3.5 -- a statistically robust effect. The pieces the report gets right: the Sharpe drops from ~1.08 to 0.49 when you remove the non-standard rank-weighting, ~$1.05/$1 sits in bottom-1%-cap (micro/nano) stocks, and transaction costs reduce BAB profitability by ~60%. So 'a real low-risk effect exists but the headline number overstates harvestable alpha' is the correct conclusion -- but the report's own supporting statistic (56 bps/yr) is wrong by an order of magnitude and, if taken literally, OVER-states the death of the premium. Net of the ~60% cost haircut, VW BAB net is ~22 bps/month -- weakened but not dead. Adversarial verdict: the artifact claim is directionally fine but the load-bearing number is wrong; harvestable BAB alpha is more robust gross, and more cost-fragile net, than the report's single garbled figure conveys.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Net-of-cost survival is genuinely contradictory and unresolved: Frazzini-Israel-Moskowitz (~$1trn live trades) find costs <1/10 of academic estimates and value/momentum scalable, while Patton-Weller (7,320 mutual funds) find momentum implementation costs of 2.2-8.5%/yr that eliminate the net premium and value -2.6 to -5.0%/yr. — Both anchor studies are accurately characterized and the contradiction is real and unresolved in the literature. FIM (1998-2011, 19 markets, ~$1trn) do find actual costs <1/10 of prior estimates with order-of-magnitude larger capacity; Patton-Weller (1970-2016, 7,320 US funds) do find 2.2-8.5%/yr momentum implementation costs that leave typical funds with ~zero net momentum and negative net value. ADVERSARIAL TILT (consistent with the 'alpha is overstated after costs' prior): the literature itself frames FIM as a single institutional manager that 'may not be representative of asset managers as a whole' and provides 'an informative LOWER BOUND' on costs -- i.e., a best-case execution benchmark, not the typical experience. Patton-Weller measure what real, diversified pools of managers actually capture. For any non-elite/retail/small-AUM implementation, the honest prior should weight Patton-Weller more heavily: momentum's net premium is plausibly near zero. The report's own 'bottom line' (survival is driven by turnover and execution skill, not the signal) is the correct and appropriately cautious synthesis.
- **[CONFIRMED]** McLean-Pontiff decay is large and real: average long-short returns fall 26% out-of-sample and 58% post-publication; crowding ACCELERATED post-2015, hitting 'mechanical' signals (momentum) hardest (2024 hyperbolic-decay model, momentum R2=0.65; predicted 0.30 vs actual 0.15 alpha for 2016-2024). — The 26% OOS / ~58% post-publication figures match the original JF 2016 paper (the 58% is sometimes restated as ~50% in the follow-on literature, e.g. Chen-Zimmermann; the 26%/58% pair is the original abstract and is reported correctly). The decay thesis is independently corroborated and SHARPENED by fresh 2024-2026 evidence: the 'Not All Factors Crowd Equally' paper (arXiv:2512.11913) confirms momentum exhibits hyperbolic alpha decay (R2=0.65, beating linear 0.51 / exponential 0.61), that crowding accelerated post-2015 in step with factor-ETF growth (rho=-0.63), and that 1995-2015-trained models over-predict 2016-2024 alpha (0.30 predicted vs 0.15 realized) -- exactly the mechanical-signal fragility the report claims. This is the single most prior-confirming finding: published alpha demonstrably decays, and the decay is worse and faster than the original 2016 estimates for crowded, mechanical signals. CAVEAT the report correctly flags: Chen-Zimmermann argue the bias-corrected (data-mining) component is only ~12-15%, with the remainder attributable to learning/arbitrage/economic change -- i.e., the 58% is real decay but not all 'fake discovery.'
- **[CONFIRMED]** The 'no-crisis' rebuttal: Jensen-Kelly-Pedersen find 82.4% of 153 factors replicate (vs HXZ's ~35%) under a Bayesian/multiple-testing model, clustering into 13 themes and working OOS across 93 countries; Chen-Zimmermann find ~100% pure-replication, FDR <10-22%, t-inflation <=28%, so t-hurdles need NOT be raised. — Every headline number is reported accurately. JKP (JF 2023): 82.4% replication on CAPM-alpha tests, 13 themes, OOS in 93 countries, evidence strengthened by more factors. Chen-Zimmermann (CFR 2022; arXiv:2209.13623): four stylized facts (near-100% pure-replication; ~74% of returns persist OOS = consistent with MP's 26% decline; t-stats mostly >3; weak cross-correlations), FDR <10% (their simple model ~0.4%, shrinkage ~10% of in-sample mean), and the explicit conclusion that t-hurdles need not be raised. HXZ's 65%-fail / ~35%-replicate is also reported correctly. IMPORTANT ADVERSARIAL CAVEAT the report should foreground more: JKP/Chen establish STATISTICAL replication (the effects are real in-sample and persist gross OOS), NOT net-of-cost harvestable alpha. JKP themselves shrink estimates heavily, and even optimists concede ~15 factors span the entire zoo and that 'new' anomalies add little portfolio value net of costs ('Has the Factor Zoo Paid Off?', Swade-Hanauer-Lohre-Blitz). So 'no replication crisis' is NOT the same as 'lots of harvestable alpha' -- the two camps converge on a small set of robust THEMES, and the practitioner-relevant count shrinks further after costs, exactly as the report concludes.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Forking paths / non-standard errors are the deepest robustness threat: Menkveld's 164-team study finds non-standard errors on par with standard errors; Coqueret et al. show each extra researcher choice widens the t-range >=30% and requiring robustness across ALL reasonable forking paths raises the honest significance bar to t>=8.2 (vs t=3 HLZ). — Both frontier methodological claims check out precisely against the primary sources. Coqueret, 'Forking Paths in Financial Economics' (arXiv:2401.08606): at the 5% level the bootstrapped significance threshold is ~4.5 but the forking-paths threshold is 'at least 8.2,' and 'each additional degree of freedom in the protocol expands the average range of t-statistics by at least 30%' -- verbatim matches. Menkveld et al., 'Nonstandard Errors' (JF 79(3) 2024, 164 teams, 6 hypotheses) find non-standard errors on par with standard errors. This is the most prior-consistent methodological result: it implies that any single backtest specification is one draw from a wide forking-paths distribution, so a reported in-sample t-stat near the conventional 2-3 range is close to meaningless unless it survives the full path distribution and OOS. Strong support for the report's conclusion that rigor (pre-registration, OOS, fixed protocol, cost-awareness) -- not signal discovery -- is the binding constraint on real, harvestable alpha.

---

## Crypto funding carry, factors and stat-arb  `crypto_carry_statarb`

Crypto carry is the standout harvestable anomaly in this space: short-perp / long-spot delta-neutral carry posted spectacular gross Sharpes (Borri-Liu-Tsyvinski-Wu report 6.45 full-sample 2020-2025), the fixed-date basis exceeded 40% p.a. at peaks and averaged ~7% p.a. (BIS WP1087, 2019-2024), and the premium is a genuine compensation for funding/liquidation risk and regulation-induced segmentation — NOT free arbitrage. Crucially it has DECAYED hard: the spot-BTC-ETF launch (Jan 2024) cut carry ~3pp (DiD), the trade that paid ~25% in early 2024 paid <5% by late 2025, and the strategy turned negative in 2025; realistic delta-neutral APY is now 8-20% in positive-funding regimes, 0-5% in chop, negative in bear unwinds. Cross-sectional factors: a market+size+momentum 3-factor model (Liu-Tsyvinski-Wu, JF 2022) prices the cross-section, with ~9-10 characteristics yielding significant gross long-shorts; but the size effect (small tercile +317%/yr gross) is an illiquidity premium concentrated in sub-10%-mcap coins that does not survive costs/shortability, and rigorous re-assessment (Han-Kang-Ryu) shows market-neutral momentum is essentially unattainable net — short legs get liquidated (most plunge ~99%), profits live only in the long leg of large coins (max Sharpe ~1.5 vs literature's >2). The robust cross-sectional survivor is a short-horizon trend/technical factor (Fieberg et al. CTREND, JFQA 2024): 3.87%/wk gross, annualized Sharpe 1.94, breakeven cost 141bps so it clears realistic 15-40bps even in liquid coins. A post-2017 low-volatility REVERSAL (low-vol now outperforms) is newly documented. Stat-arb: pairs/cointegration and PCA eigenportfolio mean-reversion show high in-sample win rates but fragile, often unprofitable net OOS in crypto; the durable cross-exchange edge (Makarov-Schoar, JFE 2020: >15% avg, 40% peak Korea-US spreads) was a 2017-18 capital-controls artifact that has largely closed. Bottom line: funding carry (cost-aware, risk-managed, regime-conditioned) and short-horizon trend are the harvestable edges; size/illiquidity and most stat-arb are paper-or-microcap artifacts net of cost.

### Findings

**Crypto carry (short-perp/long-spot delta-neutral, or long-spot/short-fixed-future cash-and-carry) earns a large premium that is compensation for funding/liquidation risk and regulation-induced market segmentation, NOT riskless arbitrage. The premium is ~10x larger than commodity or S&P 500 carry.**
- Effect size: BIS WP1087: avg annualized basis ~7% p.a. (Apr 2019-Jul 2024), peaks >40% p.a.; futures leg of cash-and-carry earns ~17% per MONTH gross excess return but with severe drawdowns; carry ~10x commodity/S&P carry. Borri-Liu-Tsyvinski-Wu (2025): delta-neutral carry annualized Sharpe 6.45 full sample (Aug2020-May2025); funding-rate leg mean ~8%/yr, vol ~0.8% (very high reward/risk on the carry leg alone). Carry predicts liquidations: +10% standardized carry -> +22% of OI in short-side liquidations next month.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Post-2020 strong then decaying. Borri et al.: Sharpe 6.45 full sample, 4.06 in 2024, NEGATIVE in 2025. BIS: spot-BTC-ETF (Jan 2024) cut carry by ~3pp in DiD (declines of 36% and 97% of mean basis depending on horizon). Practitioner: basis that paid ~25% early-2024 paid <5% late-2025; realized delta-neutral APY now 8-20% positive-funding, 0-5% choppy, negative in bear unwinds; Binance VIP0 break-even funding ~0.007%/8h.
- Cites: Schmeling, Schrimpf, Todorov 2023, 'Crypto Carry', BIS Working Paper No. 1087 (bis.org/publ/work1087.pdf); Borri, Liu, Tsyvinski, Wu 2025, 'Cryptocurrency as an Investable Asset Class: Coming of Age', arXiv:2510.14435; CEPR/VoxEU column 'Crypto carry: Market segmentation and price distortions' (Schmeling-Schrimpf-Todorov)

**Perpetual-futures prices deviate from no-arbitrage bounds far more than traditional FX; a threshold trading strategy on the funding/basis deviation earns large Sharpes even at the highest retail Binance costs. Deviations comove across coins and shrink as markets mature.**
- Effect size: He-Manela-Ross-von Wachter: mean absolute perp futures-spot spread ~60-100% per YEAR across coins (vs much smaller CIP deviations in Du-Tepper-Verdelhan FX). BTC perp deviation-trading strategy Sharpe ~1.8 under high retail trading costs, up to ~6.5 at low/institutional costs. Funding rate typically positive (longs pay shorts).
- Strength: strong · Recency: Deviations explicitly diminish over time as liquidity improves (2018-2022 sample); consistent with the post-2024 carry compression. Edge persists net of cost but is shrinking.
- Cites: He, Manela, Ross, von Wachter 2022/2023, 'Fundamentals of Perpetual Futures', arXiv:2212.06888 / SSRN 4301150; Du, Tepper, Verdelhan 2018, 'Deviations from Covered Interest Rate Parity', Journal of Finance 73(3) (FX benchmark)

**A 3-factor model — crypto market (CMKT), size (CSMB), momentum (CMOM) — prices the cross-section of crypto returns; ~9-10 price/market characteristics form significant gross long-short strategies, all subsumed by the 3 factors. Time-series momentum and investor-attention proxies also forecast returns.**
- Effect size: Liu-Tsyvinski-Wu (JF 2022): ~9-10 characteristics give significant long-shorts, all explained by the 3-factor model. Borri et al. weekly long-short returns: CMOM +2.6%/wk full sample (+2.1% post-2020); CSIZE -2.3%/wk full (-0.9% post-2020, i.e. small>big); CVALUE -3.5%/wk full (-2.3% post-2020). Liu-Tsyvinski (RFS 2021): strong time-series momentum at 1-4 week horizons; attention (Google/social) forecasts returns.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Factors persist post-2020 but premia attenuate (size effect roughly halves). Gross/in-sample evidence; these papers largely ignore realistic trading costs and shortability.
- Cites: Liu, Tsyvinski, Wu 2022, 'Common Risk Factors in Cryptocurrency', Journal of Finance 77(2):1133-1177 (NBER w25882); Liu, Tsyvinski 2021, 'Risks and Returns of Cryptocurrency', Review of Financial Studies 34(6):2689-2727 (NBER w24877); Borri, Liu, Tsyvinski, Wu 2025, arXiv:2510.14435 (Table 2)

**The crypto SIZE effect is enormous gross but is an illiquidity premium concentrated in the very smallest coins (<10% of mcap); it is a microcap/illiquidity artifact, not harvestable net of cost. Largest coins show daily MOMENTUM while small coins show daily REVERSAL.**
- Effect size: Cross-section studies: SMB sorted on mcap ~1.01%/DAY gross; bottom (small) tercile ~+317% annualized vs top (large) tercile ~-50%. Effect lives in coins that are <10% of total mcap and barely tradeable; daily reversal in small/illiquid coins, daily momentum in the handful of large liquid coins.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Robust in-sample post-2020 but fundamentally not investable: the long leg is illiquid microcaps with massive price impact and the short leg is unshortable. A paper-only premium net of realistic frictions.
- Cites: Liu, Tsyvinski, Wu 2022, Journal of Finance (size = illiquidity proxy); Zhang et al., 'Up or down? Short-term reversal, momentum, and liquidity effects in cryptocurrency markets' (RG 354881251); 'The Cross-Section of Cryptocurrency Returns' (RG 359081644)

**Under REALISTIC assumptions (daily mark-to-market, 15bps costs, futures-shortability constraints) crypto cross-sectional MOMENTUM does not deliver steady market-neutral profit: short legs get liquidated (most plunge ~99% in 2017/2020 bull runs), and profit survives only in the LONG leg of LARGE coins. Max achievable Sharpe ~1.5, well below the >2 claimed by gross studies.**
- Effect size: Han-Kang-Ryu: best TS-momentum Sharpe 1.51 (mkt 0.84); best XS-momentum Sharpe 1.28 (mkt 1.01); long-only momentum Sharpe range 0.95-1.62 (top-5% coins), all long-only beat market net of 15bps; short-only portfolios mostly liquidated. After adding a cross-overreaction (CS-CO) factor the Liu et al. size and momentum factors become insignificant. Cost model: 15bps round-trip (Binance spot 10bps, futures 4.5bps, tick 3.26bps, avg slippage 1.53bps).
- Strength: strong · Recency: Sample to Aug 2023, explicitly designed to update prior optimistic crypto-momentum papers. Directly contradicts the harvestability of market-neutral XS momentum.
- Cites: Han, Kang, Ryu 2023/2024, 'Time-Series and Cross-Sectional Momentum in the Cryptocurrency Market: A Comprehensive Analysis under Realistic Assumptions', AUT Centre for Financial Research working paper

**A short-horizon TREND/technical factor (CTREND) aggregating price+volume across horizons is the most robust harvestable cross-sectional crypto factor: it survives realistic costs, persists in big/liquid coins, prices the cross-section, and subsumes the momentum factor.**
- Effect size: Fieberg et al. (JFQA 2024): long-short 3.87%/wk gross (t=5.19), annualized Sharpe 1.94, weekly alpha 2.62% (t=4.22). Turnover 68%/wk; net returns 2.90% (t=3.89) to 2.35% (t=3.16) under 30-60bps cost scenarios; BREAKEVEN cost 141bps to zero the return, 88bps to lose 5% significance. In 10% largest coins return 2.51%, in liquid coins 4.36% — harvestable in tradeable universe. >3,000 coins, Apr2015-May2022.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Top-journal (JFQA), survives costs and concentrates in liquid coins — the cleanest factor evidence. Pre-2023 sample; OOS persistence post-2023 untested in this paper.
- Cites: Fieberg, Liedtke, Zaremba et al. 2024, 'A Trend Factor for the Cross Section of Cryptocurrency Returns', Journal of Financial and Quantitative Analysis (S0022109024000747); Han, Zhou, Zhu 2016 (base trend-factor methodology, equities)

**The LOW-VOLATILITY anomaly has REVERSED in crypto: in the post-2017 era low-realized-vol coins systematically outperform high-vol coins (a low-vol premium), opposite to early crypto findings where high-vol/lottery coins won. Interpreted as market maturation (more liquidity, depth, institutions).**
- Effect size: Recent (2026) work documents a statistically and economically meaningful low-vol premium post-2017 across multiple formation/holding windows; low-vol coins outperform high-vol. Earlier (pre-2020) papers found idiosyncratic-vol/lottery coins outperformed (positive IVOL-return relation). Liquidity-volatility premium negative (~-4.0% to -4.6%/yr) in broad markets.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: A genuine post-2017 sign flip; newer and less replicated than momentum/carry. Net-of-cost evidence thin.
- Cites: 'Revisiting the low-volatility anomaly in cryptocurrency markets' 2026, Finance Research Letters (S1544612326003818); 'Is idiosyncratic volatility priced in cryptocurrency markets?' Research in International Business and Finance (S0275531920301926); 'Cryptocurrencies and the low volatility anomaly' Finance Research Letters (S154461232030667X)

**Cross-exchange / cross-country crypto arbitrage produced large recurrent spreads driven by capital controls and segmented liquidity, but this was largely a 2017-18 phenomenon that has since compressed; the durable lesson is segmentation/limits-to-arbitrage, not a persistent harvestable edge today.**
- Effect size: Makarov-Schoar (JFE 2020): Korea-US BTC spread >15% avg, peak ~40% (Dec2017-Feb2018); Japan-US ~10%; US-Europe ~3%; WITHIN-country spreads typically <1%; >$2B aggregate potential arb profit; opportunities persist for days. Common volume component explains ~80% of BTC returns (85% daily); buying 10,000 BTC moves price ~+4% (Kyle lambda). 15 exchanges, 19 countries, Jan2017-Feb2018.
- Strength: strong · Recency: The headline spreads are specific to 2017-18 capital-controls era and have largely closed; treat as evidence of segmentation/limits-to-arbitrage rather than a live edge. CEX-DEX latency/MEV arb persists but needs infra we lack.
- Cites: Makarov, Schoar 2020, 'Trading and Arbitrage in Cryptocurrency Markets', Journal of Financial Economics 135(2):293-319

**Crypto pairs/cointegration and PCA eigenportfolio (Ornstein-Uhlenbeck residual mean-reversion) stat-arb show very high IN-SAMPLE win rates but are fragile and frequently unprofitable net of cost OOS; cointegration relationships are unstable in crypto and PCA mean-reversion is 'not robust' in crypto markets.**
- Effect size: Practitioner/working-paper backtests: ~100% in-sample win rates collapse to 79-100% live with excess returns ranging -0.4% to +8.1% per trade; only ~40% of top spread opportunities (>=20bps) profitable after costs and spread reversals; ~17% of observations show >=20bps spreads. PCA eigenportfolio OU mean-reversion explicitly reported 'not robust' in crypto. Generic crypto round-trip cost ~15bps + slippage; spreads must clear 2x legs.
- Strength: weak · Recency: 2020-2026 working papers/practitioner; heavy survivorship and in-sample selection. No top-journal evidence of a robust net-positive crypto stat-arb book. Treat claimed Sharpes skeptically.
- Cites: Jung 2025, 'Statistical Arbitrage within Crypto Markets using PCA', SSRN 5263475; Avellaneda, Lee 2010, 'Statistical Arbitrage in the US Equities Market', Quantitative Finance (PCA/OU methodology baseline); Dada (Digital Alpha Research) 'Pairs Trading Statistical Arbitrage Approach on Digital Assets'

**A comprehensive cost-of-carry / 'anatomy' framework for perpetual returns finds many predictors significant on TOTAL return (price + funding) but emphasizes that returns must be evaluated net of funding fees; basis/carry, momentum, liquidity, size, volatility categories all contribute.**
- Effect size: Cao, Luo, Cheng, Dong (SSRN 6365329, 2026): cost-of-carry model implies positive convenience yield, negligible off-chain storage; ~170 predictors across basis/momentum/liquidity/size/volatility; 63 yield statistically significant TOTAL returns (price move + funding-fee yield) in portfolio sorts.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: 2026 working paper, perp-specific and explicitly funding-aware; not yet peer-reviewed/replicated. Useful predictor taxonomy.
- Cites: Cao, Luo, Cheng, Dong 2026, 'Anatomy of Cryptocurrency Perpetual Futures Returns', SSRN 6365329

### Testable hypotheses
- H1 (carry as signal, cross-sectional): Using the 228 perps x ~23k hours of funding history, sorting coins each 8h/daily into quintiles by trailing 7-30d average funding and going short-perp/long-spot (or short high-funding vs long low-funding perp) earns positive returns. Falsifiable: net Sharpe <= 0 after 15bps round-trip + actual funding paid/received. Predict gross Sharpe 2-5, net 0.5-2, with sharp decay in 2025 (turns negative in bear unwinds).
- H2 (carry decay / regime break): Funding-carry Sharpe estimated on rolling 6-month windows shows a structural break down after Jan-2024 (spot ETF). Falsifiable: no significant decline in mean funding or carry Sharpe pre/post 2024-01 in our 2024-02 to 2026-06 sample (note: our sample starts right at the ETF launch, so test the gradient WITHIN 2024-2026 — predict monotone compression toward 0-5% APY by 2025-2026).
- H3 (funding as RETURN predictor, not just carry): Extremely negative funding (shorts crowded) predicts positive next-1-7d spot returns (relief-rally effect); extremely positive funding predicts crashes/elevated DVOL. Falsifiable: regression of forward returns and forward Deribit DVOL change on standardized funding has insignificant or wrong-signed coefficients. Predict positive funding -> higher forward realized vol / crash probability (consistent with BIS liquidation finding).
- H4 (trend/CTREND survives in top-50): A short-horizon multi-horizon trend factor (aggregate of SMA crossovers + volume across 1h/4h/1d) on top-50 coins delivers net-positive long-short returns after 15-30bps and ~50-70%/period turnover. Falsifiable: net return <= 0 or breakeven cost < realized cost. Predict net weekly long-short 0.5-2% in liquid top-50 with annualized Sharpe ~1-1.5.
- H5 (momentum is long-leg/large-coin only): In top-50, cross-sectional momentum profit comes from the long leg; the short leg is unprofitable/un-implementable. Falsifiable: short-leg alpha is significantly positive (in the profitable direction) and a fully market-neutral version nets a Sharpe > 1.5. Predict long-only momentum Sharpe ~1-1.6, market-neutral net Sharpe < 1.
- H6 (size = illiquidity, dies in top-50): Restricting to top-50 liquid coins eliminates the size premium. Falsifiable: a significant size long-short survives within top-50 after costs. Predict near-zero/insignificant size effect once microcaps are excluded.
- H7 (low-vol reversal): In top-50, sorting on trailing 30-60d realized vol, low-vol coins outperform high-vol on a risk-adjusted basis post-2024. Falsifiable: high-vol coins outperform (old lottery effect) or no significant spread. Predict modest positive low-vol premium, Sharpe ~0.5-1, possibly fragile.
- H8 (PCA/cointegration stat-arb fragility): PCA eigenportfolio OU mean-reversion and ADF-selected cointegrated pairs on top-50 1h/4h bars do NOT survive 15bps + slippage OOS. Falsifiable: a walk-forward (no look-ahead in pair/eigenvector selection) book nets Sharpe > 1 after costs. Predict in-sample Sharpe > 2 collapsing to <= 0.5 (often negative) OOS net.
- H9 (basis term-structure, Deribit): The Deribit BTC/ETH implied-vol surface / DVOL and the perp funding rate jointly predict the fixed-date futures basis and its mean-reversion; high carry coincides with high DVOL. Falsifiable: funding and DVOL have no incremental predictive power for basis changes.
- H10 (cost asymmetry kills naive signals): Re-running any of H1/H4/H5 with PER-LEG asymmetric costs (taker fees + funding + slippage scaled by Amihud-style impact from our OHLCV) reduces net Sharpe by >50% vs a flat-15bps assumption, and breakeven-cost analysis (BETC) is the decisive metric. Falsifiable: net performance is insensitive to realistic cost modeling.

### Harvest strategies
- Delta-neutral funding carry (PRIMARY): short perpetual + long spot (or long perp on a low/negative-funding venue), collect funding while market-neutral. Instruments: top-10-20 liquid perps + spot. Cost drag: taker fee ~4.5-10bps/side, funding paid in adverse regimes, ~15-30bps round-trip per rebalance, plus borrow/financing on spot; Binance VIP0 break-even funding ~0.007%/8h (~7.7%/yr). REGIME-CONDITION entry: only when trailing funding clears break-even by a margin; expect 8-20% APY in positive-funding, 0-5% in chop, negative in bear unwinds. Risk-manage liquidation (carry predicts short-side liquidations).
- Cross-sectional funding carry: long the most-negative-funding perps, short the most-positive-funding perps (dollar-neutral), rebalanced daily/8h. Captures the carry cross-section without spot. Cost drag: 2x perp taker fees + funding + ~1-2bps slippage in top-50; turnover-sensitive — net the breakeven-cost test.
- Short-horizon trend/CTREND factor in top-50: value-weighted long top-quintile / short bottom-quintile by an aggregated price-volume trend signal, weekly (or 4h-1d) rebalance. Cost drag: ~50-70%/period turnover x 15-30bps; Fieberg breakeven ~141bps means it has large cost headroom in liquid coins. Best near-term cross-sectional candidate.
