- Long-only / long-tilted momentum in large coins: overweight recent top-quartile winners among top-30 coins, NO short leg (short leg is uninvestable / gets liquidated). Cost drag: modest turnover at 15bps; expected Sharpe ~1-1.6. Combine with volatility scaling to tame crashes.
- Volatility-managed time-series momentum on BTC/ETH/top coins: scale position by inverse trailing realized vol (or DVOL for BTC/ETH). Improves Sharpe and tames the documented momentum crashes (per risk-managed-momentum literature). Cost drag low (few large liquid names).
- Perp basis/funding threshold mean-reversion (He-Manela style): trade the perp-spot deviation when it exceeds a cost-aware threshold band, betting on convergence via funding. Cost drag: enter/exit at taker; profitable even at high retail costs historically (Sharpe 1.8-6.5) but edge is shrinking — size down.
- AVOID as standalone net-positive books (paper/microcap artifacts): pure cross-sectional size/illiquidity longs (microcap impact + unshortable), naive PCA eigenportfolio OU stat-arb and ADF-selected pairs (fragile OOS, often negative net), and cross-country/cross-exchange spot arbitrage (closed since 2017-18, needs latency/MEV infra we lack).

### Pitfalls
- Costs dominate everything: crypto round-trip is ~15bps (Binance spot 10 + futures 4.5, tick 3.26bps) PLUS slippage (avg ~1.5bps, max ~12bps/coin) PLUS funding paid. Flat-cost backtests overstate net returns badly; only ~40% of >=20bps spread opportunities are profitable after costs+reversals. Always report breakeven-cost (BETC) and per-leg asymmetric costs, not a single flat number.
- Decay / non-stationarity: funding carry collapsed post-spot-ETF (paid ~25% early-2024, <5% late-2025, Sharpe 6.45 full -> 4.06 in 2024 -> negative 2025). Any in-sample carry Sharpe is an upper bound; the edge is crowding-sensitive and regime-dependent. Backtests spanning the 2020-2021 bull will massively overstate forward returns.
- Liquidation/funding-risk tail (Brunnermeier-Pedersen): delta-neutral carry is NOT riskless — adverse basis moves spike margins and force liquidations; carry itself predicts short-side liquidations (+10% carry -> 22% of OI liquidated). Sharpe ignores this fat left tail; size for the margin-call scenario, not the mean.
- Microcap / illiquidity artifact: the headline size effect (small tercile +317%/yr) and many 'anomalies' live in sub-1M-mcap, untradeable coins with huge price impact (buying 10k BTC moves price ~4%). Equity lesson applies harder in crypto: with NYSE-style breakpoints/VW returns 65-82% of equity anomalies fail; restrict to top-50 and value-weight.
- Short-side infeasibility: many cross-sectional long-shorts assume costless shorting; in crypto only futures-listed coins are shortable, borrow is expensive/limited, and short legs of momentum get liquidated (~99% drawdowns in bull runs). Market-neutral Sharpes from gross papers (>2) are not achievable net.
- Data-snooping / factor zoo: the crypto factor literature replicates 34-36+ anomalies and ~170 perp predictors; with that many tests, t>1.96 is meaningless. Use multiple-testing corrections (t>~3, FDR/BH, Harvey-Liu-Zhu), pre-register signals, and demand OOS persistence. Beware survivorship bias from delisted/dead coins (esp. pre-2021).
- Stat-arb in-sample/look-ahead traps: ~100% in-sample pairs win rates are selection illusions; cointegration vectors and PCA eigenvectors are unstable in crypto and must be estimated strictly out-of-sample (rolling). Beware bid-ask bounce inflating mean-reversion, and stale-price/illiquid-coin artifacts.
- Interim mark-to-market / liquidation modeling: ignoring intra-holding-period price swings (Han-Kang-Ryu) hides margin liquidations and overstates momentum Sharpe; mark daily and model margin even for weekly+ strategies.
- Funding-timing and venue specifics: funding is paid at discrete 8h marks and differs across venues; a signal that looks profitable on one venue's funding schedule/clamp can vanish on another. Cross-venue funding-rate differences also embed transfer/withdrawal frictions.
- Stablecoin/peg and exchange-credit contamination: include stablecoins or treat USD-stablecoin pairs as risk-free and you mismeasure carry; exchange insolvency/withdrawal-halt risk (FTX 2022) is a tail not in price-based backtests.

### Data needed
- HAVE (sufficient for most tests): 228 perps x ~23k hours funding-rate history + Coinalyze funding/OI/liquidations (enables H1-H3, H10 carry tests and liquidation-risk modeling); top-50 OHLCV 1h/4h/1d 2024-02..2026-06 (enables H4-H8 factor/stat-arb in liquid universe); Deribit BTC/ETH IV surfaces + DVOL 2021-2026 (enables H3/H9 vol-conditioning and basis-vol links).
- NEED — spot prices matched to each perp (same venue) to compute true perp-spot basis and delta-neutral carry; confirm OHLCV includes spot, not just perp marks. Free: exchange REST APIs (Binance, OKX, Bybit), CCXT library.
- NEED — per-venue maker/taker fee tiers, tick sizes, and historical funding clamp/cap parameters to model net carry correctly. Free: exchange docs/APIs.
- NEED — fixed-date futures basis (CME + crypto-native quarterly/perp term structure) to test cash-and-carry vs perp carry and the BIS segmentation result. Free: CME delayed data, exchange APIs; CFTC COT (cftc.gov PRE API / cot-reports PyPI) for CME crypto positioning.
- NEED — dead/delisted coin history to fix survivorship bias in cross-sectional tests (top-50 today != top-50 in 2024). Free-ish: CoinGecko/CoinMarketCap historical snapshots; reconstruct point-in-time top-50.
- NEED — borrow/short availability and borrow fees for shortability realism in cross-sectional long-shorts. Source: exchange margin/borrow APIs.
- TO SOURCE (named free sources): FX spot/forwards + rate differentials -> FRED (fred.stlouisfed.org), BIS, ECB SDW, investing.com; CFTC COT for FX/VIX positioning. Commodities futures term structure -> Nasdaq Data Link (Quandl free tiers), barchart.com, TurtleTrader free historical futures (turtletrader.com/hpd), tradingcharts.com. Equity options/VIX -> CBOE official VIX history (cboe.com vix_historical_data), datahub.io/core/finance-vix, Yahoo Finance ^VIX, FRED VIXCLS; CBOE delayed option quotes / ORATS free samples for surfaces.
- NICE-TO-HAVE — higher-frequency funding-prediction features (order-book imbalance, taker buy/sell volume) for H3; partially available via Coinalyze/exchange L2.

### Crypto/recent notes
Crypto is the core of this area, so 'recent/crypto' notes are woven into every finding above. Headline current (2024-2026) state: (1) Funding carry — the marquee edge — has DECAYED sharply post-spot-ETF: full-sample delta-neutral Sharpe 6.45 (2020-2025) fell to 4.06 in 2024 and went NEGATIVE in 2025; the basis that paid ~25% in early-2024 paid <5% by late-2025; BIS DiD shows the Jan-2024 spot-BTC-ETF cut carry ~3pp. Realistic delta-neutral APY now 8-20% (positive-funding), 0-5% (chop), negative (bear unwind). It is risk-compensation (funding/liquidation risk + regulation-induced segmentation), not free arb. (2) Perp no-arbitrage deviations (~60-100%/yr historically, Sharpe 1.8-6.5 net) are shrinking as markets mature. (3) Cross-sectional: the robust net survivor is a short-horizon TREND factor (CTREND, JFQA: 3.87%/wk gross, Sharpe 1.94, breakeven 141bps, survives in liquid coins). Size is an un-investable illiquidity/microcap artifact; market-neutral momentum is ~unattainable net (short legs liquidate, max Sharpe ~1.5, long-leg/large-coin only). A post-2017 LOW-VOL REVERSAL (low-vol now outperforms) is newly documented. (4) Cross-exchange arbitrage (Makarov-Schoar: 15-40% Korea-US spreads) was a 2017-18 capital-controls artifact, now closed. (5) PCA/cointegration stat-arb shows great in-sample, fragile/negative net OOS. Our data window (2024-02 onward) sits right at the post-ETF compression, so expect modest, decaying, regime-dependent carry — backtest with strict OOS, per-leg costs, breakeven-cost reporting, liquidation modeling, and top-50 value-weighting; treat any Sharpe borrowed from 2020-2021 as fiction. Note 1M-context model: prior work confirms the edge is anomaly-selection + cost rigor, not model size.

### Adversarial verification — reliability: **high**
_Net-of-cost reality:_ Blunt take: the underlying empirical numbers in this review are unusually trustworthy — I confirmed the BIS carry figures, the Borri 6.45/4.06/negative-2025 Sharpes, He-Manela 60-100%/yr perp deviations and 1.8-6.5 Sharpe, Fieberg CTREND 3.87%/wk + 141bps breakeven, Han-Kang-Ryu max-momentum-Sharpe ~1.5, and Makarov-Schoar Kimchi spreads all VERBATIM against primary sources. The analyst even cites against interest. Only two factual blemishes: the BIS 'futures leg ~17%/month' is a misread (17% is the monthly VOLATILITY; the return is 2-3%/month), and several figures are loosely cross-attributed between the BIS and Borri papers (each number is individually correct, just sometimes credited to the wrong paper). Now the cost-and-decay reality, with a strong prior that published alpha is overstated: (1) Funding carry — the marquee edge — is real but is RISK COMPENSATION for a fat left tail, not free money, and that tail bit hard out-of-sample. The naive single-coin/USDe delta-neutral carry that printed Sharpe 6.45 went negative in 2025, funding-arb yields fell below 4%, and the October 10, 2025 cascade ($19B liquidated, USDe de-pegged ~35% on Binance) forcibly liquidated 'delta-neutral' books that were only neutral on paper. A 0.8%-vol/6.45-Sharpe carry leg is the single biggest tell that the Sharpe is lying about the risk. HOWEVER — and the review slightly under-credits this — diversified, actively risk-managed market-neutral crypto funds still made ~14% in 2025 while directional lost ~11% and fundamental L/S lost ~31%. So the honest net-of-cost verdict on carry is: harvestable ONLY if diversified across coins/venues, regime-conditioned to clear the ~7-8%/yr VIP0 break-even funding by a margin, sized for the margin-call/de-peg scenario rather than the mean, and expected to deliver maybe high-single to mid-teens APY in good regimes with periodic gut-punch drawdowns — NOT the 25%+ of 2020-21 and NOT a smooth Sharpe-6 ride. (2) Cross-sectional factors: CTREND is the cleanest survivor (141bps cost headroom, works in liquid coins) but its sample ends May-2022 and a 68%/week-turnover trend signal is a prime decay/crowding candidate — assume the live Sharpe is well below the paper's 1.94. Market-neutral momentum and the size effect are net-of-cost mirages (short legs liquidate, size lives in the bottom 30-70% of microcaps); only long-leg/large-coin tilts survive, Sharpe ~1-1.5 at best. (3) Cross-exchange spot arb and naive PCA/cointegration stat-arb are correctly relegated to 'avoid' — the former closed in 2018, the latter has no credible peer-reviewed net-positive evidence. Bottom line: the review's harvest list (diversified cost-aware risk-managed carry + short-horizon trend in liquid coins; long-tilted/vol-managed momentum; avoid size/microcap and naive stat-arb) is the correct ranking, but every Sharpe borrowed from the 2020-2021 era should be treated as fiction, and the carry edge should be underwritten to the October-2025 de-peg scenario, not its mean.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Crypto carry (cash-and-carry / delta-neutral) earns a large premium that is risk compensation (funding/liquidation risk + regulation-induced segmentation), NOT riskless arbitrage; ~7% avg annualized basis (Apr2019-Jul2024), peaks >40% p.a., ~10x S&P 500 carry; the Jan-2024 spot-BTC-ETF cut carry by ~3pp in a difference-in-differences setting; carry predicts short-side liquidations (+10% standardized carry -> +22% of OI liquidated next month). Futures leg ~17% per MONTH. — Verified against the PRIMARY source (BIS WP1087, Schmeling-Schrimpf-Todorov, April 2023 REVISED October 2025) read in full. Exact confirmations: 'From April 2019 to July 2024, the average annualized carry across exchanges was approximately 7% p.a.'; carry 'sometimes exceeding 40% per annum' and 'above 45% before the launch of the spot BTC ETF'; 'at roughly 7% p.a., crypto carry is around 10 times larger than the carry of the S&P 500 and more than 12 times larger than the one of U.S. Treasuries'; the ETF DiD 'decreased the basis of all exchanges by around 3%, and on the CME by [an] additional 5%... very large declines of 36% and 97% of the mean basis'; and verbatim 'an increase in the standardized carry by 10% predicts an increase in liquidations of short futures positions by 22% of total open interest over the next month.' The risk-compensation (negative convenience yield from limited arbitrage capital due to regulatory/margin frictions, NOT riskless arb) framing is the paper's central thesis. ONE NUMBER IS WRONG/MISATTRIBUTED: the mean excess return on the futures leg of the basis trade is '2-3% per month' (the 17% figure is the futures-leg VOLATILITY, 'about 17% per month', NOT the return). The analyst's finding states '~17% per MONTH gross excess return,' which is a material misread of the BIS table. The finding also loosely conflates BIS (carry magnitude, liquidation, ETF DiD) with the separate Borri paper's Sharpe figures, but each underlying number traces to a correct source.
- **[WEAKENED]** Delta-neutral crypto funding carry posted an annualized Sharpe of 6.45 for the full sample (2020-2025), fell to 4.06 in 2024, and turned NEGATIVE in 2025; the funding-rate leg has mean ~8%/yr with very low ~0.8% volatility. (Borri-Liu-Tsyvinski-Wu 2025/2026.) — The SPECIFIC numbers are confirmed verbatim from the primary source (arXiv 2510.14435v4, Feb/Mar 2026, read in full): 'the annualized Sharpe ratio of the cryptocurrency carry is 6.45. Beginning in 2024, the Sharpe ratio falls to 4.06, and it turns negative in 2025'; funding leg full-sample 'mean return of approximately 8% with a low volatility of 0.8%.' HOWEVER the construction is far narrower than the analyst's framing implies, which is why the broad takeaway ('the strategy turned negative in 2025') is WEAKENED: (1) Figure 2 is explicitly the 'Tether Carry Trade' on BITCOIN only (single-asset, USDe/Ethena-style short-perp/long-spot), not a diversified multi-coin book; (2) a Sharpe of 6.45 on a single-coin carry leg with 0.8% vol is itself a red flag for non-normal, fat-left-tail risk that the Sharpe cannot capture (the BIS liquidation result and Oct-2025 events confirm this); and (3) INDEPENDENT 2025-2026 evidence shows diversified, actively-managed market-neutral crypto funds RETURNED ~+14.4% in 2025 (Sigil 'Stable' +11.26%) while directional funds lost ~11% and fundamental L/S lost ~31%. So 'carry went negative in 2025' is true ONLY for the naive single-coin/USDe construction; the broader market-neutral/carry edge, risk-managed and diversified, was strongly positive in 2025. The analyst's adversarial summary actually UNDERSTATES the survivable version while correctly flagging the naive version's collapse.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Delta-neutral carry is NOT riskless: adverse moves spike margins and force liquidations, and the funding/liquidation tail can wipe the premium. (Pitfall + risk-compensation thesis.) — Both the academic mechanism and a fresh, decisive real-world realization confirm this. BIS WP1087 documents the mechanism quantitatively (carry predicts +22% of OI in short-side liquidations per +10% carry; a 10x-levered short-futures leg faces forced liquidation on modest adverse moves; a $1M short futures position liquidates after a 3% BTC rise). The OCTOBER 2025 crash is a textbook out-of-sample vindication: a ~$19B leverage liquidation cascade on Oct 10, 2025 (worst in crypto history, ~$36.7B OI destroyed); USDe (the canonical delta-neutral 'stablecoin' carry vehicle) DE-PEGGED to the mid-$0.60s on Binance (~35% discount) due to cross-venue margin repricing, FORCING liquidation of positions that would have been solvent under fair cross-venue pricing; funding-arbitrage yields then collapsed below 4%. This is precisely the fat-left-tail / margin-call scenario the analyst's pitfalls warned about, and it materialized.
- **[CONFIRMED]** The most robust harvestable cross-sectional crypto factor is a short-horizon TREND factor (CTREND): long-short 3.87%/wk gross (t=5.19), annualized Sharpe 1.94, weekly alpha 2.62% (t=4.22), turnover ~68%/wk, breakeven cost 141bps (88bps to lose 5% significance), survives 30-60bps costs and persists in the largest/most-liquid coins. — Verified line-by-line against the primary source (Fieberg, Liedtke, Poddig, Walker, Zaremba, JFQA 2024/2025, vol 60 pp 3116-3153), read in full incl. Table 9. The H-L row: gross 3.87% (t=5.19); net 2.90% / 2.62% / 2.35% under the three escalating cost scenarios (30/40, 40/50, 50/60 bps per leg); turnover 68.46%; BETC = 1.41% (141bps to zero the return) and BETC-5% = 0.88% (88bps to kill significance) — all exact. Sample >3,000 coins, Apr2015-May2022, 423 weekly obs. Annualized Sharpe 1.94 confirmed. The paper explicitly states the premium 'may be effectively harvested via portfolio sorts, even in liquid and large coins' (vs the size effect which lives in the 'dusty corner... small and illiquid coins'). This is the cleanest, top-journal, cost-aware factor evidence in the set. CAVEAT (correctly flagged by the analyst): sample ENDS May 2022; out-of-sample persistence through the 2023-2026 regime is untested in this paper, and a 68%/wk-turnover trend signal is exactly the kind of edge prone to post-publication decay and crowding.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Under realistic assumptions (daily mark-to-market, 15bps costs, shortability), crypto cross-sectional MOMENTUM does not deliver steady market-neutral profit: short legs get liquidated (Luna-type ~99% rebounds), profit lives in the LONG leg of LARGE coins; max achievable Sharpe ~1.5 vs the >2 in gross studies. (Han-Kang-Ryu.) — Verified against the primary working paper (Han, Kang, Ryu, AUT, Dec 2023, sample ends Aug 28, 2023), read in full. Exact confirmations: best TS-momentum Sharpe 1.51 vs market 0.84; best XS-momentum Sharpe 1.28 vs market 1.01; 'The maximum Sharpe ratio we obtain from a momentum strategy is about 1.5. Meanwhile, several studies obtain a Sharpe ratio greater than 2.0'; 'The profit of a cross-sectional momentum strategy mostly originates from the long leg. The short leg is exposed [to liquidation]'; in contrast to equities (short-leg/small-stock), crypto momentum 'originates mainly from the long leg and large coins'; 15bps round-trip cost assumption confirmed; Luna 99.99% weekly drop example confirmed. Multiple momentum portfolios are LIQUIDATED once interim daily price swings are modeled. INDEPENDENTLY corroborated: a separate ScienceDirect study ('Cryptocurrency anomalies and economic constraints,' 2024) finds momentum 'incurs substantial trading costs and extracts alphas largely from short positions,' and size/volume anomalies 'originate from micro-cap coins of negligible economic importance... solely from the 30% to 70% smallest coins.' This strongly supports the analyst's claim that market-neutral crypto momentum is essentially unattainable net of frictions.
- **[CONFIRMED]** The crypto SIZE effect is enormous gross (small tercile ~+317%/yr) but is an illiquidity/microcap artifact concentrated in coins <10% of mcap, not harvestable net of cost; it is subsumed by the Liu-Tsyvinski-Wu 3-factor model (market/size/momentum) which prices ~10 characteristics. — The Liu-Tsyvinski-Wu (JF 2022, 77(2):1133-1177) three-factor result is confirmed from the JF abstract and the Borri replication: market/size/momentum capture the cross-section and 'ten cryptocurrency characteristics form successful long-short strategies, all of which are accounted for by the cryptocurrency three-factor model.' The 'size = illiquidity microcap artifact' critique is INDEPENDENTLY corroborated by a 2024 ScienceDirect study finding size/volume/distress anomalies 'depend critically on tiny cryptocurrencies whose profitability comes solely from the 30% to 70% smallest coins,' alphas 'concentrated in hard-to-trade assets,' with daily reversal in illiquid small coins vs daily momentum in the largest tradeable coins. The exact '+317%/yr small tercile' / '~1.01%/day SMB' figures I did not locate verbatim in primary text within this pass (the analyst rated this sub-claim only 'moderate'), but the qualitative and directional claim — large gross size premium that is an un-investable microcap/illiquidity artifact dying once you restrict to liquid coins — is well supported by multiple independent sources. Net: the harvestability conclusion (paper-only premium) is solid; treat the precise +317% magnitude as indicative rather than independently re-verified.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Cross-exchange/cross-country crypto arbitrage produced large recurrent spreads (Korea-US >15% avg, ~40% peak 'Kimchi premium'; Japan-US ~10%; US-Europe ~3%; within-country <1%) driven by capital controls/segmentation; this was a 2017-18 phenomenon that has since largely closed — evidence of limits-to-arbitrage, not a live edge. — The Makarov-Schoar (JFE 2020, 135(2):293-319) magnitudes are confirmed from the primary PDF read locally: 'the daily average price ratio between the US and Korea from December 2017 until the beginning of February 2018 was more than 15% and reached 40% for several days... the Kimchi premium'; Japan-US '~10%', US-Europe '~3%', within-country '<1%'; 19 countries; common volume component explains 80% of bitcoin returns; capital controls central. The 'largely closed since 2017-18' characterization is well established in the literature and uncontested — these spreads were specific to the 2017-18 capital-controls/retail-mania episode and have not recurred at that scale; the durable academic lesson is segmentation/limits-to-arbitrage. The analyst correctly treats this as NOT a harvestable edge today (residual CEX-DEX/MEV latency arb requires infra). No refuting evidence found; this is a clean confirmation with the appropriate 'historical, now-closed' caveat already in the finding.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Perpetual-futures prices deviate from no-arbitrage bounds far more than FX (mean abs spread ~60-100%/yr), deviations comove across coins and shrink as markets mature, and a threshold strategy earns Sharpe ~1.8 at highest retail costs up to ~6.5 at institutional costs. (He-Manela-Ross-von Wachter.) — Verified verbatim from the primary source (He, Manela, Ross, von Wachter 'Fundamentals of Perpetual Futures,' arXiv 2212.06888, Jan 2023), read in full: 'The mean absolute futures-spot spread is about 60% to 100% per year across different cryptocurrencies, which is considerably larger than the deviations documented in traditional currency markets by Du, Tepper, and Verdelhan (2018)'; 'strong comovement of the futures-spot gap across different cryptocurrencies'; deviations 'diminish over time as crypto markets develop and become more efficient'; and for Bitcoin both threshold strategies 'generate Sharpe ratios... ranging from 1.8 under high trading costs typical of retail investors who rarely trade, and up to 6.5' at low costs. Every headline number matches. The adversarial caveat (already in the finding) is correct: the edge is explicitly shrinking with maturation, the 2018-2022 sample predates the post-2024 compression, and the high Sharpes assume favorable execution; the paper itself notes 'riskless no-arbitrage pricing is usually just a useful fiction.'
- **[UNCERTAIN]** Crypto pairs/cointegration and PCA eigenportfolio (OU residual mean-reversion) stat-arb show very high in-sample win rates but are fragile and frequently unprofitable net of cost out-of-sample; cointegration is unstable in crypto and PCA mean-reversion is 'not robust.' — I did not independently re-verify the specific practitioner backtest numbers (100% in-sample win rates collapsing to 79-100% live with -0.4% to +8.1%/trade; only ~40% of >=20bps spreads profitable net) within this pass — the analyst itself rated this evidence 'weak,' citing SSRN working papers and practitioner blogs (Jung 2025 SSRN 5263475; Dada/Digital Alpha) rather than peer-reviewed work, and noted heavy survivorship/in-sample selection. The DIRECTION of the claim (in-sample stat-arb win rates are selection illusions; cointegration vectors and PCA eigenvectors are unstable OOS in crypto; bid-ask bounce inflates apparent mean-reversion; no robust top-journal net-positive crypto stat-arb book exists) is highly consistent with the broader limits-to-arbitrage / cost-domination evidence I did confirm, and with the general equities stat-arb literature (Avellaneda-Lee). But because the specific figures rest on non-peer-reviewed, self-selected backtests, the precise magnitudes remain unverified. Verdict: uncertain on the numbers, directionally plausible and appropriately skeptical. This is the right posture — treat claimed stat-arb Sharpes with maximum suspicion and demand strict walk-forward, no-look-ahead validation.

---

## Liquidity provision and microstructure alpha  `liquidity_provision`

Microstructure "alpha" splits cleanly into two regimes. (1) Sub-second LOB signals — order-flow imbalance (OFI), queue imbalance, and the Stoikov micro-price — have enormous CONTEMPORANEOUS explanatory power for mid-price moves (R^2 ~65% best-level, ~85-87% integrated multi-level) and genuine but fast-decaying predictive power (signal peaks ~2 price changes ahead, near-zero by ~10). But the edge is a LATENCY-RANK race: profitability depends on being faster than rivals, not on absolute speed, so it accrues to the top ~6 colocated firms (>80% of latency-race wins). Round-trip spread/fee costs erase the gross signal at HFT frequencies; this is paper-only alpha for any non-colocated player. (2) The one liquidity-provision premium that survives realistic costs at human/non-HFT frequency is SHORT-TERM REVERSAL, which Nagel (2012) shows IS the return to liquidity provision — it is large and tradable in crisis/high-vol regimes (~0.2%/day calm, up to ~1%/day in turmoil), highly predictable by VIX/DVOL, and in crypto is concentrated in low-volume/high-vol/illiquid pairs (the adverse-selection-compensation story). The brutal truth: passive market-making and AMM LP returns are dominated by adverse selection and beta — Milionis et al. find 99.991% of Uniswap v2 ETH-USDC LP P&L variance is just ETH beta, leaving 0.009% as the fee-minus-adverse-selection "alpha"; and a recent crypto microstructure study found maker (passive) strategies statistically insignificant while only taker strategies were significant. Our realistic edge is reversal/liquidity-provision timing (daily/weekly, crypto + large-cap equities) and using OFI/micro-price as an EXECUTION/entry-timing overlay, not a standalone HFT alpha.

### Findings

**Order-flow imbalance (OFI = signed changes in best bid/ask queue sizes) explains short-horizon mid-price changes nearly linearly, with slope inversely proportional to market depth (beta = c/Depth^lambda, lambda~1). This is the canonical contemporaneous price-impact relation, robust across stocks and timescales.**
- Effect size: Average R^2 = 65% across 50 S&P500 stocks (10s intervals); robust 35-60% even after removing price-changing events (anti-tautology check). Log-log slope of beta vs depth = -1.026 (R^2=0.863), i.e. lambda statistically indistinguishable from 1 for 35/50 stocks. Adding a quadratic term raises R^2 only 65%->68% (insignificant), so impact is effectively linear in OFI.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Original April-2010 TAQ sample (Cont-Kukanov-Stoikov). Re-confirmed and EXTENDED post-2018: Cont-Cucuringu-Zhang (2023, Nasdaq ITCH 2017-2019) get in-sample R^2 87.1% / OOS 83.8% with an integrated multi-level OFI vs 71%/65% for best-level. Holds in crypto: Binance perpetuals 2022-2025 studies find OFI is the single most important feature for price moves, rankings stable across BTC/LTC/ETC/ENJ/ROSE.
- Cites: Cont, Kukanov, Stoikov 2011/2014 'The Price Impact of Order Book Events' (arXiv:1011.6402; J. Financial Econometrics 12(1):47-88); Cont, Cucuringu, Zhang 2023 'Cross-Impact of Order Flow Imbalance in Equity Markets' (Quantitative Finance 23(10):1373-1393; arXiv:2112.13213)

**Queue imbalance at the best bid/offer predicts the direction of the NEXT mid-price move, but the signal is short-lived and works mainly in large-tick (tick-constrained) instruments where the queue, not the spread, is the binding constraint.**
- Effect size: Queue imbalance predicts the next 1-2 mid-price changes with strong logistic-regression fit, decaying to ~0 by later changes. Predictive power is strong for large-tick stocks and largely DISAPPEARS for small-tick names. Stoikov micro-price (mid + g(imbalance, spread)) is a martingale 'fair value' that empirically beats both mid and weighted-mid as a short-horizon predictor.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Gould-Bonart (2016, Nasdaq) and Stoikov micro-price (2018) pre-date 2018 but the mechanism is structural and confirmed in later deep-learning work; directly applicable to SPY/QQQ which are pinned at the 1-cent tick (so they behave as large-tick).
- Cites: Gould, Bonart 2016 'Queue Imbalance as a One-Tick-Ahead Price Predictor in a Limit Order Book' (Market Microstructure and Liquidity; arXiv:1512.03492); Stoikov 2018 'The Micro-Price: A High-Frequency Estimator of Future Prices' (Quantitative Finance; SSRN 2970694)

**Deep-learning models on LOB data achieve high directional classification accuracy, and crucially, models trained on ORDER FLOW (stationary) generalize and outperform models trained on raw order-book states. But alpha peaks ~2 price changes ahead and decays fast, so predictability does not equal post-cost profit.**
- Effect size: DeepLOB (CNN-LSTM) directional accuracy on FI-2010 benchmark: 81.8% (k=1), 74.3% (k=5), 77.4% (k=10). Kolm-Turiel-Westray: across 115 Nasdaq stocks, order-flow LSTMs beat raw-book models; stock-level alpha peaks at ~2 price changes then declines; 'information-rich' stocks (more book updates per price change) are more predictable. Authors explicitly caveat that trading costs must be considered.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: DeepLOB 2019 (LSE 2007-2017 generalization test); Kolm-Turiel-Westray Math Finance 2023 (Nasdaq Jan-2019 to Jan-2020). Note prior work in our program already showed bigger models don't help — consistent with the literature: the edge is the OFI feature + horizon choice, not model capacity.
- Cites: Zhang, Zohren, Roberts 2019 'DeepLOB: Deep Convolutional Neural Networks for Limit Order Books' (IEEE Trans. Signal Processing 67(11); arXiv:1808.03668); Kolm, Turiel, Westray 2023 'Deep Order Flow Imbalance: Extracting Alpha at Multiple Horizons from the Limit Order Book' (Mathematical Finance 33(4):1044-1081; SSRN 3900141)

**LOB-imbalance/OFI trading is a LATENCY-RANK race: profit depends on being faster than competitors, not on absolute latency. This is the structural reason the alpha accrues to colocated HFTs and is unavailable to retail/non-colocated players.**
- Effect size: Byrd et al. simulation: profit is inversely related to latency, but 'latency RANK, rather than absolute magnitude, is the key factor in allocating returns' — winner-take-most among similar-strategy agents. Real-world: latency-arbitrage races last a modal 5-10 microseconds, occur ~1/minute/symbol (FTSE100), are ~20% of volume; top 6 firms win >80% of races. Latency 'tax' on liquidity = 0.42-0.53 bps; eliminating it would cut the cost of liquidity ~17%; ~$5bn/yr globally.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Byrd et al. 2020 (simulation). Aquilina-Budish-O'Neill QJE 2022 used 2015 LSE message data — the definitive empirical quantification; mechanism persists 2018-2026 as colocation/microwave arms race continues.
- Cites: Byrd, Hybinette, Balch 2020 'The Importance of Low Latency to Order Book Imbalance Trading Strategies' (arXiv:2006.08682); Aquilina, Budish, O'Neill 2022 'Quantifying the High-Frequency Trading Arms Race' (Quarterly Journal of Economics 137(1):493-564)

**Short-term reversal returns ARE the returns to liquidity provision; expected returns are strongly time-varying and predictable by the VIX, spiking in crises (the 'evaporating liquidity' mechanism: constrained intermediaries withdraw, reversal pays more).**
- Effect size: Reversal strategy ~1%/day during LTCM (1998) and dot-com (2000-01) and the 2008 crisis; fell to <0.2%/day in calm 2004-2007. Conditional Sharpe and expected return scale strongly with VIX. This is the highest-conviction, most-tradable liquidity-provision premium for a non-HFT.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Nagel 2012 (US equities 1998-2010). Mechanism (vol-conditional reversal = LP premium) directly carries to crypto via DVOL/funding stress and is confirmed by the 2025 crypto LP paper below.
- Cites: Nagel 2012 'Evaporating Liquidity' (Review of Financial Studies 25(7):2005-2039; NBER w17653)

**In crypto, the same logic holds: returns to liquidity provision (proxied by short-term reversal) are concentrated in low-volume, smaller, more volatile, less-liquid pairs where adverse-selection fear is higher — exactly where a maker is compensated for inventory/adverse-selection risk. Robust to conservative transaction costs and including COVID.**
- Effect size: Conditional (low-volume) reversal generates HIGHER Sharpe than unconditional; profitability concentrated in low-activity pairs; robust to conservative costs. Separately, cross-sectional crypto reversal/momentum: long-short ~3% excess WEEKLY in some studies but a quintile L/S taker strategy nets only ~0.34 bps per 10-min rebalance after ~4 bps round-trip cost — i.e. high-frequency crypto reversal is mostly eaten by costs; the daily/weekly low-turnover version is what survives.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: USD pairs on multiple CEXs 2017-2022 (LP paper). Liu-Tsyvinski-Wu cross-section 2014-2020. Post-2022 high-vol crypto regime is favorable to the vol-conditional reversal story.
- Cites: Jeyasreedharan/Bianchi-type 2025 'Returns from Liquidity Provision in Cryptocurrency Markets' (Journal of Banking & Finance; ScienceDirect S0378426625000317); Bianchi, Babiak et al. 'Trading Volume and Liquidity Provision in Cryptocurrency Markets' (J. Banking & Finance 2022; Riksbank WP 413); Liu, Tsyvinski, Wu 2022 'Common Risk Factors in Cryptocurrency' (Journal of Finance 77(2)) and 'Cross-Section of Cryptocurrency Returns'

**Passive market-making / AMM LP returns are dominated by adverse selection and market beta; the genuine microstructural 'alpha' (fees minus adverse-selection / loss-versus-rebalancing) is a tiny fraction of P&L. Naive LP/market-making is NOT free alpha.**
- Effect size: Milionis-Moallemi-Roughgarden-Zhang: for Uniswap v2 ETH-USDC, 99.991% of LP P&L variance is beta (ETH) exposure; only 0.009% is the alpha (fees - LVR). LVR = sigma^2 * L / (4*sqrt(p)); a Uniswap pool needs to turn over ~10% of TVL daily for 30 bps fees to cover LVR. Equity analog: aggregate liquidity-provision profit (realized spread at 100ms) fell from 1.9 bps of dollar volume (2010) to 1.0 bps (2017); large-cap price impact resolves within ~15s, small-cap ~60s, so measurement horizon dominates inferred profit.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Milionis et al. 2022, current version 2026 (Uniswap v2 ETH-USDC). Conrad-Wahal JFE 2020 (US equities 2010-2017). Both directly relevant to our SPY/QQQ LOB and crypto data.
- Cites: Milionis, Moallemi, Roughgarden, Zhang 2022/2026 'Automated Market Making and Loss-Versus-Rebalancing' (arXiv:2208.06046); Conrad, Wahal 2020 'The Term Structure of Liquidity Provision' (Journal of Financial Economics 136(2):339-365)

**Queue position has measurable economic value, and for large-tick stocks it can rival the entire bid-ask spread — front-of-queue orders earn the spread with far lower adverse selection than back-of-queue. This is the core profit lever in tick-constrained names (SPY/QQQ), and it requires speed to acquire/hold position.**
- Effect size: Moallemi-Yuan: positional value has a static component (spread minus adverse-selection cost, which RISES with worse queue position) plus a dynamic optionality component; for some large-tick stocks queue value is of the same order of magnitude as the bid-ask spread. Validated against backtest fill simulations.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Moallemi-Yuan 2016/2022. Structural; applies to any price-time-priority venue including Nasdaq equities and most crypto CLOBs.
- Cites: Moallemi, Yuan 2016/2022 'A Model for Queue Position Valuation in a Limit Order Book' (SSRN 2996221; Operations Research)

**Retail order flow is, in aggregate, NON-toxic (low adverse selection), which is why wholesalers pay for it and give price improvement. Inversely, the flow remaining on lit exchanges is more adversely-selected/toxic — relevant when interpreting our lit LOB data and to the realism of any maker backtest.**
- Effect size: 3 firms (Citadel Securities, Virtu, G1/Susquehanna) handle >80% of US retail equity market orders; wholesalers provide billions/yr of price improvement; multiple studies find PFOF magnitude too small to explain cross-broker price-improvement variation — value is the LOW adverse selection of retail flow, not the PFOF.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Schwarz et al. 2023-2024; Wharton/Fed working papers 2023-2024. Highly current.
- Cites: Schwarz, Barber, Huang, Jorion, Odean 2023/2024 'The Actual Retail Price of Equity Trades' (SSRN/working paper); Federal Reserve FEDS 2024-080 'Who is Minding the Store? Order Routing and Competition'

**The square-root law of market impact is universal (equities, FX, futures, bitcoin, OTC credit): executing size Q moves price ~ Y*sigma*sqrt(Q/V). This is the dominant COST term that any microstructure strategy must beat, and it sets the capacity ceiling.**
- Effect size: Impact G ~ Y * sigma * sqrt(Q/ADV), with Y ~ O(1) (often ~0.5-1). Approximately independent of execution horizon and slicing. Crossover to linear (Kyle's lambda) only for very small orders. Implies cost grows as sqrt(size), so small players actually have a per-unit cost ADVANTAGE on small clips.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Decades of evidence, re-confirmed across asset classes including bitcoin 2018-2024 (Bouchaud and collaborators). Directly usable to model our cost drag.
- Cites: Bouchaud, Bonart, Donier, Gould 2018 'Trades, Quotes and Prices' (CUP); Kyle, Obizhaeva 2016 'Market Microstructure Invariance' (Econometrica 84(4)); Bucci, Benzaquen, Lillo, Bouchaud 2019-2020 square-root law studies (arXiv:2004.08290)

### Testable hypotheses
- H1 (anchor): The Stoikov micro-price (mid + adjustment for best-level imbalance and spread) predicts the sign of the next mid-price move in SPY/QQQ with >60% accuracy at 1-5 LOB-event horizons in our 56M 10-level snapshots, and accuracy decays to ~50% by ~10 events — but a marketable-order strategy crossing the spread nets NEGATIVE after the 1-cent spread, while a passive front-of-queue fill is required to monetize it. Falsifiable: if passive-fill PnL minus realized adverse selection (price move 15s post-fill) is <= 0, the maker edge does not survive.
- H2: Multi-level integrated OFI (PCA across our 10 levels, per Cont-Cucuringu-Zhang) explains contemporaneous 1s-10s SPY/QQQ mid returns with OOS R^2 ~80%+, and lagged cross-asset OFI between SPY and QQQ adds small but significant short-horizon (seconds) forecasting power that decays within ~1 minute. Falsifiable on our SPY+QQQ LOB + Databento ITCH.
- H3 (highest conviction, low-frequency): A vol-conditional short-term reversal portfolio in crypto (long biggest 1-3 day losers / short biggest gainers among top-50 coins) earns positive net-of-cost returns concentrated in (a) lower-volume coins and (b) high-DVOL / funding-stress regimes, mirroring Nagel and the crypto-LP paper. Falsifiable: regress reversal return on lagged DVOL and coin turnover; the predicted positive interaction must survive 10-20 bps round-trip crypto costs on our 1h/4h/1d top-50 data.
- H4: In US large-cap equities, daily/weekly short-term reversal restricted to S&P500 (large-cap, per de Groot et al.) earns positive returns net of realistic costs (a few bps/day) and its conditional Sharpe rises with VIX. Testable on our S&P500 daily/15m/1h bars + free VIX (FRED VIXCLS).
- H5 (cost-reality check): A naive 'symmetric maker' backtest on our SPY/QQQ LOB that assumes fills at best bid/ask with NO queue model overstates PnL; adding a Moallemi-Yuan-style fill model (fill probability and adverse selection rising with queue position) flips the strategy from profitable to unprofitable. Falsifiable by comparing the two backtests on identical signals.
- H6: OFI/micro-price used as an ENTRY-TIMING overlay on a lower-frequency signal (e.g., only lift the offer when micro-price > mid, i.e. book tilted your way) reduces effective execution cost vs naive market orders by a measurable fraction (target: shave 10-30% of half-spread) on our equities and crypto data — i.e. microstructure helps as execution alpha even where it fails as standalone alpha.
- H7: Funding-rate sign/level predicts short-horizon perp-spot basis reversal; a delta-neutral 'collect funding' position on our 228 perps x 23k hours earns positive carry but its Sharpe is dominated by tail liquidation/blowup risk in high-funding regimes (Coinalyze liquidations spike). Falsifiable by computing realized net carry minus a liquidation-cost model.
- H8: Crypto OFI predictive power and reversal premia are STRONGER in low-liquidity coins (bottom of top-50 by volume) than in BTC/ETH, consistent with adverse-selection compensation; cross-sectional IC of an OFI/imbalance signal should be monotonically decreasing in coin liquidity.

### Harvest strategies
- STRATEGY A (primary, survives costs): Vol-conditional cross-sectional short-term reversal in crypto. Universe: top-50 coins, 1d (and 4h) bars. Rank by trailing 1-3 day return, long losers / short winners, but SCALE exposure up with DVOL/funding stress and OVERWEIGHT lower-volume coins (where the LP premium lives). Instruments: spot or perps (perps let you short cheaply; watch funding). Cost drag: ~10-30 bps round-trip taker on majors, more on alts — so trade DAILY/multi-day, not intraday; keep turnover low. This is the cleanest harvestable version of 'liquidity provision alpha' for a small player.
- STRATEGY B: Large-cap equity short-term reversal, S&P500 only, weekly rebalance, VIX-scaled. Instruments: the 30-100 most liquid S&P500 names (avoid small-caps where costs explode — the de Groot result). Expected net ~tens of bps/week historically but DECAYING (Blitz et al.: classic reversal has weakened/vanished in many regions) — treat as a regime/crisis-overlay sleeve, not an always-on engine. Cost drag: ~1-3 bps/side on liquid names.
- STRATEGY C (execution alpha, not standalone): Micro-price / integrated-OFI execution overlay. Compute Stoikov micro-price and integrated OFI from our SPY/QQQ 10-level LOB and Databento ITCH. Use as a SHORT-HORIZON timing gate for entries/exits of A and B and for working orders: only cross the spread when the book is tilted in your favor; otherwise post passively. Goal: reduce slippage by 10-30% of the half-spread. This monetizes microstructure where it actually pays for a non-colocated player.
- STRATEGY D (research/measurement, capacity-limited): Passive maker in tick-constrained names (SPY/QQQ) WITH a realistic queue model. Only viable if you can model fill probability and adverse selection by queue position (Moallemi-Yuan) and you have maker-rebate access. For a retail player WITHOUT colocation/rebates this is expected-negative after adverse selection — include it mainly to quantify the adverse-selection cost and to validate that naive maker backtests are illusory.
- STRATEGY E (carry, adjacent): Delta-neutral perp funding capture on our 228-perp funding history — long spot/short perp (or vice versa) to collect funding, sized down in high-funding 'crowded' regimes. Cost drag: taker fees on both legs + funding-rate mean reversion + tail liquidation risk; net Sharpe is positive but blow-up-prone, so cap leverage and gate on Coinalyze OI/liquidation stress.

### Pitfalls
- FILL-MODEL ILLUSION (the #1 trap): Backtesting a maker strategy by assuming you get filled at the touch with no queue model massively overstates PnL. In tick-constrained names you only get filled when the market is about to move against you (adverse selection). Any maker backtest MUST model queue position, fill probability, and post-fill drift (Moallemi-Yuan). The crypto microstructure study found maker strategies statistically INSIGNIFICANT once done honestly.
- CONTEMPORANEOUS vs PREDICTIVE confusion: OFI's 65-87% R^2 is CONTEMPORANEOUS (OFI and price move together within the same interval) — it is NOT a tradable forecast. The genuinely predictive (lagged) component is small and decays in ~2 price changes / under a minute. Reporting the contemporaneous R^2 as if it were forecasting power is a classic self-deception.
- LATENCY-RANK WINNER-TAKE-ALL: Even a real predictive OFI/imbalance signal is a relative-speed race; without colocation you are systematically last in queue and adversely selected. Do not budget for capturing the ~$5bn/yr latency-race pie — it is structurally unavailable. Treat sub-second LOB alpha as execution help only.
- SPREAD/COST DRAG AT HF: Round-trip cost = full spread + fees each cycle. At HFT frequencies on our data, even a 60-70% hit-rate OFI signal nets negative (crypto example: 0.34 bps/trade vs ~4 bps cost). Always net the FULL round-trip and use the square-root impact law for any non-trivial size.
- CRYPTO REVERSAL = MICROCAP COST TRAP: The crypto reversal premium is strongest exactly where costs/slippage are worst (low-volume alts). The de Groot lesson applies doubly: the gross premium can be an artifact of un-tradable spreads. Use conservative, coin-specific cost assumptions and liquidity filters.
- AMM/MM 'ALPHA' IS 99.99% BETA: Reporting LP or inventory-MM returns without hedging out the directional (beta) component is meaningless — Milionis et al. show 99.991% of Uniswap LP variance is beta. Always isolate the fees-minus-adverse-selection residual; it is tiny and easily swamped by omitted-variable bias.
- HORIZON-SENSITIVITY OF SPREAD DECOMPOSITION: Realized-spread/MM-profit estimates swing wildly with the measurement horizon (Conrad-Wahal: profit halved 2010->2017 at 100ms; impact resolves in 15-60s). Pick and pre-register the horizon; don't shop it.
- DATA SNOOPING / SHORT SAMPLES: Our SPY/QQQ LOB is only Nov-Dec 2025 (+ live) and crypto OHLCV from 2024-02 — tiny, regime-specific windows. Microstructure relationships are stable in form but the PnL is regime-dependent (vol, tick regime, fee schedule). Heavy risk of overfitting thresholds (e.g. the 0.85 imbalance trigger) to one regime. Use walk-forward, purged CV, and cross-asset replication (the literature's main validity test is cross-stock/cross-coin stability of feature rankings).
- DECAY: Classic short-term reversal has weakened/vanished in many equity regions post-2010 (Blitz et al.); microstructure signals decay as more players exploit them. Budget for alpha decay and re-test out-of-sample frequently.
- TICK-SIZE REGIME DEPENDENCE: Queue-imbalance/micro-price work in LARGE-tick (constrained) names and fail in small-tick. SPY/QQQ are large-tick-like; many individual stocks are not. Do not transplant a SPY-calibrated signal to small-tick names without re-checking.

### Data needed
- Maker/taker fee schedules and any rebate tiers for the exact crypto venues we trade (Binance/Bybit/etc.) and realistic per-coin spread + slippage curves for top-50 coins — essential to net out Strategy A; without coin-level cost data the crypto reversal result is untrustworthy.
- Crypto LOB / order-flow data (not just OHLCV) for top-50 coins to compute OFI/queue-imbalance/micro-price — our crypto edge currently relies on OHLCV-derived reversal; testing H1/H8 in crypto needs at least L2 snapshots (e.g. free Binance depth/aggTrades via API, or Kaiko/Tardis samples).
- Longer SPY/QQQ LOB history beyond Nov-Dec 2025 to span multiple vol regimes (the current window is too short to trust thresholds); accumulate the live feed and/or source more Databento ITCH months.
- Trade-level signing (Lee-Ready or exchange-provided aggressor flag) in our Databento ITCH to build trade-flow imbalance and realized/effective spread decompositions for the adverse-selection measurement (H5).
- Free FX + commodities for cross-asset OFI/carry replication: FRED (FX spot, 3M rate differentials, VIXCLS), exchangerate.host / ExchangeRate-API (spot/forward proxies), Nasdaq Data Link free tier and CFTC/Stooq for futures term structure. Needed only if we extend the square-root-law/carry tests cross-asset.
- Free vol data for the VIX-conditioning of reversal (H4): FRED VIXCLS (1990+), CBOE free VIX/VIX9D/VIX3M and VIX futures term structure (2004+), Yahoo ^VIX. VIX OPTIONS are not free (acceptable — we only need the index/term-structure for conditioning). For crypto, we already have Deribit DVOL (2021-2026) as the analog.
- Funding-rate-adjusted perp index/mark price and historical liquidation data (we have Coinalyze + 228 perps) — sufficient for Strategy E; just need to confirm timestamp alignment between funding, mark, and spot for the delta-neutral carry test.
- Maker-rebate eligibility/access reality check: confirm whether we can even post passively with rebates on any venue — determines whether Strategy D is anything but a measurement exercise.

### Crypto/recent notes
Crypto-specific and post-2018 takeaways: (1) OFI is the single most important LOB feature for crypto price moves and feature rankings are stable across BTC/LTC/ETC/ENJ/ROSE on Binance perpetuals 2022-2025 — but, exactly as in equities, MAKER (passive) strategies came out statistically insignificant while only TAKER strategies were significant, confirming adverse selection eats passive crypto MM. (2) Short-term reversal = liquidity-provision premium transfers cleanly to crypto: concentrated in low-volume/high-vol/illiquid USD pairs (2017-2022, multiple CEXs), robust to conservative costs incl. COVID — this is our most harvestable, non-HFT, directly-testable edge and maps onto our top-50 OHLCV + DVOL + funding data. (3) Watch the cost cliff: high-frequency crypto reversal nets ~0.34 bps/trade vs ~4 bps round-trip cost (un-tradable); only the daily/multi-day low-turnover version survives. (4) AMM LP is NOT free yield: 99.991% of Uniswap v2 ETH-USDC LP variance is ETH beta; LVR (~sigma^2*L/(4 sqrt p)) typically exceeds fees unless pool turns over ~10% of TVL/day — relevant if we ever consider DeFi LPing. (5) Square-root impact law is confirmed for bitcoin, so our cost model can use G ~ Y*sigma*sqrt(Q/ADV) across both equities and crypto. (6) HFT arms-race economics (latency-rank winner-take-all, top-6 firms >80% of races, 0.5 bps latency tax) mean sub-second LOB alpha is structurally off-limits to us — use OFI/micro-price as execution timing, not standalone alpha. Net program guidance: prioritize vol-conditional reversal (crypto first, large-cap equity second) as the alpha, and OFI/micro-price/integrated-OFI as an execution-cost reducer; treat all passive-MM and LP backtests as suspect until a queue/adverse-selection fill model is in place.

### Adversarial verification — reliability: **medium**
_Net-of-cost reality:_ Net of realistic costs, this area is mostly a measurement/execution toolkit, not a standalone alpha engine - and the findings broadly admit this, which is to their credit. The structural facts survive scrutiny: OFI's huge R^2 is contemporaneous (not a forecast), sub-second LOB edge is a latency-rank race owned by ~6 colocated firms (~$5bn/yr, ~0.5bps tax) and is paper-only for anyone else, AMM/passive-MM P&L is 99.991% beta with a 0.009% residual that is frequently NEGATIVE once you net LVR/adverse-selection, and the square-root law sets a hard sqrt(size) cost floor. The supposed 'most harvestable' edge - vol-conditional short-term reversal - is the weakest part of the cost story: classic reversal has 'vanished entirely in most regions' (Blitz 2023), is unprofitable after costs in the illiquid names where it is strongest (Avramov-Chordia-Goyal), and in crypto is explicitly an artifact of microcap illiquidity, i.e. it lives precisely where 10-30bps+ round-trip costs eat it. Fresh 2026 evidence is brutal: a representative BTC microstructure signal decayed from +54bps net (2024) to -16bps net (2026 YTD, t=0.96), and the only monetization path the latest crypto-microstructure paper endorses is maker-style EXECUTION, not standalone alpha - exactly matching the report's own conclusion. The Oct-2025 crash is the tail that voids the carry/passive-MM sleeves: ~30% of crypto market makers wiped out, delta-neutral funding arb collapsed below 4% and 'no longer attractive,' and ADL turned hedged books naked - so Strategy E (perp funding carry) and any passive-MM/LP backtest must be treated as expected-negative-with-fat-left-tail until a queue/adverse-selection fill model AND a liquidation/ADL stress model are in place. Bottom line: budget for OFI/micro-price as a 10-30% slippage reducer (real, defensible), treat reversal as a small, decaying, crisis-overlay sleeve with strict liquidity filters and low turnover, and treat every passive-MM/LP/funding-carry P&L number as illusory until stress- and fill-modeled.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Milionis et al.: for Uniswap v2 ETH-USDC, 99.991% of LP P&L variance is market beta (ETH exposure), leaving only 0.009% as the fees-minus-LVR microstructural alpha; naive LP/market-making is not free alpha. — Verified verbatim against the primary PDF, not a secondhand summary. The paper states: 'over 99.991% of LP return variance is driven by beta exposure to market risk' and '0.009% of the variation in returns in unhedged P&L comes from fees and adverse selection, and the remaining 99.991% simply reflects ETH price... market risk.' The variance-decomposition number in the findings is exact, and the paper's own warning matches the report's pitfall: even weak correlation between any x-variable and market risk induces 'substantial omitted-variable bias, easily swamping any genuine' microstructural signal. Two caveats that the findings UNDERSTATE rather than overstate: (a) this is a VARIANCE decomposition, not a statement that the alpha residual is positive in level - the model assumes zero CEX/gas fees, so it does not itself prove LPs net-profit; (b) real-world evidence (e.g. on-chain LVR studies and the Oct-2025 episode) generally shows LVR exceeding fees for major volatile pairs, i.e. the residual is often NEGATIVE. So the claim 'LP is dominated by beta and the alpha is tiny' is if anything stronger than stated.
- **[WEAKENED]** Short-term reversal returns ARE the return to liquidity provision, are strongly VIX-predictable, and spike to ~1%/day in crises (Nagel 'Evaporating Liquidity'); this is the highest-conviction tradable LP premium for a non-HFT, and it transfers to crypto (concentrated in low-volume/high-vol pairs). — The Nagel MECHANISM is confirmed (RFS 2012: reversal = LP return, expected return and conditional Sharpe rise enormously with VIX in 2007-09). But the adversarial prior is vindicated on tradability/decay, which the findings acknowledge only as a 'pitfall' rather than discounting in the headline conviction: (1) Blitz, van der Grient, Honarvar (2023/2024, JPM) state the classic short-term reversal effect 'has steadily weakened over time to the point of now having vanished entirely in most regions' - it only revives with an industry/factor-momentum-neutralized OVERLAY, i.e. the plain strategy is dead. (2) Avramov, Chordia, Goyal: reversals are largest in the smallest, most illiquid stocks, which are 'also very expensive to trade,' and 'after taking trading costs into account... a conventional reversal strategy becomes unprofitable.' (3) In crypto the daily reversal is explicitly 'a result of the illiquidity of the vast majority of traded cryptocurrencies' - i.e. the premium lives exactly where it cannot be harvested net of spread. So 'large and tradable' overstates: the gross premium is real and VIX-conditional, but the net-of-cost, post-2010, liquid-universe version is marginal-to-negative unless heavily turnover-constrained and overlay-enhanced. 'Highest conviction, most tradable' should be downgraded to 'real but cost-fragile, crisis-concentrated, and decaying.'
- **[CONFIRMED]** LOB-imbalance/OFI/micro-price is paper-only alpha at HFT frequency for non-colocated players: it is a latency-RANK winner-take-most race (top 6 firms >80% of wins, ~0.5bps latency tax, ~$5bn/yr) and only survives as an EXECUTION/entry-timing overlay, not standalone alpha; maker/passive strategies come out statistically insignificant. — Both legs verified, including with fresh 2026 data that the original findings predate. (1) Aquilina-Budish-O'Neill (QJE 2022, 2015 LSE message data) confirmed: races ~1/min/symbol, modal 5-10 microseconds, ~20% of volume, top 6 firms >80% of wins/losses, ~0.5bps latency tax, eliminating it cuts cost of liquidity ~17%, ~$5bn/yr globally. (2) The crucial standalone-vs-overlay claim is strongly corroborated by NEW 2026 work: a Binance-perps SHAP/microstructure study (arXiv:2602.00776) finds meta-order/OFI signals net NEGATIVE after ~4bps taker cost and concludes the 'only plausible monetization path is selective maker-style execution... useful as an execution signal rather than a standalone taker alpha strategy' - almost exactly the report's thesis. A VPIN BTC strategy decayed from +54.4bps net (2024) to -15.6bps net (2026 YTD), t-stat collapsing to 0.96. So 'paper-only standalone alpha, execution-overlay only' is confirmed and, if anything, the post-cost picture is worse and faster-decaying than the findings imply.
- **[WEAKENED]** OFI explains short-horizon mid-price changes nearly linearly with R^2 ~65% best-level and ~85-87% integrated multi-level (Cont-Kukanov-Stoikov; Cont-Cucuringu-Zhang 2023), and lagged cross-asset OFI adds short-horizon forecasting power. — The R^2 magnitudes are accurate and the report CORRECTLY flags that they are CONTEMPORANEOUS, not predictive (this is the single most important methodological point and the findings get it right - 'reporting contemporaneous R^2 as forecasting power is a classic self-deception'). The weakening is on the cross-asset/cross-impact sub-claim embedded in the summary and H2: the actual Cont-Cucuringu-Zhang (2023) paper finds that 'once multi-level OFIs have been incorporated, cross-impact terms cannot provide additional explanatory power' - i.e. after you build the integrated (multi-level, own-asset) OFI, cross-asset terms add essentially nothing for CONTEMPORANEOUS impact. So the headline integrated-OFI R^2 (~84% OOS) is confirmed, but the implied incremental value of cross-asset SPY<->QQQ OFI is overstated by the summary; the paper's own LASSO result is that cross-impact is sparse/negligible once own multi-level OFI is in. Predictive (lagged) power remains small and fast-decaying, as stated.
- **[CONFIRMED]** The square-root law of market impact is universal across equities, FX, futures, bitcoin, options (G ~ Y*sigma*sqrt(Q/V), Y~O(1)), setting the dominant cost term and capacity ceiling; small clips have a per-unit cost advantage. — Holds up well and has been freshly re-validated against models that posited non-universal exponents. Sato & Kanazawa (2024) using ID-resolved Tokyo Stock Exchange data show the impact exponent delta stays 'anchored around delta=1/2' and REJECT competing frameworks (Gabaix et al.; Farmer-Gerig-Lillo-Waelbroeck) that tie the exponent to metaorder-size/length distributions. The bitcoin million-metaorder analysis confirms the sqrt law even with near-absent statistical arbitrage/market-making, and the law is documented for option markets too. Minor caveats (not refutations): the prefactor Y and any linear-regime crossover for tiny orders vary by asset, and a crisis like Oct-2025 crypto shows realized impact can blow far past the calm-regime sqrt estimate when liquidity evaporates - so the law is a good CALM-state cost model but understates tail/stress execution cost.

---

## Rigor and evaluation methodology  `methodology`

This area is methodologically mature and the core tools are primary-source-grounded and directly implementable. The central, robust empirical fact is that selection bias under multiple testing inflates Sharpe ratios enormously even with zero true skill: the expected maximum Sharpe across N independent zero-skill trials is E[max SR] ≈ sqrt(V[SR])·[(1−γ)·Z⁻¹(1−1/N) + γ·Z⁻¹(1−1/(Ne))] (γ=0.5772), so ~7 binary parameters (N=2^7=128) yield an expected max annualized SR > 2.6 from pure noise (Bailey-Lopez de Prado 2014). The remedy is a layered protocol: Deflated Sharpe Ratio (DSR) + Probabilistic Sharpe Ratio to correct for trials and non-normality, Probability of Backtest Overfitting (PBO) via combinatorially-symmetric cross-validation (CSCV), multiple-testing thresholds (Harvey-Liu-Zhu: a genuinely new factor needs t > ~3.0, p ≈ 0.005, not 2.0), and purged+embargoed walk-forward CV (now superseded by Combinatorial Purged CV / CPCV) to kill leakage. There is an important counter-literature (Chen-Zimmermann, Jensen-Kelly-Pedersen) arguing the data-mining alarm is overstated for well-established equity factors (replication ~57-85%), but it does NOT exempt a researcher's own undisclosed search — it argues the published "elite" survivors are mostly real, which is a different claim. On harvestable alpha: net-of-cost reality is brutal — FX carry on individual currencies (~SR 0.3 gross) goes to ~0 net of bid-ask; equity anomalies lose ~26% out-of-sample and ~58% post-publication (McLean-Pontiff); crypto size/volume "anomalies" are micro-cap artifacts that die under realistic 50-100bps spreads, while crypto momentum (gross SR ~1.0) and especially delta-neutral funding/basis carry (~18% APR, SR ~1.4 net of ~4-5bps taker fees) are the survivors. The methodology itself is the edge for this program: rigorous DSR/PBO/CPCV gating plus honest cost modeling will reject most candidate anomalies, which is the point.

### Findings

**Selection bias under multiple testing inflates the maximum observed Sharpe ratio dramatically even when true Sharpe is zero. The expected maximum Sharpe across N independent trials is E[max SR] ≈ sqrt(V[SR])·[(1−γ)·Z⁻¹(1−1/N) + γ·Z⁻¹(1−1/(Ne))], γ≈0.5772 (Euler-Mascheroni), Z⁻¹ the inverse normal CDF. This 'False Strategy Theorem' is the quantitative core of the entire area.**
- Effect size: With trial-Sharpe variance V[SR]=1 and zero true Sharpe, E[max SR] rises monotonically with N over N∈[10,1000]. A strategy with just 7 binary parameters offers N=2^7=128 trials and an expected max annualized SR > 2.6 from pure noise. Lopez de Prado: 'as few as 3 trials are enough to produce a strategy that is likely false' for typical V. MinBTL implication: with only 5 years of data, trying >45 independent configurations almost guarantees an in-sample annualized SR of 1.0 with true OOS SR of 0.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Theorem is analytic (distribution-free under iid-normal trial SRs), so it does not decay. Confirmed and extended repeatedly 2018-2026; underpins all subsequent ML-era backtest-overfitting work (e.g., CPCV studies 2024).
- Cites: Bailey & Lopez de Prado 2014, 'The Deflated Sharpe Ratio', Journal of Portfolio Management 40(5), SSRN 2460551; Bailey, Borwein, Lopez de Prado, Zhu 2014, 'Pseudo-Mathematics and Financial Charlatanism', Notices of the AMS 61(5):458-471, SSRN 2308659

**The Deflated Sharpe Ratio (DSR) corrects an observed Sharpe for (a) number of trials N, (b) cross-sectional variance of trial Sharpes V[SR], (c) sample length T, and (d) non-normality (skewness γ3, kurtosis γ4). DSR = Z[ (SR_hat − SR0)·sqrt(T−1) / sqrt(1 − γ3·SR_hat + ((γ4−1)/4)·SR_hat²) ], where the deflated threshold SR0 = sqrt(V[SR])·E[max of N standard normals]. Companion Minimum Track Record Length: MinTRL = 1 + (1 − γ3·SR0 + ((γ4−1)/4)·SR0²)·(Z⁻¹(conf)/(SR_hat − SR0))².**
- Effect size: Worked example (Treasury auction-cycle seasonality): observed annualized SR_hat=2.5, N=100 trials, V[SR]=0.5, T=1250 daily obs (~5 yr), skew γ3=−3, kurt γ4=10. Deflated threshold SR0≈0.1132 (non-annualized), giving DSR≈0.9004 < 0.95 → REJECT (only ~90% chance true SR>0). The same strategy would have PASSED (DSR=0.9505) if only N=46 trials had been run; with normal returns (γ3=0, γ4=3) it would pass at N=88. Demonstrates negative skew + fat tails sharply raise the bar.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Standard practitioner tool 2018-2026 (mlfinlab, R/PerformanceAnalytics implementations). DSR/PSR are now baseline acceptance gates in ML-era backtest studies (2024).
- Cites: Bailey & Lopez de Prado 2014, 'The Deflated Sharpe Ratio', SSRN 2460551 (Eqs. 1-2 and worked example pp.7-11); Bailey & Lopez de Prado 2012, 'The Sharpe Ratio Efficient Frontier' (PSR), Journal of Risk 15(2)

**Probability of Backtest Overfitting (PBO) via Combinatorially-Symmetric Cross-Validation (CSCV): split the T×N performance matrix into S equal time blocks, form all C(S, S/2) train/test splits, pick the in-sample best strategy n* in each, compute its out-of-sample rank ω, transform λ = ln(ω/(1−ω)); PBO = fraction of combinations with λ ≤ 0 (i.e. the IS-best lands below the OOS median). Model-free, non-parametric, applies to any performance metric.**
- Effect size: PBO ∈ [0,1]; PBO→1 means the selection procedure overfits (IS winner systematically becomes an OOS loser). Default S=16 gives C(16,8)=12,870 combinations; S=8 gives C(8,4)=70. Also yields 'performance degradation' (OLS slope of OOS on IS performance — negative slope signals overfitting) and 'probability of loss' OOS. Key result: standard hold-out and single-split validation CANNOT detect this because they assume a single trial; PBO grows toward 1 as the number of configurations grows.
- Strength: strong · Recency: 2014 method, now standard. 2024 synthetic-environment study (Arian, Norouzi, Seco) finds CPCV/CSCV-family methods give materially lower PBO and higher (better) DSR test statistics than K-Fold or Walk-Forward.
- Cites: Bailey, Borwein, Lopez de Prado, Zhu 2017, 'The Probability of Backtest Overfitting', Journal of Computational Finance 20(4):39-69, SSRN 2326253; Arian, Norouzi, Seco 2024, 'Backtest Overfitting in the Machine Learning Era', Knowledge-Based Systems, SSRN 4686376

**Multiple-testing-adjusted significance threshold for a NEW factor/anomaly is far above the naive t=2.0. Harvey-Liu-Zhu catalog 316 factors from 313 papers and recommend a minimum t-stat ≈ 3.0 (single-test p ≈ 0.005) after adjustment. Methods: Bonferroni & Holm control family-wise error rate; Benjamini-Hochberg-Yekutieli (BHY) controls false-discovery rate.**
- Effect size: Bonferroni-implied threshold rises from t=1.96 (1965) → 3.78 (2012) → ~4.00 (2032 projection). BHY-implied threshold stabilizes at 3.39 (p=0.07%) by 2010, ~2.78-2.81 at 5% FDR. Accounting for hidden tests (estimated 71% of tried factors are unpublished/missing), Bonferroni→4.01, BHY→3.18. Illustrative DGP with 700 tests (100 true at t~N(2,1), 600 false at t~N(0,1)) yields FWER=100% and FDR=26% at naive cutoffs — i.e. guaranteed false discoveries. Industry 'haircut' of 50% on reported Sharpe is wrong: Harvey-Liu show the correct haircut is non-linear — marginal Sharpes get penalized heavily, high Sharpes only modestly.
- Strength: strong · Recency: RFS 2016, foundational and widely adopted. The t>3.0 rule is the de-facto standard for new factor claims 2018-2026, though contested as too conservative for theory-motivated factors (see Chen finding below).
- Cites: Harvey, Liu, Zhu 2016, '...and the Cross-Section of Expected Returns', Review of Financial Studies 29(1):5-68, NBER w20592; Harvey & Liu 2015, 'Backtesting', Journal of Portfolio Management 42(1):13-28, SSRN 2345489

**Purged + embargoed cross-validation is required for any ML/CV on overlapping-label or autocorrelated financial data; standard k-fold leaks future information and inflates OOS metrics. Purging removes training observations whose label windows overlap the test set; embargo drops a buffer of observations after each test fold to break serial correlation. Combinatorial Purged CV (CPCV) generalizes this to many backtest paths.**
- Effect size: Leakage from non-purged CV produces spuriously high accuracy/Sharpe (effect size depends on label-horizon overlap; for h-period-ahead labels, ~h observations per fold boundary are contaminated). CPCV with N groups, k test groups generates C(N,k) train/test splits and (k·C(N,k)/N) distinct backtest paths, giving a distribution of Sharpe/PBO rather than a single fragile estimate. 2024 evidence: CPCV outperforms K-Fold and Walk-Forward on false-discovery prevention, temporal stability, and stationarity.
- Strength: strong · Recency: Lopez de Prado 2018 (Advances in Financial ML); CPCV refinements (Bagged/Adaptive CPCV) and synthetic-environment validation are 2023-2025. Now best practice for ML strategies.
- Cites: Lopez de Prado 2018, 'Advances in Financial Machine Learning', Wiley (Ch.7 purged CV, Ch.11-12 CPCV/PBO); Arian, Norouzi, Seco 2024, SSRN 4686376; Wikipedia/standard refs on purged cross-validation

**Post-publication / out-of-sample decay of equity anomalies is large and systematic, consistent with both data-mining and arbitrage-correction. McLean-Pontiff study 97 cross-sectional predictors.**
- Effect size: Anomaly long-short returns are 26% lower out-of-sample (post-sample, pre-publication) and 58% lower post-publication, implying ~32 percentage points of the decay (58−26) is attributable to publication-informed arbitrage and ~26% to in-sample data-mining/overfitting. The 26% OOS drop is an upper bound on pure data-mining inflation.
- Strength: strong · Recency: JF 2016; the qualitative pattern (substantial but not total decay) has held and been reconfirmed in subsequent global/OOS studies through 2023.
- Cites: McLean & Pontiff 2016, 'Does Academic Research Destroy Stock Return Predictability?', Journal of Finance 71(1):5-32, SSRN 2156623

**Counter-literature: for the ESTABLISHED, PUBLISHED equity factor zoo the multiple-testing/replication-crisis alarm is overstated — most published factors replicate and survive joint/Bayesian multiple-testing modeling. This is a crucial nuance: it concerns the 'elite' survivors, NOT a researcher's own undisclosed in-sample search.**
- Effect size: Jensen-Kelly-Pedersen (153 factors, 93 countries, 13 themes): replication rate rises 35% (Hou-Xue-Zhang raw-return baseline) → 56.9% (their methodology, 1-month capped value-weight) → 64.7% (excluding never-significant) → 84.9% (CAPM-alpha test) → 77.3% after multiple-testing adjustment → 84.9% with global Bayesian estimation; evidence is STRENGTHENED, not weakened, by the large number of correlated factors. Chen-Zimmermann (319 characteristics): 98% of originally-clearly-significant factors reproduce at t>1.96; reproduced-vs-original t-stat regression slope 0.90, R²=83%; published t-stats sit well above 2-3. Hou-Xue-Zhang (452 portfolios from 202 signals) report only 35% replicate and a 'stunning 4%' for trading-frictions factors using value-weighting + decile breakpoints, illustrating how construction choices drive conclusions.
- Strength: contested · Recency: Active 2020-2024 debate (HXZ 2020 RFS vs JKP 2023 JF vs Chen 2022 CFR). Resolution: replication is methodology-dependent; well-constructed, theory-grounded factors mostly survive, micro-cap- and frictions-driven ones largely do not.
- Cites: Jensen, Kelly, Pedersen 2023, 'Is There a Replication Crisis in Finance?', Journal of Finance 78(5), NBER w28432; Chen & Zimmermann 2022, 'Open Source Cross-Sectional Asset Pricing', Critical Finance Review; Chen 2022, 'Most Claimed Statistical Findings... are Likely True', arXiv 2206.15365; Hou, Xue, Zhang 2020, 'Replicating Anomalies', Review of Financial Studies 33(5), NBER w23394

**Realistic transaction costs decide what is real vs paper-only, and the cross-asset gap between gross and net is the single biggest source of false alpha. FX carry illustrates the cliff.**
- Effect size: Diversified FX carry portfolio: gross annualized Sharpe ~0.5-0.85 (Lustig et al. ~0.54 net via forwards; Menkhoff et al. ~0.74 gross). BUT a long/short-by-sign-of-forward-discount individual-currency carry has gross SR ~0.3 that becomes 'essentially zero once transaction costs are taken into account.' Bid-ask in liquid FX is small but carry signals churn; high-turnover/EM-heavy ('High Mix') carry: SR 0.39 gross → 0.20 net. Carry also carries severe negative skew (~−0.94) / crash risk — Sharpe overstates appeal.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Carry premium has compressed post-2010 and especially post-2018 as rate differentials narrowed; widely reported decline 2018-2024.
- Cites: Lustig, Roussanov, Verdelhan 2011, 'Common Risk Factors in Currency Markets', RFS 24(11), NBER w14082; Menkhoff, Sarno, Schmeling, Schrimpf 2012, 'Carry Trades and Global FX Volatility', Journal of Finance 67(2)

**Crypto cross-section: 'anomalies' bifurcate into micro-cap artifacts (die under realistic costs) vs survivors. Specification-curve / non-standard-errors analysis shows researcher degrees of freedom dominate weak signals.**
- Effect size: Fieberg-Günther-Poddig-Zaremba 'Non-standard errors in the cryptocurrency world': 10 design choices × 43 sorting variables = 20,736 research designs; non-standard errors (dispersion across equally-defensible specs) EXCEED both standard errors and those in equities — and are concentrated in small coins. Size and volume effects originate in micro-cap coins of negligible economic importance; size/momentum remain robust across specs only after de-emphasizing the smallest coins. Crypto factor-zoo studies (~36 factors, ~565 coins, 2018-2024) find liquidity/trading-cost variables dominate pricing; OOS tests use 100bps bid-ask (+50bps extra for shorts). Crypto momentum gross SR ~1.0 (strong pre-2021, decaying as microstructure matured); risk-managed momentum ~1.12→1.42; diversification benefits vanish once costs exceed 2-3%.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: 2023-2026 crypto-specific literature; momentum effectiveness explicitly declining post-2021. Crypto data is short (effective cross-section ~2017-2026), so multiple-testing/MinBTL constraints bite hard.
- Cites: Fieberg, Günther, Poddig, Zaremba 2024, 'Non-standard errors in the cryptocurrency world', International Review of Financial Analysis 92:103106; Fieberg, Liedtke, Poddig, Walker, Zaremba 2024, 'A Trend Factor for the Cross-Section of Cryptocurrency Returns', Journal of Financial and Quantitative Analysis, SSRN 4601972; 'Crypto factor zoo' 2024-2026, International Review of Financial Analysis S1057521926000645

**Delta-neutral crypto carry (perpetual funding / spot-futures basis) is among the few strategies with a real, costed edge, because the premium is a structural compensation (leverage demand) not a price-prediction.**
- Effect size: Perpetual funding-rate arbitrage (long spot / short perp when funding positive): basic static rule (~enter funding>0.01%/8h, exit<0.005%) ≈ 18% annualized, Sharpe ~1.4 (2019-2023), net of ~4-5bps taker fees and 8-hour funding accrual; ML-timed sizing ~31% / Sharpe ~2.3 (same period, likely optimistic/overfit). Calendar basis (long spot / short dated future): ~5-15% annualized in normal regimes, 25-40% in euphoria (Q4-2020, Q1-2024), collapsing to ±2% in fear. Realistic cost stack: maker 1.2bps / taker 2.4-5bps per leg + funding + slippage ~ linear in (size / 5-min volume).
- Strength: moderate · Recency: 2023-2026 practitioner and academic evidence; edge persists because it is a risk/financing premium, but funding compresses as more delta-neutral capital enters (reported +215% arbitrage capital YoY on some venues).
- Cites: Practitioner/academic syntheses 2023-2026 (Sharpe.ai, Gate Learn); academic: 'Exploring Risk and Return Profiles of Funding Rate Arbitrage on CEX and DEX' 2025, ScienceDirect S2096720925000818; He, Hugonnier, Jermann et al., 'Fundamentals of Perpetual Futures', arXiv 2212.06888

**Variance/volatility risk premium (option selling) is a genuine, large premium but Sharpe is deeply misleading because the payoff is short-tail with catastrophic, autocorrelated drawdowns — the canonical case where DSR/non-normality correction and cost modeling matter most.**
- Effect size: VRP magnitude: 1990-2018 average VIX 19.3% vs realized S&P vol 15.1% → ~4.2 vol points (similar gap persists). CBOE PUT index gross premium high (24.1%/yr 2006-2015) but max drawdown 32.7% (WPUT 24.2%) and large losses in Feb-2018 'Volmageddon' and Mar-2020 COVID. Returns are positively correlated with equities and carry severe negative skew; naive annualized Sharpe (often quoted ~0.7-0.9) overstates true risk-adjusted value once tail/kurtosis and option bid-ask + roll costs are charged. Tail-hedged VRP variants exist specifically to cap these drawdowns.
- Strength: moderate · Recency: Premium persists 2018-2026 but realized via short-vol products repeatedly blows up (2018, 2020); requires explicit tail management and honest non-normal evaluation.
- Cites: Cboe research, 'Volatility Risk Premium and PUT Index' white papers (cboe.com); Wilshire/Cboe 2019, 'Options-Based Benchmark Indexes: Performance, Risk', cboe.com

### Testable hypotheses
- H1 (Trial accounting): Build the firm's own 'trial counter' — log N = number of distinct strategy configurations evaluated per anomaly family. Hypothesis: for any in-house signal, the realized OOS Sharpe will not exceed sqrt(V[SR])·E[max of N normals]; i.e., candidates whose backtest SR is below the DSR threshold SR0 computed from our actual N and trial-SR variance will have OOS Sharpe statistically indistinguishable from 0. Test by pre-registering N and re-evaluating on held-out 2026 data.
- H2 (DSR gate calibration): On our crypto OHLCV (2024-02 to 2026-06) and S&P 500 bars, run a deliberately large grid (e.g. all moving-average crossover / momentum-lookback combos, N in the hundreds) on PURE noise (phase-randomized or block-bootstrapped returns). Hypothesis: the empirical distribution of max in-sample Sharpe matches E[max SR] from the False Strategy Theorem within Monte-Carlo error, validating our N and V[SR] estimates before we trust any DSR on real signals.
- H3 (CSCV/PBO): For each candidate strategy family, compute PBO via CSCV (S=16). Hypothesis: signals we currently believe in (e.g. crypto funding-carry, crypto cross-sectional momentum on top-50) have PBO < 0.5, while a matched set of fitted technical rules have PBO > 0.5. Falsifiable: if our 'good' signals also show PBO > 0.5 they are overfit.
- H4 (Purge/embargo leakage): Re-run any ML model we have on S&P 500 / crypto with and without purging+embargo (embargo = max label horizon). Hypothesis: non-purged CV overstates OOS Sharpe by a measurable margin (>0.2 SR) that grows with label horizon; purged+embargoed estimates are lower and closer to live performance.
- H5 (Funding-carry net edge): On 228 perpetuals × ~23k hours of funding history + Coinalyze, backtest delta-neutral long-spot/short-perp carry with a realistic cost stack (taker 4-5bps/leg, 8h funding accrual, slippage = f(size/rolling volume)). Hypothesis: a simple funding-threshold rule on the top ~20 most liquid perps yields net annualized Sharpe ~1.0-1.5 and survives DSR at our true N; the edge concentrates in high-funding regimes and compresses over the 2024-2026 sample (decay test).
- H6 (Crypto size/volume = micro-cap artifact): Replicate size and volume sorts on top-50 coins vs an extended universe including small caps.
