Hypothesis (per Fieberg-Zaremba): size/volume 'alpha' exists only in the smallest, least-liquid coins and vanishes net of 50-100bps spreads in the top-50 tradable set; momentum survives in large coins but with materially lower net Sharpe than gross.
- H7 (Non-standard errors / specification curve): For one crypto anomaly (e.g. short-term reversal on 1h/4h bars), enumerate a multiverse of defensible design choices (universe filter, rebalance frequency, weighting, winsorization, cost assumption) and plot the specification curve. Hypothesis: the dispersion of net Sharpe across specs (non-standard error) is large relative to its mean — the signal is fragile/researcher-dependent — whereas funding-carry's curve is tight.
- H8 (VRP non-normality): On Deribit BTC/ETH IV surfaces + DVOL (2021-2026), measure the implied-minus-realized vol premium and backtest systematic short-vol (or DVOL-future short) with option bid-ask + delta-hedge costs. Hypothesis: gross Sharpe looks attractive (>1) but DSR with the actual (large negative skew, high kurtosis) return moments and 2021/2022 drawdowns pushes it below the 0.95 confidence threshold — i.e. a paper-only edge unless tail-hedged.

### Harvest strategies
- Methodology-as-edge (primary deliverable): implement a standardized acceptance gate every candidate strategy must pass before paper/live: (1) pre-register and log N (trials); (2) DSR ≥ 0.95 using actual N, trial-SR variance V[SR], sample length T, and realized skew/kurtosis; (3) PBO < 0.5 via CSCV (S=16); (4) purged+embargoed walk-forward or CPCV out-of-sample; (5) net-of-cost Sharpe with asset-specific cost stack. This is cheap (CPU-bound, fits RTX/H100) and is itself the alpha for a small shop — it prevents capital allocation to noise.
- Crypto delta-neutral funding carry (best risk-adjusted survivor): long spot (or long-dated perp) / short perpetual on the ~10-20 most liquid coins when 8h funding exceeds a threshold. Cost drag: taker ~2.4-5bps + maker ~1.2bps per leg per rebalance, 8h funding accrual on the short, slippage ~ linear in order/rolling-volume; net ~18% APR / Sharpe ~1.4 historically. Manage venue/counterparty risk; monitor funding compression (decay).
- Crypto calendar basis (cash-and-carry): long spot / short dated future when annualized basis > cost-of-capital + fees (basis 5-15% normal, 25-40% euphoria). Same cost stack; capture convergence. Best harvested opportunistically in euphoric regimes; near-zero in fear regimes.
- Crypto cross-sectional momentum on large coins ONLY: long top-quantile / short bottom-quantile by trailing return on top-50 by liquidity, weekly rebalance. Gross SR ~1.0 (decaying post-2021); charge 10-30bps round-trip taker+slippage on small coins. Harvest only the large-coin sleeve where net survives; use risk-managed (vol-scaled) version to lift SR toward ~1.4 gross.
- VRP / short-vol with explicit tail hedge: systematically sell BTC/ETH options (or short DVOL futures) to capture the ~4-vol-point implied-minus-realized premium, but buy OTM tail protection sized to cap the 30%+ drawdowns that hit short-vol in stress (2018/2020 analogues). Cost drag: option bid-ask (wider on far expiries), delta-hedge slippage, premium spent on tails. Only deploy if DSR (with true negative-skew moments) passes — otherwise it is paper-only.
- FX carry — DO NOT trade naively at the individual-currency level (net SR ~0). If pursued at all, only as a diversified, low-turnover basket with EM-cost awareness, and explicitly model the negative-skew crash risk; treat gross Sharpe as a ceiling, expect ~0.2-0.3 net.
- Equity anomalies — apply a non-linear publication haircut (Harvey-Liu) not a flat 50%: expect ~26% OOS and ~58% post-publication decay; only trade survivors with t > ~3.0 after multiple-testing adjustment, value-weighted/capped to avoid micro-cap illusion, and net of realistic spread+impact on the S&P 500 universe.

### Pitfalls
- Unlogged trials (the cardinal sin): every grid-search, hyperparameter sweep, feature-selection pass, and discarded variant counts toward N. If N is unknown, DSR/PBO cannot be computed honestly and the backtest is, per Bailey-Lopez de Prado, 'worthless regardless of how excellent the reported performance.' For ML pipelines, N is effectively the size of the searched configuration space, not the number of models you chose to report.
- Hold-out / single-split self-deception: a single train/test split or k-fold does NOT control overfitting — it assumes one trial. Run it enough times (≥20 for 95%) and a false positive is expected, then published as a single-trial result. Must use CSCV/PBO or CPCV.
- Data leakage from non-purged CV and overlapping labels: standard k-fold on autocorrelated series or h-period-ahead labels leaks future info and inflates OOS Sharpe. Forgetting the embargo leaves residual serial-correlation leakage even after purging.
- Ignoring non-normality in Sharpe: negative skew + fat tails (option selling, FX carry, crypto crashes) make naive Sharpe wildly optimistic. The DSR example shows skew=−3/kurt=10 alone can flip a strategy from 'pass' to 'fail'. Sharpe is the wrong headline metric for short-tail strategies.
- Cost-model optimism: using mid-price fills, ignoring funding accrual, assuming infinite liquidity, or applying a single bps spread to all coins. Crypto small-cap spreads are 50-100bps+ (and worse for shorts); options far-expiry spreads are wide; impact is convex in size. Many anomalies (crypto size/volume, individual-currency FX carry) are POSITIVE gross and ZERO/negative net.
- Micro-cap / illiquidity illusion: equal-weighting and decile-on-all-stocks (or all-coins) loads alpha onto names you cannot actually trade. Capped value-weighting (NYSE-80th in equities; top-N liquid in crypto) is the honest construction; failing to do so manufactures fake premia.
- Non-standard errors (researcher degrees of freedom): even with no formal multiple testing, the dispersion of results across equally-defensible design choices (20,736 designs for crypto) can exceed sampling error. A result that lives or dies on one arbitrary choice (window, filter, weighting) is fragile. Report a specification curve.
- Snooping the same data repeatedly across a research program: the published 'elite' factors mostly replicate (JKP/Chen), but that does NOT license a team to mine its own data and claim the low FDR of the published literature. Your private FDR is governed by YOUR N, not the literature's survivors.
- Short crypto history + MinBTL: with an effective tradable cross-section of only ~a few years, the Minimum Backtest Length constraint is severe — a handful of configurations on 2-4 years of data is enough to guarantee a SR~1 in-sample / 0 out-of-sample. Crypto demands especially harsh trial budgets.
- Regime/decay blindness: anomalies decay post-publication (~58% equities) and as capital enters (crypto funding compression, momentum decline post-2021). A static backtest over a favorable regime (e.g. 2020-2021 crypto bull) massively overstates forward Sharpe; always include adverse regimes and a decay/sub-period stability test.
- Degenerate / non-diverse predictions: an ML model that collapses to a near-constant or single-factor proxy can post good backtest stats while being economically empty. Check prediction dispersion, effective number of bets, and that the signal is not just a disguised market-beta or size exposure (use CAPM/factor-alpha, not raw return — per JKP).

### Data needed
- Trial-tracking infrastructure: a persistent log (DB or experiment tracker) recording N = every configuration evaluated per anomaly family, plus the cross-sectional variance of trial Sharpes V[SR] — required inputs to DSR and PBO. This is a build item, not an external dataset.
- Already have / sufficient: crypto OHLCV top-50 (1h/4h/1d, 2024-02 to 2026-06), 228 perpetuals × ~23k h funding (for H5 carry), Coinalyze funding/OI/liquidations, Deribit IV surfaces + DVOL 2021-2026 (for H8 VRP), S&P 500 daily/15m/1h + LOB + Databento L2 (for equity cost/impact modeling), FnSpID fundamentals+sentiment.
- Crypto realistic-cost calibration: per-coin historical bid-ask spread / order-book depth time series (derive from your 56M LOB snapshots for equities; for crypto, pull exchange L2 or use Kaiko/Amberdata-style spread series — or estimate from your OHLCV high-low and volume). Exchange fee schedules (Binance maker 1.2bps / taker 2.4bps tiers; Deribit options fees) — free from exchange docs.
- FX (to source, FREE): Dukascopy tick/bar data (1600+ instruments, free, API or duka/dukascopy-node downloaders) and HistData.com (free CSV, MT-importable) for spot + bid/ask; interest-rate differentials / forward points from FRED (free) and central-bank policy-rate series. Enables H-FX carry net-of-spread tests.
- Commodities (to source, FREE): FRED Commodities category (~1,969 series) for spot/price; CME/exchange settlement and term-structure data for futures roll/carry (some free via exchange or Quandl/Nasdaq Data Link free tier).
- Equity options / VIX (to source, FREE-ish): VIX index and VIXCLS from CBOE (free) and FRED (free); VVIX, term-structure, PUT/BXM index levels from CBOE indices page (free). Full historical option chains (for true VRP net-of-spread) are largely paid — free/cheap partial sources: OptionsDX (free EOD samples), CBOE DataShop (paid), Nasdaq/ORATS (paid). For BTC/ETH options you already have Deribit.
- Software: mlfinlab or equivalent implementations of DSR, PSR, MinTRL, PBO/CSCV, purged+embargoed CV, and CPCV (open-source). Validate the False Strategy Theorem numerically (H2) against your own N before trusting any DSR output.

### Crypto/recent notes
Crypto-specific and 2018-2026 recency notes. (1) Methodology tooling has shifted toward Combinatorial Purged CV (CPCV) as the 2023-2025 best practice over plain purged k-fold and walk-forward; a 2024 synthetic-environment study (Arian-Norouzi-Seco) shows CPCV gives lower PBO and better deflated-Sharpe statistics — directly relevant given the program's ML usage and the prior finding that bigger models don't help (rigor, not size, is the edge). (2) The replication-crisis debate is now nuanced: published equity factors mostly replicate (JKP 2023: up to ~85%; Chen-Zimmermann: 98% of clear factors at t>1.96) and publication bias is modest, but this exonerates the literature's SURVIVORS, not a researcher's own undisclosed search — your private false-discovery rate is set by your own trial count, so DSR/PBO gating remains essential. (3) Crypto is the hardest case for these methods: effective tradable history is only ~2017-2026, so Minimum Backtest Length bites hard (a few configs on 2-4 yrs guarantees in-sample SR~1 / OOS~0); non-standard errors are LARGER than in equities (20,736-design study, Fieberg-Zaremba 2024); size/volume 'anomalies' are micro-cap artifacts that die under 50-100bps spreads, while momentum (gross SR~1.0, decaying post-2021) survives only in large coins and only partially net of cost. (4) The genuinely costed crypto survivors are delta-neutral structural-premium trades: perpetual funding carry (~18% APR, Sharpe~1.4 net of ~4-5bps taker + 8h funding) and spot-futures basis (5-15% normal, 25-40% euphoria), because these harvest a financing/leverage-demand premium rather than predicting price — but funding is compressing as delta-neutral capital floods in (reported large YoY increases in deployed arbitrage capital). (5) Crypto VRP via Deribit (DVOL/IV surfaces 2021-2026): an implied-minus-realized premium exists but returns are severely negatively skewed/fat-tailed, so honest evaluation REQUIRES the non-normality terms in DSR and adverse-regime inclusion; gross Sharpe is a trap. Realistic crypto cost stack to model everywhere: maker ~1.2bps / taker ~2.4-5bps per leg + 8h funding + slippage ≈ linear in (order size / rolling 5-min volume).

### Adversarial verification — reliability: **medium**
_Net-of-cost reality:_ The methodology half of this area is solid and ages well: the False Strategy Theorem, DSR/PSR, PBO/CSCV, Harvey-Liu-Zhu hurdles, purged/embargoed CV and McLean-Pontiff decay are all confirmed and largely analytic or repeatedly replicated. The harvestable-alpha half does NOT survive a hard net-of-cost, most-recent-data look. The single biggest problem is the headline crypto 'survivor': delta-neutral funding/basis carry at ~18% APR / Sharpe ~1.4 is a 2019-2023 artifact that has been substantially competed away by 2024-2026 — basis fell from ~25% to ~4.5%, mean perp funding in the 2024 bull was ~0.017%/8h (barely above the trade's own entry threshold), pure yields dropped below US T-bills by mid-2024, and only ~40% of top opportunities now clear costs. Presenting it as the current best edge in a June-2026 report is precisely the post-publication / capital-entry decay the adversarial prior warns about; the realistic forward number is a low-single-digit-percent yield with Sharpe well under 1.0 unless you stack collateral yield or trade venue/counterparty risk. FX individual-currency carry is correctly written off (~0 net), and the Aug-2024 yen unwind freshly confirms the crash risk. VRP/short-vol is real but, net of bid-ask and tail hedging, runs ~0.7-0.8 Sharpe (not the naive ~1.0+) and periodically blows up (2018, 2020). Bottom line: trust the rigor toolkit and the decay/cost warnings; treat every quoted survivor Sharpe — especially the crypto carry 1.4 — as a stale, pre-decay gross ceiling, not a live net edge.
- **[WEAKENED]** Crypto delta-neutral funding/basis carry is the best costed survivor: perpetual funding arbitrage ~18% APR / Sharpe ~1.4 net of ~4-5bps taker fees (2019-2023), and spot-futures basis 5-15% normal / 25-40% in euphoria. — The historical 2019-2023 backtest figure is plausible, but the central error is presenting it as the LIVE best survivor as of a 2026-06 report. Fresh, independent 2024-2025 evidence shows the edge has largely self-arbitraged away exactly as the adversarial prior predicts when structural-premium capital floods in. BitMEX's own Q2-2025 derivatives report: the 2024 bull market saw a MAX 8h funding rate of only 0.1308% and a MEAN of just 0.0173% (the strategy's own entry threshold is ~0.01%/8h, so the edge is now marginal), versus 0.2-0.3% routinely in 2017/2021. Multiple independent sources: front-month BTC basis collapsed from ~25% (Feb 2024) to 4.46% (Dec 2025) with 93% of trading days BELOW the 5% breakeven; annualized yields 'plummeted below 4%' by mid-2024, falling beneath the risk-free US Treasury rate; arbitrage capital deployed +215% YoY; protocols like Ethena built billions of automated short-perp capital around the trade and 'effectively eliminated' it. A November-2025 academic study finds only 40% of top funding-arb opportunities generate POSITIVE returns after transaction costs and spread reversals. The findings' own crypto-notes concede funding is compressing, but the headline still markets 18%/1.4 as a current harvestable edge. Net: real but heavily decayed; forward Sharpe is far below 1.4 and the pure trade now competes with T-bills.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Equity anomaly long-short returns are 26% lower out-of-sample (pre-publication) and 58% lower post-publication (McLean-Pontiff 2016, 97 predictors), splitting decay into ~26% data-mining and ~32pp arbitrage-correction. — Reproduced verbatim across multiple independent sources and described as 'replicated many times' / 'known as anomaly decay.' The 26%/58% decomposition and its data-mining vs investor-learning interpretation are accurately stated and remain a foundational, robust empirical fact. The only refinement from the adversarial direction is that subsequent work disagrees on how much of the 26% OOS drop is pure data-mining: Chen-Zimmermann argue the publication-bias / data-mining component is much smaller (bias-adjusted returns only ~12.3% smaller than in-sample), implying most of the 58% post-pub decay is genuine mispricing being arbitraged, not statistical illusion. Either way the headline numbers stand.
- **[CONFIRMED]** FX carry on individual currencies (gross SR ~0.3) becomes 'essentially zero once transaction costs are taken into account'; diversified carry SR ~0.5-0.85 gross but with severe negative skew (~-0.94) / crash risk that makes Sharpe overstate appeal. — Independent sources corroborate: simple nominal carry runs ~0.4-0.5 gross Sharpe over full cycles (0.3-0.5 including crises), individual-currency churn erodes this to roughly zero net, and the strategy carries documented crash risk. The adversarial prior is freshly validated by the August-2024 yen carry unwind (BIS Bulletin 90): a single BoJ policy surprise triggered a violent multi-day drawdown, and 2024 EM currency losses (JPM EM FX index -9%, BRL -20%, MXN -16%) directly hit carry. The 'gross Sharpe is a ceiling, expect ~0.2-0.3 net' framing is well-supported. Mild caveat: the exact -0.94 skew and the '~0 net' figure trace to specific older specifications, but the qualitative claim is robust and if anything understated post-2024.
- **[CONFIRMED]** Multiple-testing-adjusted significance for a NEW factor is t>~3.0 (p~0.005), far above naive t=2.0 (Harvey-Liu-Zhu), and the replication debate is methodology-dependent (HXZ ~35% replicate vs JKP 57-85% vs Chen ~98% reproduce). — The t>3.0 hurdle and the HLZ multiple-testing framework are confirmed. Two honest nuances in the adversarial direction: (1) HLZ's headline 3.0 is the conservative/Bonferroni-flavored cutoff; their own FDR-controlling BHY hurdle is lower (~2.78-2.81), and HXZ also use a 2.78 multiple-test bar — so '3.0' is a round-number upper guide, not a single agreed threshold. (2) The replication spread is accurately represented and genuinely unresolved: HXZ report 65% of 452 anomalies FAIL even t=1.96 (82% fail at t=2.78) under value-weighting + NYSE breakpoints, with 96% of trading-frictions anomalies failing; JKP counter with 56.9%-84.9% replication via capped value-weighting and Bayesian shrinkage; Chen-Zimmermann find ~near-100% reproduce at t>1.96. The findings correctly flag that this exonerates the published elite, NOT a researcher's own undisclosed search. Accurately stated.
- **[CONFIRMED]** The False Strategy Theorem / Deflated Sharpe Ratio: E[max SR] across N independent zero-skill trials grows so ~7 binary params (N=128) yield expected max annualized SR > 2.6 from pure noise; DSR corrects for N, trial-SR variance, sample length, skew and kurtosis. — The result is analytic (extreme-value asymptotics of the maximum of N standard normals scaled by trial-SR dispersion), is uncontested in the literature, and underpins all ML-era backtest-overfitting work; it cannot decay. Independent sources restate it precisely (e.g., 'a Sharpe of 2.0 from 500 trials over 3 years has only ~34% chance of being genuine'). The one legitimate adversarial caveat — which strengthens rather than refutes the methodology — is the independence assumption: real strategy variations (e.g., adjacent moving-average lookbacks) are highly correlated, so the EFFECTIVE number of independent trials is smaller than the raw configuration count. Naively plugging raw N over-deflates; the standard fix (used by Bailey-Lopez de Prado and noted in implementations) is to estimate effective N via clustering of trial returns. So the theorem is correct; the practical risk is mis-estimating N, not the formula.
